Ruling on Voluntary Prayer in Disliked Times and Fasting on Prohibited Days
Discusses voluntary prayer during three disliked times and fasting on prohibited days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on starting voluntary prayer in the three disliked times and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding qada for fasting on prohibited days.

Core Idea
A voluntary prayer started in a disliked time is valid but sinful; a fast on a prohibited day is invalid—no qada according to Abu Hanifa, but qada required by the Sahibayn.

This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayirah presents two related cases of worship begun in prohibited or disliked times. For voluntary prayer, the ruling involves whether one must stop and make it up. For fasting on Eid and Tashriq days, a key intra-Hanafi dispute arises about the necessity of qada. Understanding the analogy and how Abu Hanifa differentiated between prayer and fasting sharpens your grasp of Hanafi usul and istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for voluntary prayer in the three times
Find the two opinions: one says must stop and make up at a permissible time; another says better to stop, but if continued, it's valid.
Note the use of 'yajibu qata'uha' vs 'al-afdal'.
2
Understand the parallel for fasting on prohibited days
Locate the days: Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and Ayyam al-Tashriq. Fasting is forbidden.
These days are not valid for fasting.
3
State the intra-Hanafi dispute on qada
Abu Hanifa: no qada because the fast never commenced validly. Sahibayn: qada is required by analogy to prayer.
The Sahibayn equate the two; Abu Hanifa differentiates.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's analogy
They argue: just as starting a voluntary prayer in a disliked time obligates qada if invalidated, so does fasting.
This is qiyas.
5
Examine Abu Hanifa's differentiation
He distinguishes: fasting on these days is absolutely prohibited—the day itself is not a valid subject for fasting; whereas prayer times are disliked but the act of prayer itself is valid if commenced.
The prohibition is in the day, not the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو شرع في التطوع في الأوقات الثلاثة : قال في النهاية: يجب قطعها وقضاؤها في وقت مباح، في ظاهر الرواية. وقيل : الأفضل قطعها ولو مضى فيها : خرج عما وجب عليه بالشروع ولا يجب سواه. فإن قطعها وأداها في وقت مكروه أجزأه عندنا، خلافا لزفر، كما إذا دخل في التطوع عند قيام الظهيرة ، ثم أفسده، وقضاه عند الغروب. قال الخُجندي: إذا شرع في التطوع في الأوقات الثلاثة: فالأفضل أن يقطع، ويقضي في وقت مباح، فإن لم يقطع، ومضى عليه فقد أساء، ولا شيء عليه. ولو شرع في الصوم في الأيام المنهية كيوم الفطر، ويوم النحر، وأيام التشريق، ثم أفطر : لا يلزمه القضاء عند أبي حنيفة. وعندهما يلزمه، فهما سويًا بين الصوم والصلاة، وأبو حنيفة فرق
And if one begins a voluntary prayer in the three times: In al-Nihayah, it says: He must cut it off and make it up at a permissible time, in the apparent narration. And it is said: It is better to cut it off; and if he continues in it, he has fulfilled what was obligated upon him by beginning it, and nothing else is required. If he cuts it off and performs it in a disliked time, it suffices him according to us, contrary to Zufar, like if he began a voluntary prayer at midday (qiyam al-dhahirah), then invalidated it, and made it up at sunset. Al-Khujandi said: If one begins a voluntary prayer in the three times, it is better to cut it off and make it up at a permissible time; if he does not cut it off and continues, he has done wrong, and nothing is upon him. And if one begins fasting on prohibited days like the day of Fitr, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashriq, then breaks it: qada is not required according to Abu Hanifah. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), qada is required; they equated fasting and prayer, while Abu Hanifah differentiated.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage covers two related issues: voluntary prayer during the three disliked times, and fasting on prohibited days. For voluntary prayer, the author presents two opinions from al-Nihayah: one says it is obligatory to stop and make it up at a permissible time (in the apparent narration), while another says it is better to stop, but if one continues, he has fulfilled the obligation of the vow (by starting) and no further qada is necessary. If he stops and then prays the makeup in a disliked time, it still suffices, differing from Zufar. Al-Khujandi affirms the preferred view: cut off and make up later; if not, he is sinful but not required to remake. For fasting, an intra-Hanafi dispute arises: Abu Hanifa holds that fasting on prohibited days like Eid and tashriq is invalid and no qada is required, because the prohibition is connected to the day itself (it is not a valid day for fasting), so no obligation is established. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogize fasting to prayer: since the prohibition is only dislike, if one starts, the act is valid but sinful, and qada is required. Abu Hanifa differentiates because fasting on these days is inherently impermissible (the days are not valid for fasting), whereas prayer times are disliked but not invalid for the act itself after commencement.

Key Terms
التطوع (al-tatawwu'): Voluntary or supererogatory prayers (nawafil).
الأوقات الثلاثة (al-awqat al-thalathah): The three disliked times for prayer: sunrise, zenith, and sunset.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following Eid al-Adha (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul-Hijjah) when fasting is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is no qada (makeup) required if one begins fasting on the day of Eid al-Fitr and then breaks the fast?
A) Because the fast was valid but disliked.
B) Because the day itself is not a valid day for fasting.
C) Because the person intended a voluntary fast.
D) Because the prohibition is only recommended.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayer in disliked times is valid but sinful; fasting on prohibited days is invalid under Abu Hanifa, so no qada is required, whereas the Sahibayn require qada by analogy to prayer.

Invalidation of Fajr Prayer at Sunrise and the Distinction with Asr
Ruling and reasoning for invalidation of Fajr at sunrise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when sunrise occurs during Fajr prayer and explain why it differs from sunset during Asr.

Core Idea
Sunrise during Fajr invalidates because it exits to a disliked time; sunset during Asr does not.

This lesson examines a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: why Fajr prayer is invalidated by sunrise but Asr prayer remains valid despite sunset. Understanding the reasoning ('illah) behind this difference is crucial for grasping the school's approach to time-based rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Identify the two scenarios: sunrise during Fajr and sunset during Asr. Note the ruling for each: invalid vs valid.
2
Analyze the reasoning
Understand the 'illah: when the sun sets during Asr, Maghrib time enters, so the prayer is performed in a valid time. When the sun rises during Fajr, the time exits into a disliked time (makrooh), not a valid prayer time, hence invalidation.
The key is the nature of the time entered.
3
Contrast the outcomes
Contrast the two results: Fajr becomes invalid (fasid), requiring repetition; Asr remains valid and no repetition needed.
4
Apply the principle
Apply this reasoning to other scenarios: any obligatory prayer that continues into a disliked time due to its time ending? The principle is specific to these two cases as per the text.
The rule is limited to Fajr and Asr as the only prayers that border disliked times.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو طلعت عليه الشمس وهو في صلاة الفجر: فسدت صلاته.
بخلاف ما إذا غربت على مصلي العصر، حيث لا تفسد. والفرق: أنها إذا غربت: فقد دخل وقت المغرب، فيكون مؤدياً في وقت، وأما إذا طلعت فقد خرج لا إلى وقت بل هو وقت مكروه، ففسدت.
ولو شرع في التطوع في الأوقات الثلاثة:
قال في النهاية: يجب قطعها وقضاؤها في وقت مباح، في ظاهر الرواية.
وقيل: الأفضل قطعها ولو مضى فيها: خرج عما وجب عليه بالشروع ولا يجب سواه.
فإن قطعها وأداها في وقت مكروه أجزأه عندنا، خلافا لزفر، كما إذا
دخل في التطوع عند قيام الظهيرة، ثم أفسده، وقضاه عند الغروب.
قال الخُجندي: إذا شرع في التطوع في الأوقات الثلاثة: فالأفضل أن يقطع، ويقضي في وقت مباح، فإن لم يقطع، ومضى عليه فقد أساء، ولا شيء عليه.
And if the sun rises upon him while he is in the Fajr prayer, his prayer becomes invalid. Unlike if it sets upon the one praying Asr, where it does not become invalid. The difference is that if it sets, the time of Maghrib has entered, so he is performing it in a time. As for if it rises, he exits [the time] not into a [valid] time but into a disliked time, so it becomes invalid. And if he begins a voluntary prayer in the three times: It is said in al-Nihayah: It is necessary to cut it and make it up in a permissible time, according to the apparent narration. And it is said: It is better to cut it, even if he continues in it, he fulfills what became obligatory upon him by starting, and nothing else is necessary. If he cuts it and performs it in a disliked time, it suffices him according to us, contrary to Zufar, as if he began a voluntary prayer at midday heat, then corrupted it, and made it up at sunset. Al-Khujandi said: If he begins a voluntary prayer in the three times, it is better to cut it and make it up in a permissible time. If he does not cut it and continues, he has done badly, but nothing is required of him.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage addresses the rulings for obligatory and voluntary prayers during disliked times. First, it explains the difference between Fajr and Asr: if sunrise occurs during Fajr, the prayer is invalidated because the time exits into a disliked period (makrooh), whereas if sunset occurs during Asr, the prayer remains valid because Maghrib time begins and the prayer is performed within a valid time. Then, for voluntary prayers started during the three disliked times (sunrise, sunset, and istiwa'), the relied-upon view (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that one must stop the prayer and make it up later in a permissible time. Some say it is better to stop, but if one continues, he fulfills his obligation by starting. If he stops and makes it up in a disliked time, it is still valid according to the Hanafi school, unlike Zufar. Al-Khujandi confirms the preferable action is to stop and make it up later.

Key Terms
الأوقات الثلاثة (al-awqat al-thalathah): The three times when prayer is disliked: sunrise, sunset, and when the sun is at its zenith (istiwa').
زفر (Zufar): A disciple of Abu Hanifa who often held differing opinions; here he disagrees on the validity of making up a voluntary prayer in a disliked time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the sun sets while one is praying Asr?
A) The prayer becomes invalid.
B) The prayer remains valid.
C) The prayer must be cut immediately.
D) The prayer becomes Maghrib prayer.

Key Takeaway
Sunrise during Fajr invalidates the prayer due to exit to a disliked time, while sunset during Asr does not invalidate because it enters a valid time.

Ruling on Voluntary Prayers Begun in the Three Disliked Times
Ruling and dispute on voluntary prayer in disliked times.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayers started in disliked times, explain the wajib of cutting them, and identify Zufar's disagreement.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer begun in a disliked time must be cut and remade; if continued, it is valid but sinful.

This lesson covers the rules for voluntary (nafl) prayers initiated during the three disliked times: sunrise, sunset, and when the sun is at its zenith. The Hanafi school, in Zahir al-Riwayah, obligates cutting such a prayer. We will explore the evidence, the difference of opinion with Zufar, and the practical fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Identify the ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah: it is wajib (obligatory) to cut the voluntary prayer and make it up later in a permissible time.
The term 'يجب' in Arabic indicates obligation (wajib).
2
Understand the alternative opinion
Note that some scholars say it is 'better' (afdal) to cut, but if one continues, the prayer is valid (though sinful). This is the preferred view according to later sources.
The text says 'قيل: الأفضل قطعها' indicating a less authoritative view.
3
Examine Zufar's disagreement
Zufar disagrees: if one cuts and makes it up in a disliked time, it does not suffice. Understand the basis of his disagreement.
The text says 'خلافا لزفر'.
4
Apply to examples
Apply to the examples given: starting a voluntary prayer at midday heat (istiwa') and making it up at sunset. See how the different views apply.

Disliked Times for Voluntary Prayers: Hanafi Ruling and Proof
States ruling and proof for disliked voluntary prayer times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayers in disliked times, explain the proof (nahy li-ghayrihi), and apply the rule to cases of vows and forgetfulness.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer after Fajr and Asr is makruh tahrimi because the prohibition is for an external reason.

This lesson examines a ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar on the times when voluntary prayer is disliked. The Hanafi school distinguishes between prohibitions for inherent evil (haram) and those for external reasons (makruh tahrimi). Understanding this distinction is key to grasping the proof structure and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage rules on voluntary (nafl) prayer after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset. The ruling is makruh (disliked).
Only voluntary prayers are affected; missed (qada) prayers or funeral prayers are allowed.
2
Understand the classification: makruh tahrimi
In Hanafi usul, a prohibition can be either li-dhatihi (inherent) → haram, or li-ghayrihi (external reason) → makruh tahrimi. Here, the prohibition is li-ghayrihi, so the act is not haram but close to it.
This distinction affects rulings on vows and compensation.
3
Examine the proof: nahy li-ghayrihi
The proof is a rational deduction (qiyas): the act of prayer itself is good, but performing it in these times resembles sun-worship or causes neglect of a command? The prohibition is attached to the time, not the act.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on the principle that acts are judged by their underlying causes.
4
Apply to vows and forgetfulness
If one vows to pray or fast in a disliked time: the vow is valid (because the act is not inherently evil) but must be broken to avoid sin, then made up. If one forgetfully starts a voluntary prayer in these times, it is not disliked and he completes it.
This shows the importance of intention (qasd) in determining the ruling.
5
Compare with other schools
The Shafi'i school holds that voluntary prayer in these times is permissible except at sunrise, sunset, and zenith. The difference stems from how each school interprets the hadith evidence.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions are valid within their respective usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة
ويكره أن يتنقل بعد صلاة الفجر حتى تطلع الشمس.
وبعد صلاة العصر حتى تغرب الشمس.
٤٣٣
ولنا: أن النهي لغيره، وهو ترك إجابة دعوة الله، فيصح نذره، لكنه يفطر؛ احترازاً عن المعصية المجاورة، ثم يقضي؛ إسقاطاً للواجب.
وإن صام فيه : يخرج عن نذره؛ لأنه أداه كما التزمه.
* قوله: (ويكره أن يتنفل بعد صلاة الفجر حتى تطلع الشمس، وبعد صلاة العصر حتى تغرب الشمس).
يعني قصداً، أما لو قام في العصر بعد الأربع ساهياً، أو في الفجر : لا يكره، ويُتِمُّ؛ لأنه من غير قصد.
Chapter on times in which prayer is disliked. It is disliked to perform voluntary prayer after Fajr prayer until the sun rises. And after Asr prayer until the sun sets. And for us: The prohibition is for something else (ghayr), which is abandoning responding to Allah's call, so his vow is valid, but he breaks his fast; as a precaution against the adjacent disobedience, then he makes it up; to discharge the obligation. And if he fasts in it (the disliked time): he fulfills his vow; because he performed it as he obligated himself. * His statement: (It is disliked to perform voluntary prayer after Fajr prayer until the sun rises, and after Asr prayer until the sun sets.) Meaning intentionally, but if he stood up in Asr after the four (sunnah) forgetfully, or in Fajr: it is not disliked, and he completes (the prayer); because it is without intention.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira presents the ruling on disliked times for voluntary prayers. The author states the matn: it is makruh (disliked) to perform nafl (voluntary) prayer after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset. The sharh then provides a proof (dalil) by explaining that the prohibition here is 'li-ghayrihi' (for an external reason), meaning the act itself is not inherently evil but is prohibited due to an external factor—in this case, abandoning the response to Allah's call (i.e., the time is meant for worship, but these specific times resemble sun-worship). This has implications: if someone vows to pray or fast during these times, the vow is valid (because the prohibition is not in the essence), but he must break it to avoid sin and then make it up. The commentary clarifies that the ruling applies only when one intentionally begins a voluntary prayer; if one forgetfully stands up for an extra rak'ah in Fajr or Asr, it is not disliked and he completes the prayer, as there was no intention to transgress.

Key Terms
نهي (nahy): Prohibition; in this context, it is a prohibition for an external reason (li-ghayrihi), meaning the act is not inherently evil but becomes prohibited due to an external factor.
نذر (nadhr): A vow; a promise to perform an act of worship. Here, a vow to fast or pray in disliked times is valid but must be broken to avoid sin.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed or invalidated act of worship. In this context, one must make up the prayer or fast after breaking it due to the prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone intentionally starts a voluntary prayer after Asr, what should he do?
A) Continue and complete the prayer; it is valid.
B) Cut the prayer and then make it up.
C) Cut the prayer and no compensation is required.
D) Continue but it is sinful.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayer after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset is makruh tahrimi; if begun intentionally, it must be cut and made up later.

Exceptions and Disputes in Disliked Prayer Times
Details exceptions and intra-Hanafi disputes on disliked times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exceptions to the dislike of prayer in the prohibited times and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding qada for spoiled prayers in these times.

Core Idea
Even in disliked prayer times, missed obligatory prayers, sajdah tilawah, and janazah are allowed, but tawaf rak'ahs are not, due to 'Umar's practice.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira clarifies which prayers are permitted during the times when voluntary prayer is makruh tahrimi. It also presents a dispute within the Hanafi school: when someone mistakenly begins a prayer or fast they think is obligatory and then spoils it, is qada required? The Hanafi majority says no, while Zufar says yes. Understanding these nuances is essential for correct practice and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and exceptions
State the general ruling that voluntary prayer is makruh in certain times. Then list the exceptions mentioned: fawa'it, sajdah tilawah, janazah. Note that nadhr and tawaf rak'ahs are NOT included.
The exceptions are from the zahir al-riwayah.
2
Analyze the evidence for excluding tawaf rak'ahs
The passage uses the athar of 'Umar (ra) to show that tawaf rak'ahs are disliked in these times despite being wajib. Contrast this with sajdah tilawah which is allowed. Identify the dalil (athar) and its wajh al-dalalah.
The athar is from Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on qada
Read the scenario: one begins a prayer or fast mistakenly thinking it is obligatory, then spoils it. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that no qada is required. Zufar requires qada. Work through the reasoning: the obligation never existed, so no compensation.
The dispute shows that the act was not validly begun due to the mistake.
4
Apply the dispute to specific scenarios
Consider the case of a person starting Zuhr thinking he missed it, then a follower joins as nafl, then the imam cuts the prayer. According to al-Khujandi, no qada for either; but some mashayikh require the follower to make up. Note the difference.
This highlights that even within the Hanafi school, there are variant views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتاوى صاعد قال أبو يوسف من شرع في التطوع بعد العصر : يؤمر بالقطع، ثم بالقضاء.
أما لو دخل فيها على أن العصر عليه، ثم تبين أنها ليست عليه: يؤمر
بالإتمام.
ولو شرع في صلاة، أو صوم على ظنّ أنه عليه، ثم تبين له أنه لا
شيء عليه فأفسده : لا يلزمه القضاء عندنا، وقال زفر: يلزمه.
ولو افتتح الظهر على ظنّ أنها عليه، فاقتدى به رجل بنية التطوع، ثم ذكر أنه قد صلاها، فقطعها فلا قضاء عليه، ولا على الذي اقتدى به. ذكره الخجندي في باب السهو.
وفي «النهاية»: يجب على المقتدي القضاء عند بعض المشايخ.

ويصلي على الجنازة، ولا يصلي ركعتي الطواف .

ولو أفسدها، ولم يُضف إليها أخرى: لا يلزمه قضاؤها.
وعند زفر: يلزمه قضاء ركعتين.

فإن قلت: هما واجبتان من جهة الشرع كوجوب سجدة التلاوة،
فينبغي أن يؤتى بهما في هذين الوقتين، كسجدة التلاوة. قلت: إنا عرفنا كراهتهما بالأثر، وهو ما روي «أن عمر طاف بالبيت بعد صلاة الفجر، ثم خرج من مكة، حتى إذا كان بذي طُوَى

بعد طلوع الشمس صلى ركعتين قال: ركعتان مقام ركعتين»(۱).
فقد أخرهما إلى ما بعد طلوع الشمس.
(۱) صحيح البخاري تعليقاً ٤٨٨/٣ ، وينظر فتح الباري ٤٨٩/٣ لوصله.
And in Fatawa Sa'id, Abu Yusuf said: Whoever begins a voluntary prayer after Asr is commanded to cut it, then make it up. But if he entered (the prayer) thinking that Asr was due on him, then it becomes clear that it is not due on him, he is commanded to complete it. And if he began a prayer or fast thinking it was due on him, then it becomes clear that nothing was due on him, and he spoiled it, then qada is not necessary according to us, and Zufar said: it is necessary. And if he began Zuhr thinking it was due on him, then a man followed him with the intention of voluntary prayer, then he remembered that he had already prayed it, and he cut it, then there is no qada on him, nor on the one who followed him. Al-Khujandi mentioned this in the chapter on forgetfulness. And in al-Nihaya: The follower must make it up according to some mashayikh. [Page 434] Chapter on times in which prayer is disliked. There is no harm in these two times to pray missed prayers, to prostrate for recitation, to pray over the deceased, and he should not pray the two rak'ahs of tawaf. And in al-Jundi: He should not add another rak'ah in Fajr and Asr; because voluntary prayer after them is disliked. And if he spoiled it, and did not add another to it, then qada is not necessary for him. And according to Zufar: He must make up two rak'ahs. His statement: (There is no harm in these two times to pray missed prayers, to prostrate for recitation, to pray over the deceased). And he should not pray in them the vowed (prayer), nor the two rak'ahs of tawaf, nor what he began and then spoiled. His statement: (And he should not pray the two rak'ahs of tawaf). For if you say: They are obligatory from the perspective of the law like the obligation of the prostration of recitation, so it should be performed in these two times, like the prostration of recitation. I say: We know their dislike through the athar, which is what was narrated that 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) performed tawaf after Fajr prayer, then left Makkah until when he was at Dhi Tuwa after sunrise, he prayed two rak'ahs and said: Two rak'ahs in place of two rak'ahs.' So he delayed them until after sunrise.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira covers several detailed rulings and intra-Hanafi disputes concerning the disliked prayer times. It begins by citing a fatwa from Abu Yusuf: if someone starts a voluntary prayer after Asr, he is commanded to cut it and then make it up (qada). However, if one enters a prayer thinking it is obligatory (e.g., he thinks he missed Asr), then discovers it is not, he completes it. Then there is a dispute: if one begins a prayer or fast mistakenly thinking it is required, then finds out it is not, and then spoils it, the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) says no qada is required, while Zufar says qada is required. A scenario is given: a person starts Zuhr thinking it is obligatory, a follower joins with intention of nafl, then the imam remembers he already prayed and cuts the prayer; no qada is required for either, according to al-Khujandi, but al-Nihaya records that some mashayikh require the follower to make up. The chapter then states exceptions: missed prayers (fawa'it), sajdah tilawah, and janazah prayer are allowed in these times. However, nadhr (vowed prayers) and the two rak'ahs of tawaf are not allowed. The reason for prohibiting tawaf rak'ahs is given based on the athar (tradition) of 'Umar (ra): he performed tawaf after Fajr but delayed the two rak'ahs until after sunrise. This serves as a proof that the two rak'ahs of tawaf are disliked in these times despite being wajib, because the prohibition is for an external reason. Lastly, there is a dispute with Zufar: if one spoils a prayer in these times without adding another rak'ah, no qada is required according to the Hanafi school, but Zufar requires qada of two rak'ahs.

Key Terms
فوائت (fawa'it): Missed obligatory prayers that are being made up (qada). These are allowed in disliked times.
ركعتي الطواف (rak'atay al-tawaf): The two rak'ahs prayed after completing tawaf around the Ka'bah; they are wajib according to the Hanafi school.
أثر (athar): A tradition or report from a Companion (in this case, from 'Umar). Used as evidence for the dislike of tawaf rak'ahs in these times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are the two rak'ahs of tawaf prohibited in the disliked times despite being wajib?
A) Because they are not obligatory.
B) Because of a hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) explicitly forbidding them.
C) Because of the action of 'Umar (ra) who delayed them until after sunrise.
D) Because they are considered voluntary prayers.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, exceptions to the disliked prayer times are limited to fawa'it, sajdah tilawah, and janazah; tawaf rak'ahs are excluded by a companion tradition, and if one mistakenly prays or fasts in these times, no qada is required upon spoiling it according to the majority.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Principles for Allowed Prayers in Disliked Times
States which prayers are allowed in disliked times and the underlying principle of obligation source.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between prayers allowed and not allowed in disliked times based on whether the obligation originates from Allah or from the servant's action, and state the Hanafi position on qada' for corrupted voluntary prayers in these times.

Core Idea
What Allah obligates directly is allowed in disliked times; what the servant's act obligates is not.

This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayirah addresses which prayers may be performed during the two disliked times (after Fajr and after 'Asr). The commentator explains a foundational principle that categorises prayers based on the source of their obligation—divine command versus the servant's own action. It also addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a corrupted voluntary prayer begun in a disliked time must be made up.

Guided Path
1
Identify the allowed prayers
List the prayers that the passage explicitly permits in the two disliked times: make-up prayers (fawa'it), prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah), and funeral prayer (salat al-janazah).
Also note that these are obligated directly by Allah (bi ijab Allah).
2
Identify the prohibited prayers
List the prayers that are not allowed: two rak'ahs of tawaf, vowed prayers (al-mandhurah), corrupted voluntary prayers, and any additional voluntary prayers beyond the sunnah of Fajr and 'Asr.
These are obligated by the servant's action (mudaf ila al-'abd).
3
Understand the underlying principle
The passage states: 'That which is obligated by Allah's command is permissible, and that which is obligated in relation to the servant is not permissible.' Examine how this principle is applied to the two rak'ahs of tawaf versus sajdat al-tilawah.
Sajdat al-tilawah is wajib li 'aynihi (for its own sake) while the two rak'ahs of tawaf are wajib li ghayrihi (for completing tawaf).
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Zufar argues that a corrupted voluntary prayer in a disliked time requires qada'; the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) say no qada'. Understand each side's reasoning.
The majority holds the prayer was invalid from the start; Zufar considers it validly begun.
5
Apply the principle to the dispute
The principle that 'what is obligated by the servant's action is not allowed' implies that the prayer itself was not validly begun (since it is a servant-originated obligation), so no qada' is due.
This supports the majority view.

(1) صحيح البخاري (٦١٨)، صحيح مسلم (۷۲۳)، وينظر التعريف والإخبار (٢) أي أن صلاة فرض آخر، كمن عليه قضاء، في وقت سنة الفجر: يجوز؛ لأنه فوق سنة الفجر.
Chapter on the times when prayer is disliked. There is no harm in praying make-up prayers in these two times, and performing the prostration of recitation, and praying the funeral prayer, but he should not pray the two rak'ahs of tawaf. And in al-Jundi: He should not add another rak'ah in Fajr and 'Asr, because voluntary prayer after them is disliked. And if he corrupts it and does not add another to it, he is not required to make it up. According to Zufar, he is required to make up two rak'ahs. His statement: 'There is no harm in praying make-up prayers in these two times, and performing the prostration of recitation, and praying the funeral prayer.' And he should not pray in them the vowed prayer, nor the two rak'ahs of tawaf, nor what he began and then corrupted. His statement: 'And he does not pray the two rak'ahs of tawaf.' If you say: They are obligatory from the perspective of the Law like the obligation of the prostration of recitation, so it should be performed in these two times like the prostration of recitation. I say: We know their dislikedness by the narration, which is what was narrated that 'Umar performed tawaf around the House after Fajr prayer, then left Mecca until when he was at Dhu Tuwa (may Allah be pleased with him) after sunrise, he prayed two rak'ahs and said: 'Two rak'ahs in place of two rak'ahs.' So he delayed them until after sunrise. (1) Sahih al-Bukhari mu'allaqan 3/488, see Fath al-Bari 3/489 for its connection. And the principle is: That which is obligated by Allah's command is permissible in these two times, and that which is obligated in relation to the servant is not permissible, like the vowed prayer, the voluntary prayer that he corrupts, and the two rak'ahs of tawaf, because their obligation is by his action, which is his commencing tawaf. If you say: The obligation of the prostration of recitation is by his action, which is recitation. I say: The obligation in it is for its own sake, while in the two rak'ahs of tawaf the obligation is for something else, i.e., for other than the time, which is the completion of tawaf and preserving the performed action from dislikedness. His statement: 'It is disliked to perform voluntary prayer after dawn more than the two rak'ahs of the sunnah of Fajr,' because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not add more than them. (1) Sahih al-Bukhari (618), Sahih Muslim (723), see al-Ta'rif wa al-Ikhbar. Shaykh al-Islam said: The prohibition of what is other than them is for the sake of the two rak'ahs of Fajr, not due to a defect in the time, because the time is specifically for them, such that if one intends a voluntary prayer, it becomes from them, so he is prevented from another voluntary prayer so that all the time remains as if occupied by them, but another obligatory prayer is above the two rak'ahs of Fajr (2), so it is permissible to direct the time to it. (2) i.e., another obligatory prayer, like one who has a make-up prayer in the time of the sunnah of Fajr, is permissible because it is above the sunnah of Fajr.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayirah is a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar discussing the chapter on times when prayer is disliked (specifically after Fajr and after 'Asr). The commentator begins by stating the base ruling: in these two disliked times, one may perform make-up prayers (fawa'it), the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah), and the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). However, one should not pray the two rak'ahs of tawaf. The commentary then adds a detail from 'al-Jundi': one should not add another rak'ah to a voluntary prayer begun in Fajr or 'Asr, because voluntary prayer after these times is disliked. If one corrupts such a prayer and does not add another rak'ah, he is not required to make it up according to the Hanafi school; but Zufar holds that he must make up two rak'ahs. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The commentator then explains that the base matn prohibits not only the two rak'ahs of tawaf but also vowed prayers (al-mandhurah) and any voluntary prayer that one begins and then corrupts. A potential objection is raised: both the two rak'ahs of tawaf and sajdat al-tilawah are wajib by the Law, so why allow one and not the other? The commentator answers by citing an athar from 'Umar (ra) who delayed the two rak'ahs of tawaf until after sunrise, indicating their dislikedness during the prohibited times. The underlying principle is then articulated: any obligation that comes directly from Allah (e.g., make-up prayers, sajdat al-tilawah, funeral prayer) is permissible in disliked times, whereas any obligation that is caused by the servant's own action (e.g., vowed prayer, a corrupted voluntary prayer, the two rak'ahs of tawaf) is not permissible. The reason for the two rak'ahs of tawaf being disliked is that their obligation is due to the servant's act of beginning tawaf, and the purpose is to complete tawaf, not to pray at that specific time. In contrast, sajdat al-tilawah is obligatory for its own sake once the verse is recited, so it is not tied to a specific time and thus can be performed in disliked times. Finally, the passage addresses voluntary prayer after dawn: it is disliked to pray more than the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr, because the Prophet did not increase beyond them. The prohibition of other voluntary prayers is to honor the time of the Fajr sunnah, not because the time itself is inherently flawed. However, if one has an obligatory prayer to make up, it takes precedence over the sunnah and is permissible because it is of higher rank.

Key Terms
الفوائت (al-fawa'it): Make-up prayers for missed obligatory prayers.
ركعتي الطواف (rak'atay al-tawaf): Two rak'ahs prayed after completing tawaf around the Ka'bah.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran.
المنذورة (al-mandhurah): A prayer vowed by a person (nadhr) making it obligatory upon themselves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for allowing make-up prayers in disliked times?
A) They are obligatory and cannot be missed.
B) They are obligated by Allah's command, not the servant's action.
C) They are minor prayers.
D) The Prophet specifically permitted them.

Key Takeaway
Prayers obligated directly by Allah are exempt from the disliked time restriction; those obligated by the servant's action are not.

Salah — Prayer

Makruh Times for Nafl: After Fajr Dawn and Before Maghrib
Ruling with proof: explains makruh times and underlying principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supererogatory prayer after Fajr dawn and before Maghrib, apply the underlying principle regarding obligations, and distinguish between times disliked due to conflict and times disliked due to inherent flaws.

Core Idea
Extra nafl after Fajr dawn and before Maghrib is disliked not because the time is flawed, but to preserve the priority of superior acts.

This passage from the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri addresses a common question: when is it disliked to pray voluntary prayers? The Hanafi school distinguishes between obligations that are tied to the time and those that arise from the servant's action. Understanding this distinction helps clarify why some prayers are allowed in these times while others are not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage states two specific rulings: (1) It is disliked to perform voluntary prayer (nafl) after Fajr dawn beyond the two rak'ahs of Sunnah of Fajr. (2) It is disliked to perform any voluntary prayer before Maghrib. Note the hukm level: makruh tanzihi.
The dislike is not absolute; the prayers are valid but one should avoid them.
2
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
For the first ruling, the proof is that the Prophet (ﷺ) never prayed more than two rak'ahs after Fajr dawn. This is a Sunnah ahad report (Bukhari and Muslim). The Hanafi school interprets the Prophet's consistent practice as indicating disapproval (karahah).
The second ruling (before Maghrib) is not explicitly proved by a specific hadith in this passage; it is deduced from the general principle of avoiding delay of the obligatory prayer.
3
Understand the underlying principle (asl)
The commentator states a key principle: that which is obligatory by Allah's direct command (e.g., the five daily prayers, missed fard prayers) is permissible in these two times. However, that which becomes obligatory due to the servant's own action (e.g., a vowed prayer, the two rak'ahs of Tawaf, making up a spoiled nafl) is not permissible. The reason is that the latter obligations are tied to the person's action, not to the time itself, so they are subject to the dislike of the time.
This principle helps resolve apparent contradictions, such as why the two rak'ahs of Tawaf are disliked but a missed Fajr prayer is not.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal inference)
From the hadith, the Hanafi scholars derive that the Prophet's omission of extra prayer indicates that doing so is not recommended. Since the Prophet had the ability to pray more but did not, it implies that praying more is disliked. This is a form of dalil al-fi'l (action-based evidence) and the Hanafi usul principle that the Prophet's persistent abandonment of an act indicates disapproval.
The dalala is zanni (probative), which is why the ruling is makruh tanzihi rather than haram.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and evaluate the response
The Shafi'i school holds that it is permissible to pray extra nafl after Fajr dawn, citing general permission for prayer at any time. The Hanafi response is that the specific practice of the Prophet provides a restriction. The passage also addresses a possible objection regarding sajdat al-tilawah and clarifies the principle further.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a Hanafi will avoid extra nafl after Fajr, while a Shafi'i may pray it.

Source Text

باب الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة
ويكره أن يتنفل بعد طلوع الفجر بأكثر من ركعتي سنة الفجر.
والأصل: أن ما وجب بإيجاب الله : فإنه يجوز في هذين الوقتين، وما وجب مضافاً إلى العبد : لا يجوز، كالمنذورة، والنفل الذي يفسده، وركعتي الطواف؛ لأن وجوبهما بفعله، وهو شروعه في الطواف.
فإن قلت: وجوب سجدة التلاوة بفعله، وهو التلاوة.
قلت: الوجوب فيها لعينه، وفي ركعتي الطواف الوجوب فيها لغيره، أي لغير الوقت، وهو ختم الطواف، وصيانة المؤدى عن الكراهة.
قوله: (ويكره أن يتنفل بعد طلوع الفجر بأكثر من ركعتي سنة الفجر)؛ لأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام لم يزد عليهما.
قال شيخ الإسلام النهي عما سواهما لحق ركعتي الفجر، لا لخلل في الوقت؛ لأن الوقت متعيّن لهما، حتى لو نوى تطوعاً: كان عنهما، فقد منع عن تطوع آخر ؛ ليبقى جميع الوقت كالمشغول بهما، لكنَّ صلاة فرض آخر : فوق ركعتي الفجر، فجاز أن يُصرف الوقت إليه.
وفي التجنيس : من صلى تطوعاً في آخر الليل، فلما صلى ركعة: طلع الفجر: كان الإتمام أفضل ؛ لأن وقوعه في التطوع بعد طلوع الفجر لا عن قصد.
قال في «الفتاوى» : ولا ينوبان عن سنة الفجر، على الأصح. ولو صلى ركعتين وهو يظن أن الفجر لم يطلع، ثم تبين أنه قد طلع: فإنه يجزئه عن ركعتي الفجر، ولا ينبغي أن يعيد.
قوله: (ولا يتنفَّلُ قبل المغرب) ؛ لما فيه من تأخير المغرب، فإن المبادرة إلى أداء المغرب مستحب، فكان النهي لئلا يكون النفل شاغلاً عن أداء المغرب، لا لمعنى في الوقت.
وكذا التنفل بعد خروج الإمام للخطبة يكره؛ لئلا يتشاغل عن سماعها، لا لمعنى في الوقت، والله أعلم.
Chapter on times when prayer is disliked.
It is disliked to perform supererogatory prayer after dawn more than the two rak'ahs of the Sunnah of Fajr.
The principle: that which is obligatory by Allah's command is permissible in these two times, and that which is obligatory attributed to the servant is not permissible, such as the vowed prayer, the supererogatory prayer that one spoils, and the two rak'ahs of Tawaf; because their obligation is by his action, that is, his commencement of Tawaf.
If you say: The obligation of the prostration of recitation is by his action, that is, recitation.
I say: Its obligation is for itself, while in the two rak'ahs of Tawaf the obligation is for other than itself, that is, for other than the time, which is the completion of Tawaf, and safeguarding the performed act from dislike.
His statement: (It is disliked to perform supererogatory prayer after dawn more than the two rak'ahs of the Sunnah of Fajr) because the Prophet, peace be upon him, did not exceed them.
Shaykh al-Islam said: The prohibition of other than them is for the sake of the two rak'ahs of Fajr, not due to a defect in the time; because the time is exclusive to them, such that if one intends a supererogatory prayer, it becomes from them, so he is prevented from another supererogatory prayer so that the entire time remains as if occupied by them, but another obligatory prayer is above the two rak'ahs of Fajr, so it is permissible to direct the time to it.
In al-Tajnis: Whoever prays a supererogatory prayer at the end of the night, and when he prays one rak'ah dawn breaks: completing it is better because its occurrence in supererogatory prayer after dawn is without intention.
He said in al-Fatawa: They do not substitute for the Sunnah of Fajr, according to the soundest opinion. If one prays two rak'ahs thinking that dawn has not risen, then it becomes clear that it has risen: it suffices for the two rak'ahs of Fajr, and he should not repeat.
His statement: (And he should not perform supererogatory prayer before Maghrib) because of the delay of Maghrib contained therein, for hastening to perform Maghrib is recommended, so the prohibition is lest the supererogatory prayer occupy one from performing Maghrib, not due to a meaning in the time.
Similarly, supererogatory prayer after the Imam comes out for the sermon is disliked, lest he be distracted from listening to it, not due to a meaning in the time, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, discussing times when supererogatory prayer is disliked. The chapter begins by stating it is disliked to pray nafl after Fajr dawn more than the two rak'ahs of the Sunnah of Fajr. The commentator then explains a general principle: obligations that come directly from Allah (like the five daily prayers) are allowed in these two times (after Fajr and before Maghrib), but obligations that arise from the servant's own action (like a vowed prayer, making up a spoiled nafl, or the two rak'ahs of Tawaf) are not allowed because their obligation is tied to the person's action, not to the time itself. A potential objection is raised about the prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah), whose obligation also comes from the servant's action (recitation). The reply is that sajdah tilawah is obligatory for itself (its obligation is inherent in the act of recitation), whereas the two rak'ahs of Tawaf are obligatory for something else (completing the Tawaf), so they are disliked in the prohibited times. The commentary then cites the hadith that the Prophet never prayed more than two rak'ahs after Fajr dawn, establishing the ruling. Shaykh al-Islam explains that the prohibition of extra nafl is to preserve the time for the Sunnah of Fajr, not because the time itself is inherently flawed. In fact, obligatory prayers (like missed ones) are allowed during that time, as they are superior to the Sunnah. The text then discusses a scenario where one starts a nafl before dawn and it continues after dawn: completing it is better. A fatwa states that such a prayer does not count for the Sunnah of Fajr, but if one mistakenly prayed the Sunnah after dawn thinking it was still night, it suffices and should not be repeated. Finally, it is disliked to pray nafl before Maghrib because it delays the obligatory Maghrib prayer, which is recommended to perform early. Similarly, praying nafl during the Friday sermon is disliked because it distracts from listening. In both cases, the dislike is due to the conflict with a superior act, not because the time is inherently disliked.

Key Terms
التطوع (al-tatawwu'): Supererogatory or voluntary prayer, also called nafl.
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of sunnah before the Fajr obligatory prayer, emphasized (sunnah mu'akkadah).
ركعتي الطواف (rak'atay al-tawaf): The two rak'ahs prayed after completing the Tawaf around the Ka'bah; they are wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it disliked to pray nafl before Maghrib?
A) Because the time before Maghrib is inherently disliked.
B) Because it delays the obligatory Maghrib prayer, which is recommended to be performed early.
C) Because the Prophet forbade any prayer at that time.
D) Because it distracts from the Friday sermon.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school dislikes extra nafl after Fajr dawn and before Maghrib not because the time is inherently flawed, but to preserve the priority of the Sunnah of Fajr and the recommended early performance of Maghrib.

Why is Voluntary Prayer Before Maghrib Disliked?
States the ruling and reason for dislike of voluntary prayer before Maghrib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why voluntary prayer before Maghrib is disliked in the Hanafi school and distinguish between dislike due to the time itself versus due to delaying an obligation.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer before Maghrib is disliked not because the time is bad, but because it delays the obligatory prayer.

In this passage, the author clarifies a common misconception: the dislike (karahah) of voluntary prayer before Maghrib is not due to the time itself being inherently disliked, but because it delays the performance of the obligatory Maghrib prayer, which is recommended to be performed promptly. This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi approach to legal rulings based on reasoning (ta'lil).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the passage and find the stated ruling: voluntary prayer before Maghrib is disliked (makruh).
2
Locate the reason given in the text
The text explicitly says: 'because it involves delaying Maghrib, for hastening to perform Maghrib is recommended.'
3
Distinguish between dislike of the time and dislike due to distraction
The author emphasizes that the prohibition is 'not due to any inherent meaning in the time.' The dislike is purely because it delays an obligation.
4
Apply the reasoning to the parallel case of Friday sermon
The text mentions that voluntary prayer after the imam comes out for the sermon is also disliked for the same reason: it distracts from listening to the sermon.

Chapter of the times in which prayer is disliked. And he should not perform voluntary prayer before Maghrib. He said in al-Fatawa: And they do not substitute for the sunnah of Fajr, according to the more correct view. Likewise, voluntary prayer after the imam comes out for the sermon is disliked, so as not to be distracted from hearing it, not due to any inherent meaning in the time. And Allah knows best.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the chapter on disliked times for prayer. The core ruling is that performing voluntary prayer (nafl) before the Maghrib prayer is makruh (disliked). The commentary explains that the reason for this dislike is not because the time itself is inherently disliked, but because it delays the performance of the obligatory Maghrib prayer, which is recommended to be done promptly. The text also mentions a related case: if a person prays two rak'ahs thinking Fajr has not yet risen, but it becomes clear that it had risen, those two rak'ahs suffice for the sunnah of Fajr, and repeating them is not recommended. Additionally, voluntary prayer after the imam has come out for the Friday sermon is also disliked, for the same reason: it distracts from listening to the sermon. The author emphasizes that the dislike is due to external factors (distraction from obligation), not because the time is impermissible.

يتنفَّل (yatanafafal): Performs voluntary (supererogatory) prayer.
يكره (yukrah): It is disliked (makruh), meaning it is better to avoid, but not sinful.

Defining Nafl: Scope and Relationship to Sunnah
Defines the term 'nafl' linguistically and technically, distinguishing it from sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'nafl' linguistically and technically, and correctly classify any voluntary act as nafl or sunnah according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Nafl is any voluntary worship beyond what is required; every sunnah is a nafl but not all nafl are sunnah.

Before we dive into the rulings of supererogatory prayers, we must first understand the terminology. This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira lays out the Hanafi definition of 'nafl' (supererogatory act) and explains how it relates to the more specific category of 'sunnah'. This distinction is crucial for correctly classifying voluntary acts and understanding the hierarchy of reward and emphasis.

Guided Path
1
Extract the linguistic meaning
Identify the root meaning of 'nafl' (increase) and note the examples given (spoils of war, grandchild) to anchor the term.
The verse from Al-Anbiya (21:72) is cited as a linguistic proof.
2
Identify the technical definition
Locate the phrase 'عبارة عن فعل ليس بفرض، ولا واجب، ولا مسنون' and parse each negation. This gives the strict sense of nafl as an act that is not obligatory (fard/wajib) and not even a sunnah.
This definition may seem to exclude sunnah, but the next step resolves the apparent contradiction.
3
Analyze the relationship between nafl and sunnah
Read the key sentence: 'وكل سنة : نافلةٌ، وليس كل نافلة : سُنَّةٌ'. Understand that sunnah is a subset of nafl; the broader category (nafl) includes both emphasized and non-emphasized acts, while sunnah refers specifically to those with prophetic practice.
Thus, nafl is used in two senses: broad (encompassing all voluntary acts) and narrow (excluding sunnah).
4
Understand the purpose of nafl
Read Imam Abu Zayd's statement that nafl compensates for deficiencies in fard. This explains why even perfect performers are not blamed for leaving sunan.
This teleological insight helps us appreciate the wisdom behind supererogatory acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
النَّفْل في اللغة هو الزيادة، ومنه سُمِّيت الغنيمة: نفلاً؛ لأنها زيادة على ما وضع له الجهاد، وهو إعلاء كلمة الله.
وسمي ولد الولد : نافلة؛ لأنه زيادة على الولد، قال الله تعالى: وَوَهَبْنَا لَهُ إِسْحَقَ وَيَعْقُوبَ نَافِلَةً ) . الأنبياء / ٧٢.
ـ وفي الشرع : عبارة عن فعل ليس بفرض، ولا واجب، ولا مسنون. وكل سنة : نافلةٌ، وليس كل نافلة : سُنَّةٌ، فلهذا لقبه بالنوافل؛ لأنها مشتملة على السنن. وفي النهاية»: لقبه بالنوافل وفيه ذكرُ السنن؛ لكون النوافل أعم، كما لقب الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة.
قال الإمام أبو زيد : النفل شرع لجبرِ نقصان يمكن في الفرض؛ لأن العبد وإن علت رتبته لا يخلو عن تقصير، حتى إن أحداً لو قدر أن يصلي الفرض من غير تقصير : لا يُلام على ترك السنن.
Chapter of the voluntary prayers. Linguistically, 'nafl' is increase; from this spoils of war are called 'nafl' because it is an increase over what jihad is intended for, which is elevating the word of Allah. And the child's child is called 'nafila' because it is an increase over the child; Allah said: 'And We gave him Isaac and Jacob as a gift (nafilatan).' [Al-Anbiya 72]. In sacred law, it is an expression for an action that is not fard, nor wajib, nor sunnah. And every sunnah is a nafila, but not every nafila is a sunnah; therefore he titled it with 'nawafil' because it includes the sunan. In al-Nihaya: He titled it with 'nawafil' and in it mentions the sunan because the nawafil are more general, just as he titled the times in which prayer is disliked. Imam Abu Zayd said: The nafl is legislated to compensate for possible shortcomings in the fard; because the servant, though high in rank, is not free from deficiency, so much so that if one could pray the fard without deficiency, he would not be blamed for abandoning the sunan.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on supererogatory prayers (nawafil). It begins by defining 'nafl' linguistically as 'increase,' giving examples: spoils of war are called nafl because they are an increase beyond the primary objective of jihad, and a grandchild is called nafila as an increase over one's child, supported by Quranic verse (21:72). Technically (in sacred law), nafl is defined as any act that is not fard (obligatory), wajib (necessary), or sunnah (recommended). Importantly, the author clarifies the relationship between 'nafl' and 'sunnah': every sunnah is a nafl, but not every nafl is a sunnah. Sunnah is a more specific category of voluntary acts that have particular emphasis from the Prophet. Thus, the chapter is titled 'Nawafil' (plural of nafl) because it encompasses the sunnan (plural of sunnah). The passage further quotes Imam Abu Zayd, stating that nafl is legislated to compensate for potential deficiencies in the performance of obligatory acts, recognizing that humans are imperfect. If one could perform the fard perfectly, there would be no blame for leaving the sunan.

Key Terms
النَّفْل (al-nafl): Linguistically means increase; technically, any voluntary act of worship that is not fard, wajib, or sunnah (narrow sense) or all voluntary acts (broad sense).
السُّنَّة (al-sunnah): A recommended act established by the Prophet, which is a type of nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are synonyms.
B) Every sunnah is a nafl, but not every nafl is a sunnah.
C) Every nafl is a sunnah, but not every sunnah is a nafl.
D) They are completely separate categories.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, 'nafl' is the genus of all voluntary acts; 'sunnah' is a species within it, distinguished by prophetic practice.

Definition of Nafil and the Ruling of the Sunnah of Fajr
Definition of nafil and ruling on sunnah of Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define nafil, distinguish it from sunnah, and state the Hanafi ruling on the sunnah of Fajr along with its conditions and evidence.

Core Idea
Sunnah of Fajr is the most emphasized sunnah, close to wajib, but not obligatory.

In this lesson, we begin the chapter on supererogatory prayers (nawafil) by clarifying the term 'nafil' itself: it means 'increase' and in Islamic law refers to any act of worship that is not required. The sunnah of Fajr is singled out as the most stressed of the regular sunan, with conditions and proofs that highlight its special status. You will learn why it is considered sunnah muakkadah and what practical rules apply to its performance.

Guided Path
1
Define nafil linguistically and technically
Identify the linguistic root of 'nafl' (increase) and its technical meaning as an act that is not fard, wajib, or sunnah. Note the examples given: spoils of war and grandchildren.
The technical definition is hierarchical: every sunnah is a nafil, but not every nafil is a sunnah.
2
Distinguish nafil from sunnah
Understand that sunnah is a subset of nafil, specifically those acts the Prophet regularly performed. The chapter title 'Nawafil' includes sunan because nafil is more general.
This distinction is sharper in Hanafi fiqh than in some other schools.
3
State the ruling on the sunnah of Fajr
The text says it is the most emphasized sunnah, 'close to wajib'. Identify the mufta bihi (sunnah muakkadah) and note the weak opinion (qila) that it is wajib.
The strong emphasis does not raise it to the level of obligation.
4
List the conditions for its valid performance
Extract the conditions: must be after true dawn (fajr sadiq), must be performed standing if able, and must not be performed riding without an excuse.
Sitting or riding without excuse renders the act makruh tahrimi but still valid (according to the weak view, it would be invalid if wajib).
5
Examine the proofs (adillah)
Review the hadith: 'They are better than the world and all it contains' and 'Pray them even if the cavalry charges at you.' Also note the Prophet's constant practice in travel and residence. Analyze why these indicate sunnah not wajib.
The Hanafi principle: an emphatic command can indicate wujub unless there is a contrary indicator; here the virtue language and permissibility of leaving in danger show it is sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
النَّفْل في اللغة هو الزيادة، ومنه سُمِّيت الغنيمة: نفلاً؛ لأنها زيادة على ما وضع له الجهاد، وهو إعلاء كلمة الله.
وسمي ولد الولد : نافلة؛ لأنه زيادة على الولد، قال الله تعالى: وَوَهَبْنَا لَهُ إِسْحَقَ وَيَعْقُوبَ نَافِلَةً ) . الأنبياء / ٧٢.
ـ وفي الشرع : عبارة عن فعل ليس بفرض، ولا واجب، ولا مسنون. وكل سنة : نافلةٌ، وليس كل نافلة : سُنَّةٌ، فلهذا لقبه بالنوافل؛ لأنها مشتملة على السنن. وفي النهاية»: لقبه بالنوافل وفيه ذكرُ السنن؛ لكون النوافل أعم، كما لقب الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة.
قال الإمام أبو زيد : النفل شرع لجبرِ نقصان يمكن في الفرض؛ لأن العبد وإن علت رتبته لا يخلو عن تقصير، حتى إن أحداً لو قدر أن يصلي الفرض من غير تقصير : لا يُلام على ترك السنن (۱).
السُّنَّةُ في الصلاة : أن يصلي ركعتين بعد طلوع الفجر .
قال رحمه الله : السُّنَّةُ في الصلاة أن يصلي ركعتين بعد طلوع الفجر.
بدأ بسنة الفجر ؛ لأنها أكد من سائر السنن ، ولهذا قيل: إنها قريبة من الواجب.
ولا يجوز أن يصليها قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام.
ولا يجوز أداؤها راكباً من غير عذر.
ولأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام لم يَدَعها في سفر، ولا حضر. وقال في ركعتي الفجر : هما خير من الدنيا وما فيها. وقال: «صلوها ولو طرقتكم الخيل».
وقدم في المبسوط سُنَّةَ الظهر ؛ لأنها تبع للظهر، والظهر أول صلاة فرضت.
وقيل: إن سنة الفجر واجبةٌ، حتى لو انتهى إلى الإمام وهو في صلاة الفجر، وخشي أن تفوته ركعةٌ : فإنه يصليها بعد الصف، ويدخل مع الإمام بعد فراغه منها.
Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers. Linguistically, nafal means increase. From it, spoils of war are called nafal because they are an increase upon what was set for jihad, which is raising the word of Allah. The grandchild is called nafil because it is an increase upon the child. Allah Most High said: 'And We gave him Isaac and Jacob as a gift' (21:72). Technically, it is an action that is not fard, not wajib, and not sunnah. Every sunnah is nafilah, but not every nafilah is sunnah. For this reason, the author titled it 'Nawafil' because it includes the sunan. In al-Nihayah: He titled it Nawafil and mentioned the sunan because nawafil is more general, just as he titled the times in which prayer is disliked. Imam Abu Zayd said: Nafil is legislated to compensate for a deficiency that may occur in the fard, because a servant, no matter how high his rank, is not free from shortcomings. Indeed, if one were able to pray the fard without any shortcoming, he would not be blamed for leaving the sunan. The sunnah in prayer is to pray two rak'ahs after dawn. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The sunnah in prayer is to pray two rak'ahs after dawn. He began with the sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized than other sunan, and for this reason it is said that it is close to wajib. It is not permissible to pray it sitting while able to stand. It is not permissible to perform it riding without an excuse. Because the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) never abandoned it in travel or residence. He said regarding the two rak'ahs of Fajr: 'They are better than the world and all it contains.' And he said: 'Pray them even if the cavalry charges at you.' In al-Mabsut, he presented the sunnah of Dhuhr first because it follows Dhuhr, and Dhuhr was the first prayer made obligatory. And it is said that the sunnah of Fajr is wajib, such that if one arrives at the imam while he is in the Fajr prayer and fears missing a rak'ah, he prays it behind the row and enters with the imam after finishing it.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on supererogatory prayers (nawafil). The author first defines 'nafl' linguistically as 'increase' and gives examples including spoils of war and grandchildren. Technically, nafil is any act that is not fard, wajib, or sunnah. Crucially, every sunnah is a nafil, but not every nafil is a sunnah. This hierarchy distinguishes between general supererogatory acts and specifically recommended sunan (like the sunan rawatib). The author notes that Imam Abu Zayd viewed nafil as compensating for deficiencies in obligatory acts. The second part addresses the specific sunnah of Fajr: two rak'ahs after dawn. This sunnah is the most emphasized, even described as 'close to wajib.' Conditions include standing if able (not sitting) and not riding without excuse, as the Prophet never omitted them. Proofs include authentic hadith on their virtue. A minority view (qila) considers them wajib, with a practical consequence: if one arrives late to Fajr congregation, they should pray the sunnah first behind the row before joining the imam. However, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that it is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib. The text also notes that in al-Mabsut, the sunnah of Dhuhr is mentioned first because Dhuhr was the first obligatory prayer.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Linguistically increase; technically any act of worship that is not fard, wajib, or sunnah.
السنة (al-sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet regularly performed, considered a subset of nafil.
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): Two rak'ahs prayed after dawn before the obligatory Fajr prayer, the most emphasized of the regular sunnan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on performing the sunnah of Fajr while sitting if one is able to stand?
A) It is permissible and valid.
B) It is not permissible (makruh tahrimi) but the prayer is valid.
C) The prayer is invalid.
D) It is recommended to sit for humility.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of Fajr is the most emphasized supererogatory prayer, sunnah muakkadah, not wajib; its conditions include standing and not riding without excuse, and its proofs emphasize virtue and consistency.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Fajr Sunnah: Rulings, Emphasis, and Qada
Explains the ruling, emphasis, and qada of the Fajr sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of the Fajr sunnah, explain its emphasis, and apply the mufta bihi position on making it up when missed individually.

Core Idea
The Fajr sunnah is the most emphasized sunnah, close to wajib, but not made up when missed individually.

The Fajr sunnah holds a unique position among the supererogatory prayers. This lesson examines its ruling, conditions, and the important dispute within the Hanafi school on whether it should be made up if missed. We will see how the text from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira presents the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf as the relied-upon position, and why the Fajr sunnah is treated differently from other sunnah prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, recognize that the passage discusses the Fajr sunnah (two rak'ahs after dawn). The author explicitly states it is the most emphasized sunnah, and some scholars consider it close to wajib.
The Hanafi position is that it is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
2
Examine the conditions and proofs
Note the conditions: it cannot be prayed sitting if able to stand, nor riding without excuse. The proof includes hadith on its virtue and the Prophet's constant practice.
The proofs demonstrate emphasis but do not elevate it to wajib.
3
Analyze the qada dispute
The text presents a dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say no qada when missed individually; Muhammad al-Shaybani prefers qada before zawal. Understand the basis for each view.
The mufta bihi is the view of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).
4
Distinguish between missed individually vs. with fard
If missed together with the Fajr fard (e.g., both were missed), the Fajr sunnah is made up with the fard, according to the two. After zawal, only the fard is made up alone.
This exception applies only to Fajr sunnah among sunnah prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
السُّنَّةُ في الصلاة : أن يصلي ركعتين بعد طلوع الفجر .
قال رحمه الله : السُّنَّةُ في الصلاة أن يصلي ركعتين بعد طلوع الفجر.
بدأ بسنة الفجر ؛ لأنها أكد من سائر السنن ، ولهذا قيل: إنها قريبة من الواجب.
ولا يجوز أن يصليها قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام.
ولا يجوز أداؤها راكباً من غير عذر.
ولأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام لم يَدَعها في سفر، ولا حضر. وقال في ركعتي الفجر : هما خير من الدنيا وما فيها. وقال: «صلوها ولو طرقتكم الخيل».
وقدم في المبسوط سُنَّةَ الظهر ؛ لأنها تبع للظهر، والظهر أول صلاة فرضت.
وقيل: إن سنة الفجر واجبةٌ، حتى لو انتهى إلى الإمام وهو في صلاة الفجر، وخشي أن تفوته ركعةٌ : فإنه يصليها بعد الصف، ويدخل مع الإمام بعد فراغه منها.
وعن أبي جعفر : أنه إذا خشي أن تفوته الركعتان من الفرض، ويدرك الإمام في التشهد : فإنه يصلي السنةَ عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف بعد الصف، أو في الصف إن لم يجد موضعاً.
وأشد الكراهة أن يصليها مخالطاً للصف إذا كان يجد موضعاً غيره.
والسنة فيها : الأداء في البيت، وكذا سائر السنن، إلا التراويح، على ما يأتي من بيانها إن شاء الله تعالى.
ثم إذا فاتت سنة الفجر على الانفراد: لا تُقضى عندهما. وقال محمد: : أَحبُّ إليَّ أن تُقضى إذا ارتفعت الشمس إلى قبل قيام الظهيرة.
وأما عندهما فلا تُقضى إلا إذا فاتت مع الفرض تبعاً للفرض، سواء قضى الفرض بجماعة، أو وحده إلى الزوال.
وفيما بعده: اختلف المشايخ فيه :
قيل : يقضي الفرض وحده، وقيل: يقضي السنة معه.
وأما سائر السنن سواها : فلا تُقضى بعد خروج الوقت وحدها. واختلفوا في قضائها تبعاً للفرض، على ما نبين بعد.
قوله : (وأربعاً قبل الظهر) : يعني بتسليمة واحدة.
Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers. The sunnah in prayer: to pray two rak'ahs after the dawn. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: The sunnah in prayer is to pray two rak'ahs after the dawn. He began with the sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized than other sunnahs, and it is said that it is close to obligatory. It is not permissible to pray it sitting while able to stand. Nor is it permissible to perform it riding without an excuse. And because the Prophet, peace be upon him, never abandoned it, in travel or residence. And he said about the two rak'ahs of Fajr: 'They are better than the world and everything in it.' And he said: 'Pray them even if the horses trample you.' And in al-Mabsut, the sunnah of Zuhr is presented first because it is a follower of Zuhr, and Zuhr is the first prayer that was made obligatory. It is said that the sunnah of Fajr is obligatory, such that if one arrives at the imam while he is in the Fajr prayer, and fears missing a rak'ah, he prays it behind the line (of worshippers) and then joins the imam after finishing it. And from Abu Ja'far: if one fears missing two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer and catches the imam in tashahhud, he prays the sunnah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf after the line, or in the line if he finds no other place. It is severely disliked to pray it intermingled with the line if he finds another place. The sunnah for it is to perform it at home, and likewise all other sunnahs except Tarawih, as will be explained later. Then if the sunnah of Fajr is missed individually, it is not made up according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). And Muhammad said: I prefer that it be made up after the sun rises until before the noon sun stands high. As for the two, it is not made up unless it was missed together with the obligatory prayer as a follower of the obligatory prayer, whether the obligatory prayer is performed in congregation or alone until zawal. And after that, the scholars differed: it is said he prays the obligatory prayer alone, and it is said he prays the sunnah with it. As for all other sunnahs besides this, they are not made up after the time has passed alone. And they differed about making them up following the obligatory prayer, as we will explain later. His saying: 'And four before Zuhr' means with one taslim.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on supererogatory prayers (nawafil) discusses the ruling of the sunnah of Fajr. The author begins by stating that the sunnah prayer is to pray two rak'ahs after the dawn (Fajr time). He starts with the Fajr sunnah because it is the most emphasized of all sunnahs, to the point that some scholars said it is close to being obligatory (wajib). The text then gives several rules: it cannot be performed sitting if one is able to stand, nor while riding without a valid excuse. The proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) never abandoned it in travel or residence, and the hadith: 'They are better than the world and everything in it' and 'Pray them even if the horses trample you.' The author notes that in al-Mabsut, the sunnah of Zuhr is mentioned first because Zuhr was the first prayer made obligatory. However, the Fajr sunnah is more emphasized. A difference of opinion is reported: some say the Fajr sunnah is obligatory (wajib), and because of that, if one arrives at the mosque when the imam is in the Fajr prayer and fears missing a rak'ah, he should pray the sunnah behind the line (not in the row) and then join the imam after finishing it. According to Abu Ja'far, if one fears missing two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer and catches the imam in the final tashahhud, the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is that he prays the sunnah behind the line, or in the line if he finds no other space, though it is severely disliked to intermingle if he can find another place. The sunnah is to perform it at home, as with other sunnah prayers except Tarawih. Regarding making up (qada) the missed Fajr sunnah, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two, 'anhuma), if it is missed individually (i.e., not together with the obligatory prayer), it is not to be made up. Muhammad al-Shaybani prefers that it be made up after sunrise until before the sun stands high at noon. However, if it was missed together with the obligatory prayer (e.g., one missed both the sunnah and the fard), then the view of the two is that it should be made up, as a follower of the fard, whether the fard is made up in congregation or alone, as long as it is before zawal (the time when the sun passes the meridian). After zawal, the qada of the sunnah is not performed. For other sunnahs besides Fajr, they are not made up after the time has passed individually, but there is a difference regarding making them up following the fard, which will be explained later. The passage ends by clarifying that 'four before Zuhr' means with one taslim (i.e., two separate pairs or four with one salam? The text says meaning with one taslim, so it is prayed as a set of four with one taslim? Actually in Hanafi school, the four before Zuhr are prayed with two taslims, but here the text says 'means with one taslim', which is a note from the commentator; it might mean the four are two pairs of two, each pair with its own taslim. The passage as written is open to interpretation.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): Here, the supererogatory prayer (nafl) that is regularly performed by the Prophet.
القضاء (al-qada): Making up a missed prayer (whether fard or sunnah) after its time has passed.
النوافل (al-nawafil): Supererogatory prayers; plural of nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, when is the Fajr sunnah made up?
A) It is always made up, whether missed individually or with the fard.
B) It is never made up, even if missed with the fard.
C) It is made up only when missed together with the obligatory Fajr prayer before zawal.
D) It is made up only if missed individually before zawal.

Key Takeaway
The Fajr sunnah is a highly emphasized sunnah muakkadah, and the mufta bihi position is that it is not made up when missed individually, but is made up with the fard if both were missed together before zawal.

Qada of the Missed Sunnah of Fajr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada of Fajr sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up the missed sunnah of Fajr and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its permissibility.

Core Idea
The Fajr sunnah is only made up if missed with the fard, not alone.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayra addresses a specific intra-Hanafi point: when a person misses the two rak'ahs sunnah of Fajr, can they be made up? The answer depends on whether the sunnah was missed alone or with the fard, and there is a difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on one side and Imam Muhammad on the other. Understanding this ruling clarifies the principle that sunnan generally follow the fard in qada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and context
The act is missing the sunnah of Fajr. Two scenarios: missed individually (without the fard) or missed together with the fard.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They hold that if missed individually, it is not made up. If missed with the fard, it is made up following the fard until zawal.
This is the default position ('عندهما').
3
State the position of Muhammad al-Shaybani
He prefers that it be made up if missed individually, from sunrise until just before noon.
His view is expressed as 'أحب إلي'.
4
Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
One who misses the Fajr sunnah alone should not make it up according to the mufta bihi, but if one follows Muhammad, they may make it up before zawal.
After zawal, the dispute shifts for the fard-sunnah pair.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the Fajr sunnah is not made up when missed individually.
Muhammad's view is a valid preference but not the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إذا فاتت سنة الفجر على الانفراد: لا تُقضى عندهما. وقال محمد : أحب إليَّ أن تُقضى إذا ارتفعت الشمس إلى قبل قيام الظهيرة. وأما عندهما فلا تُقضى إلا إذا فاتت مع الفرض تبعاً للفرض، سواء قضى الفرض بجماعة أو وحده إلى الزوال. (1) وفيما بعده: اختلف المشايخ فيه : قيل : يقضي الفرض وحده، وقيل: يقضي السنة معه. وأما سائر السنن سواها : فلا تُقضى بعد خروج الوقت وحدها. واختلفوا في قضائها تبعاً للفرض، على ما نبين بعد.
Then if the sunnah of Fajr is missed individually, it is not made up according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). And Muhammad said: I prefer that it be made up from when the sun rises until just before noon. And according to the two, it is only made up if it was missed with the obligatory, following the obligatory, whether he made up the obligatory in congregation or alone until zawal. (1) And after it (after zawal), the mashayikh differed: some said he makes up the obligatory alone, and some said he makes up the sunnah with it. And as for other sunnan besides it, they are not made up after the time exits alone. And they differed about making them up following the obligatory, as we will clarify later.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute on making up the missed sunnah of Fajr. The two imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that if the Fajr sunnah is missed individually (i.e., without the fard), it is not made up at all. However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani prefers that it be made up between sunrise and before zawal. If the Fajr sunnah is missed together with the fard (i.e., one missed both), then according to the two imams, it is made up along with the fard, and this can be done until zawal. After zawal, there is a difference among later scholars: some say only the fard is made up, others say both the fard and sunnah are made up. For other sunnan (like those of Zuhr), they are not made up individually after their time leaves, but there is disagreement about making them up along with the fard. This ruling is based on the principle that sunnan follow the fard in qada.

Key Terms
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Making up a missed prayer after its designated time has passed.
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs sunnah prayed before the Fajr obligatory prayer.
تبعاً للفرض (tabaʿan lil-farḍ): Following the obligatory, i.e., the sunnah is made up only if the fard is also made up.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, when is the Fajr sunnah made up?
A) It is always made up, whether missed alone or with the fard.
B) It is only made up if missed together with the fard, until zawal.
C) It is never made up under any circumstance.
D) It is made up only if missed alone, from sunrise to zawal.

Key Takeaway
The Fajr sunnah is made up only when missed with the fard, and this is limited to before zawal according to the majority Hanafi position.
