The Four Rak'ahs Before Zuhr: Method and Status
Ruling on the number and method of the sunnah before Zuhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for the four rak'ahs before Zuhr and explain the correct method (one taslim) and the underlying qiyas principle.

Core Idea
The four before Zuhr are sunnah mu'akkadah, prayed as one unit with one taslim, following the fard's number.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira expands on the matn's simple statement 'and four before Zuhr'. It clarifies that these four are a confirmed sunnah, performed with one taslim, not two. The author also provides the analogical reasoning (qiyas) that supererogatory prayers match the obligatory in number, and addresses exceptions like the two rak'ahs after Zuhr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the four rak'ahs before Zuhr. The text explicitly states 'هن مؤكدات' (they are mu'akkadah). So the ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Understand the method
These four rak'ahs are to be prayed with one taslim (one concluding salam) after all four. If one prays them with two taslims (i.e., two separate pairs), it does not count as the sunnah.
The sunnah must be performed in the same manner as the fard in terms of number of rak'ahs.
3
Trace the legal reasoning
The author uses qiyas: 'النفل تبع للفرض' (the supererogatory follows the obligatory). Since Zuhr fard is four rak'ahs, its sunnah must also be four. The exception of the two-rak'ah sunnah after Zuhr is a facilitation (taysir), not the default.
This principle is applied consistently: Fajr (2 fard → 2 sunnah), Jumu'ah (originally 4, reduced to 2 due to khutbah → sunnah remains 4 per original analogy).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل وأربعاً قبل الظهر، وعن أبي جعفر : أنه إذا خشي أن تفوته الركعتان من الفرض، ويدرك الإمام في التشهد : فإنه يصلي السنةَ عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف بعد الصف، أو في الصف إن لم يجد موضعاً. وأشد الكراهة أن يصليها مخالطاً للصف إذا كان يجد موضعاً غيره. والسنة فيها : الأداء في البيت، وكذا سائر السنن، إلا التراويح، على ما يأتي من بيانها إن شاء الله تعالى. قوله : (وأربعاً قبل الظهر) : يعني بتسليمة واحدة. وهنَّ مؤكدات. قال في «المجرد»: يقرأ في كل ركعة نحواً من عشر آيات. وكذا في الأربع بعد العشاء. وإن أداهنَّ بتسليمتين: لم يُعتَدَّ بهن من السنة؛ لأن النفل تبع للفرض، والفرض أربع، فكذا النفل ، ألا ترى أن الفجر لما كانت ركعتين: كان نفله مثله. وأما بعد الظهر : شرع ركعتين تيسيراً. والجمعة أصلها أربع، وبسبب الخطبة عادت إلى ركعتين، فكان النفل أربعاً، على أصل القياس.
Chapter of supererogatory prayers. And four rak'ahs before Zuhr. And from Abu Ja'far: that if he fears that the two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer will be missed, and he catches the Imam in the tashahhud, then he prays the sunnah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf after the row, or in the row if he cannot find a place. And the strongest dislike is that he prays it mixed in the row while he can find another place. And the sunnah regarding it is performance at home, and likewise all other sunnahs, except taraweeh, as will come in its explanation, if Allah wills. His saying: (And four before Zuhr) means with one taslim. And they are mu'akkadah (confirmed). He said in al-Mujarrad: he recites in every rak'ah about ten verses. And likewise in the four after Isha. And if he performs them with two taslims, they are not counted as the sunnah because the supererogatory follows the obligatory, and the obligatory is four, so likewise the supererogatory. Do you not see that when Fajr was two rak'ahs, its supererogatory was like it. And as for after Zuhr, it was prescribed as two rak'ahs for facilitation. And Jumu'ah: its origin is four, and due to the khutbah it became two, so the supererogatory is four, based on the original analogy.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on the matn of al-Quduri. It begins by stating that the four rak'ahs before Zuhr are sunnah mu'akkadah and are prayed with one taslim, not two. The author explains that if one prays them with two taslims, it does not replace the sunnah because the supererogatory prayer follows the obligatory in number: Zuhr is four, so its sunnah is four; Fajr is two, so its sunnah is two. The exception of after Zuhr being two rak'ahs is a facilitation (taysir). Similarly, Jumu'ah's sunnah is four because its original obligation was four, reduced to two due to the khutbah. The passage also includes a ruling from Abu Ja'far: if one fears missing the two rak'ahs of the fard and catches the imam in tashahhud, he should pray the sunnah after the row, or in the row if no space. Praying mixed in the row when another place is available is highly disliked. The general sunnah is to pray these at home, except taraweeh. This expands the matn's simple statement with detailed rulings and analogical reasoning.

Key Terms
نوافل (nawāfil): Supererogatory prayers, voluntary acts of worship beyond the obligatory.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah; the Prophet ﷺ consistently performed it and rarely left it.
تسليمة (taslīmah): The greeting of salaam that concludes the prayer; one taslim to the right (or both directions) counts as one closing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a person prays the four rak'ahs before Zuhr with two taslims, what is the ruling?
A) It is valid and counts as the sunnah.
B) It is valid but does not count as the sunnah.
C) It is invalid and must be repeated.
D) It is makruh and should be avoided.

Key Takeaway
The four rak'ahs before Zuhr are sunnah mu'akkadah, prayed with one taslim, based on the principle that supererogatory prayers follow the obligatory in number.

قضاء سنة الظهر الأولى – الخلاف في النية والترتيب
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada of first Zuhr sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi imams' positions on the qada of the first Zuhr sunnah and distinguish the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
The missed Zuhr sunnah can be made up as a new nafl without qada intention – Abu Hanifa's distinctive view.

When a Hanafi misses the first sunnah of Zuhr to catch the congregation, how should it be recovered? The school's founding imams differ on both the timing and the need for a special intention. This lesson unpacks the three views and identifies the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the issue
What is the situation? The person left the four-rak'ah sunnah before Zuhr due to fear of missing the congregation. The issue: how to make it up – order relative to the two-rak'ah sunnah after Zuhr, and whether a qada intention is needed.
2
State the 'correct' view
The text begins with 'فالصحيح' (the correct view): he makes it up after the fard. This is the preferred position.
Note the use of 'al-sahih' to indicate tarjih.
3
Analyze the discrepancies among the imams
Muhammad: make it up before the two-rak'ah sunnah. Abu Yusuf: give precedence to the two-rak'ah sunnah over the four, and intend qada. The Nawadir transmission: according to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), begin with the two-rak'ah sunnah, but Muhammad said with the four; then both require qada intention. Abu Hanifa: no qada intention; it becomes a fresh nafl.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical difference: whether the missed sunnah is offered before or after the two-rak'ah sunnah, and whether one must specify 'qada' in intention. The mufta bihi is to make it up after the fard, but the dispute on niyyah remains; many later scholars adopt Abu Hanifa's view as easier.

Source Text

فإن ترك سنة الظهر الأولى خشية فوت الجماعة: فالصحيح أنه يقضيها بعد الفرض. ويقضيها قبل الركعتين عند محمد. وعند أبي يوسف: يقدم الركعتين على الأربع، وينوي القضاء. وفي «النوادر»: يبدأ بالركعتين عندهما، وقال محمد: بالأربع، ثم ينوي القضاء عندهما. وعند أبي حنيفة: لا ينوي القضاء، ويكون تطوعاً مبتدأ، فلا يفتقر إلى نية القضاء.
If he leaves the first sunnah of Zuhr for fear of missing the congregation, the correct view is that he makes it up after the obligatory prayer. And he makes it up before the two rak'ahs according to Muhammad. And according to Abu Yusuf: he gives precedence to the two rak'ahs over the four, and he makes niyyah of qada. And in al-Nawadir: he begins with the two rak'ahs according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Muhammad said: with the four, then he makes niyyah of qada according to the two. And according to Abu Hanifa: he does not make niyyah of qada, and it becomes a new supererogatory act, so he does not need the intention of qada.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage addresses the dispute among the three Hanafi imams regarding the first sunnah of Zuhr (the four rak'ahs before Zuhr) when it is missed due to fear of losing the congregation. The correct view (as reported) is that it is made up after the obligatory prayer. However, the imams differ on the details. Imam Muhammad says the missed sunnah is made up before the two-rak'ah sunnah after Zuhr. Imam Abu Yusuf says give precedence to the two-rak'ah sunnah over the four, and one must make the intention of qada (making up). The Nawadir transmission reports that according to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), one begins with the two-rak'ah sunnah, but Muhammad says begin with the four; then according to both, one makes niyyah of qada. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no niyyah of qada is needed; the prayer becomes a new nafl (supererogatory) without the obligation to specify qada. This shows the flexibility within the Hanafi school on the technicalities of making up missed sunan.

Key Terms
سنة الظهر الأولى (sunnat al-ẓuhr al-ūlā): The four-rak'ah sunnah before the Zuhr fard.
نية القضاء (niyyat al-qaḍāʾ): The intention to make up a missed prayer as a qada.
تطوع مبتدأ (taṭawwuʿ mubtadaʾ): A new, spontaneous supererogatory prayer, not a make-up.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits flexibility in making up missed rawatib, with Abu Hanifa's view that no specific qada intention is needed being the most lenient.

The Hanafi Principle: Sunnah Follows Fard in Rak'ah Number
States the number of rak'ahs for sunnah prayers and the principle that nafl follows fard.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the number of rak'ahs in emphasized sunnah prayers follows the obligatory prayer, and apply it to determine the correct rak'ahs for Fajr, Zuhr, Isha, and Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
The sunnah prayer follows the fard in number of rak'ahs; four-rak'ah sunnah must be performed with one taslim.

In this passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, Al-Quduri establishes a fundamental principle of Hanafi fiqh regarding the regular sunnah prayers (sunan rawatib). The number of rak'ahs for emphasized sunnah prayers is determined by the number of rak'ahs in the corresponding obligatory prayer. This lesson will walk through the rule, its exceptions for Zuhr and Jumu'ah, and the practical implication that four-rak'ah sunnah prayers must be performed continuously with one taslim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Read the statement: 'the supererogatory is a follower of the obligatory.' This is the key principle: the number of rak'ahs in the sunnah (nafl) follows the number in the fard prayer.
The principle is derived from the analogy with Fajr.
2
Analyze the exception for Zuhr
The text states that after Zuhr, only two rak'ahs were legislated as an easing (taysir). This is an exception to the general principle due to the length of the Zuhr fard.
‘Taysir’ indicates a concession, not a contradiction of the principle.
3
Apply the principle to Jumu'ah
Jumu'ah fard is two rak'ahs due to the sermon, but originally it is four. Since the principle looks at the original number, the sunnah for Jumu'ah remains four rak'ahs according to qiyas.
This demonstrates that the principle considers the original obligation, not the actual shortened form.
4
Understand the condition of one taslim
The text rules that performing four rak'ahs with two taslimas (i.e., as two separate two-rak'ah prayers) does not count as the sunnah. The sunnah must be continuous with a single taslim.
This is derived directly from the principle: the sunnah must mirror the fard in form.
5
Summarize the rak'ah counts
Based on the passage: Fajr sunnah = 2; Zuhr sunnah = 2; Isha sunnah = 4; Jumu'ah sunnah = 4. These are all emphasized (mu'akkadah).
The recitation recommendation of ten verses per rak'ah also applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل وهنَّ مؤكدات. قال في «المجرد»: يقرأ في كل ركعة نحواً من عشر آيات. وكذا في الأربع بعد العشاء. وإن أداهنَّ بتسليمتين: لم يُعتَدَّ بهن من السنة؛ لأن النفل تبع للفرض، والفرض أربع، فكذا النفل ، ألا ترى أن الفجر لما كانت ركعتين: كان نفله مثله. وأما بعد الظهر : شرع ركعتين تيسيراً. والجمعة أصلها أربع، وبسبب الخطبة عادت إلى ركعتين، فكان النفل أربعاً، على أصل القياس.
Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers. They are emphasized. He said in Al-Mujarrad: One recites in each rak'ah about ten verses. Likewise in the four after Isha. And if one performs them with two taslimas, they are not counted from the sunnah; because the supererogatory is a follower of the obligatory, and the obligatory is four, so likewise the supererogatory. Do you not see that when Fajr was two rak'ahs, its supererogatory was like it. As for after Zuhr, two rak'ahs were legislated as an easing. Jumu'ah originally is four, but due to the sermon it returned to two rak'ahs, so the supererogatory became four, according to the original analogy.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on supererogatory prayers (nawafil) establishes the general principle that the number of rak'ahs in sunnah prayers follows the number in the obligatory prayer (fard), with some exceptions for ease. The text begins by stating that these nawafil are 'mu'akkadah' (emphasized). It then quotes Al-Mujarrad recommending recitation of about ten verses per rak'ah, applicable also to the four rak'ahs after Isha. A key rule is introduced: if one performs these four rak'ahs with two taslimas (i.e., two sets of two rak'ahs), they are not counted as the sunnah; because the supererogatory (nafl) follows the obligatory (fard), and the fard is four rak'ahs, so the sunnah must also be four continuous rak'ahs. The analogy (qiyas) with Fajr is given: Fajr fard is two, so its sunnah is two. For Zuhr, two rak'ahs were legislated as an easing due to the length of the fard. For Jumu'ah, the fard is originally four but shortened to two due to the sermon, so the sunnah remains four according to the original qiyas. This passage is foundational for understanding the Hanafi classification of sunnah prayers and their rak'ah counts.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer, in this context referring to the regular sunnah prayers (sunan rawatib).
مؤكد (mu'akkad): Emphasized; indicating that these sunnah prayers are strongly recommended and regularly performed by the Prophet.
تسليمة (taslimah): The salutation ending prayer; here used to refer to a set of two rak'ahs concluded with one taslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Because two taslimas are only allowed for the witr prayer.
D) Because the recitation would be too short.

Key Takeaway
The number of rak'ahs for emphasized sunnah prayers is determined by the obligatory prayer they accompany, with the exception of Zuhr (eased to 2) and Jumu'ah (returned to original 4).

Making up the Missed First Sunnah of Zuhr (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada of missed first sunnah of Zuhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on qada of the missed first sunnah of Zuhr and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Missed sunnah after fard qada: order and intention differ among Hanafi imams.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: a person misses the four-rak'ah first sunnah of Zuhr because they fear losing the congregational fard. The text presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on how to make up this missed sunnah—whether before or after the two rak'ahs after Zuhr, and whether intention of qada is required. Understanding these positions is key for proper practice and shows how later Hanafi authorities weighed differing views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Note the condition: the first sunnah of Zuhr is missed specifically due to fear of missing the congregation. This triggers the discussion on qada.
2
List the positions of the three imams
Abu Hanifa: no intention of qada; it becomes a fresh voluntary (tatthawwu' mubtada'). Abu Yusuf: pray the two rak'ahs after Zuhr first, then the four with intention of qada. Muhammad: pray the four (qada) before the two rak'ahs after Zuhr.
The source also mentions differences in transmission from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
3
Understand the key legal terms
Qada' (making up a missed prayer), tatthawwu' mubtada' (fresh voluntary without need for qada intention), sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). These terms define the nature of the prayer.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is the order: if one follows Muhammad, the missed four are prayed before the two after Zuhr; if Abu Yusuf, after; if Abu Hanifa, no specific order as it is a fresh voluntary that can be offered anytime.
This affects the sequence of supererogatory prayers around the fard.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
According to Al-Haqa'iq, the relied-upon fatwa is Muhammad's view: the four rak'ahs should be made up before the two after Zuhr.
This is based on the principle that a missed sunnah should be given priority, analogous to faraid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن ترك سنة الظهر الأولى خشية فوت الجماعة: فالصحيح أنه يقضيها بعد الفرض. ويقضيها قبل الركعتين عند محمد. وعند أبي يوسف: يقدم الركعتين على الأربع، وينوي القضاء عند أبي يوسف. وفي «النوادر»: يبدأ بالركعتين عندهما، وقال محمد: بالأربع، ثم ينوي القضاء عندهما. وعند أبي حنيفة: لا ينوي القضاء، ويكون تطوعاً مبتدأ، فلا يفتقر إلى نية القضاء. وفي «الحقائق»: يقدم الركعتين عندهما، وقال محمد: الأربع، وعليه الفتوى. وفي «المنظومة»: في مقالة أبي يوسف على خلاف مقالات محمد: والسنة الأولى من الظهر إذا فاتت فقبل شفعها: لها القضا أي قبل الركعتين الأخريين. - وفي «المصفى»: اختلفوا في قضاء الأربع: هل هو نفل مبتدأ، أو سنة؟ فعلى قول من يقول: نفل مبتدأ: يقضيها بعد الركعتين، وعلى قول من يقول إنها سنة: يقضيها قبل الركعتين؛ لأن كل واحدة منهما سنة، إلا أن إحداهما فائتة، فيبدأ بالفائتة، كما في الفرائض.
If one leaves the first sunnah of Zuhr for fear of missing the congregation, then the correct view is that he makes it up after the fard. According to Muhammad, he makes it up before the two rak'ahs. According to Abu Yusuf, he gives precedence to the two rak'ahs over the four, and intends qada according to Abu Yusuf. In Al-Nawadir: with them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he begins with the two rak'ahs, and Muhammad said: with the four, then he intends qada with them. According to Abu Hanifa: he does not intend qada, and it becomes a fresh voluntary (tatthawwu'), so he does not require the intention of qada. In Al-Haqa'iq: with them he gives precedence to the two rak'ahs, and Muhammad said: the four, and upon it is the fatwa. In Al-Manzuma: in the statement of Abu Yusuf contrary to the statements of Muhammad: the first sunnah of zuhr when missed is made up before its 'shaf' (pair), i.e. before the last two rak'ahs. And in Al-Masfa: they differed concerning the qada of the four: is it a fresh voluntary (nafl mubtada') or a sunnah? According to the one who says fresh voluntary: he makes it up after the two rak'ahs; and according to the one who says it is a sunnah: he makes it up before the two rak'ahs; because each of them is a sunnah, except that one of them is missed, so he begins with the missed one, as in the obligatory prayers.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific situation: a person misses the first sunnah of Zuhr (the four rak'ahs before the fard) because they fear losing the congregational prayer. The text presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on how to make up (qada) this missed sunnah. The relied-upon (sahih) position is that the qada is performed after the fard (the two rak'ahs after Zuhr). However, Imam Muhammad holds that one should make up the missed four before the two after Zuhr. Abu Yusuf says one should perform the two after Zuhr first, then the four with intention of qada. The Nawadir reports that both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree that one begins with the two, but Muhammad says to begin with the four (this may be a contradiction). Abu Hanifa's unique view is that one should not intend qada at all; instead, the prayer becomes a fresh voluntary (tatthawwu'), so no specific intention is needed. Later texts like Al-Haqa'iq give fatwa on Muhammad's view (four first). The Al-Masfa provides a further distinction: the four rak'ahs (the missed first sunnah) could be considered either a fresh nafl or a sunnah. If considered nafl, qada is after the two; if sunnah, qada is before the two, analogizing to making up missed fard prayers where the missed one is given priority. This shows the complexity of Hanafi legal methodology where multiple positions within the school are preserved and weighed.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed prayer after its prescribed time.
تطوع مبتدأ (tatthawwu' mubtada'): A fresh voluntary prayer that is not a make-up of a missed sunnah.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah prayer that the Prophet regularly performed and encouraged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) After the two rak'ahs after Zuhr.
B) Before the two rak'ahs after Zuhr.
C) With intention of qada after the fard.
D) Without any intention as a fresh voluntary.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that the missed first sunnah of Zuhr should be made up before the two rak'ahs after the fard, following Imam Muhammad's position.

Sunnah After Zuhr and Before Asr: Levels of Emphasis
Rules for sunnah after Zuhr and before Asr with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the two rak'ahs after Zuhr and the four before Asr, and distinguish between sunnah mu'akkadah and mustahabb with the supporting proof.

Core Idea
Two rak'ahs after Zuhr are emphasized sunnah; four before Asr are recommended (mustahabb) with an option for two.

This lesson clarifies two voluntary prayers closely tied to the obligatory Zuhr and Asr. You will learn how the Hanafi school classifies each, based on the degree of prophetic consistency, and see the hadith evidence for the prayer before Asr. Understanding these levels helps you prioritize your sunnah acts correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prayers
The passage refers to two rak'ahs after Zuhr and four rak'ahs before Asr (with an option to pray two).
These are rawatib (associated) sunnah prayers.
2
Classify the ruling for each
The two after Zuhr are 'mu'akkadah' (emphasized); the four before Asr are 'mustahabb' (recommended) as explicitly stated: 'wa hunna mustahabbaat'.
Mu'akkadah is a higher level than mustahabb.
3
Examine the proof for before Asr
The hadith: 'Whoever prays four before Asr, the Fire will not touch him' is cited to show the virtue of this prayer.
The reward indicates desirability, not obligation.
4
Distinguish the practical implications
Missing an emphasized sunnah is makruh tanzihan; missing a mustahabb is not censured.
This affects how one should view the two prayers.

The text then provides a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) stating that whoever prays four rak'ahs before Asr will not be touched by the Fire. This hadith is cited as evidence for the virtue of this prayer. The commentary here is from the sharh (explanation) of the Mukhtasar al-Quduri, where the author is explaining the text of the matn. The ruling for after Zuhr is straightforward: two emphasized rak'ahs. For before Asr, the ruling is more flexible: four is recommended, but two is also permissible, and the hadith encourages four.

Making Up the Missed Sunnah of Dhuhr: New Nafl or Missed Sunnah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada of missed sunnah of Dhuhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions on qada of the missed Dhuhr sunnah and explain which is mufta bihi and why.

Core Idea
A missed sunnah mu'akkadah is made up as a sunnah, not as a new nafl, and is prayed before the current sunnah.

The Hanafi school is unanimous that the two rak'ahs after Dhuhr are sunnah mu'akkadah. But if one misses the four rak'ahs before Dhuhr, a dispute arises: should they be made up before or after the two rak'ahs? This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi debate and the principle that resolves it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sets of sunnah rak'ahs for Dhuhr
Recognize that the Dhuhr prayer has a sunnah of four rak'ahs before and two rak'ahs after. Both are sunnah mu'akkadah.
The matn mentions only the two after, but the dispute concerns the four before.
2
Understand the question
If the four rak'ahs before Dhuhr are missed, when should they be performed? The answer depends on whether the qada is treated as a new nafl or as a missed sunnah.
3
State the two positions
Position 1: The missed four are a new nafl (nafl mubtada') and can be performed any time, so they are prayed after the two rak'ahs after Dhuhr. Position 2: The missed four are a sunnah that must be made up as a sunnah, so they are prayed before the two rak'ahs.
The text cites al-Mustafa for this classification.
4
Analyze the reasoning
The principle: each set (the four before and the two after) is a sunnah, but one is missed. Analogy to obligatory prayers: the missed one is prioritized. Hence, one begins with the missed sunnah.
The commentary states: 'because each of them is a sunnah, except that one of them is missed, so he begins with the missed one, as in the obligatory prayers.'
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text leans towards praying before the two rak'ahs, as it is a sunnah. The fatwa is on Muhammad's view that the four are a sunnah.
There is ambiguity in the source: 'وعليه الفتوى سنة؟' likely means the fatwa is upon it (the four) being a sunnah.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the qada (making up) of the missed sunnah of Dhuhr. The matn states that there are two rak'ahs after Dhuhr. The commentator then reports a disagreement on whether the four rak'ahs before Dhuhr (the sunnah) if missed should be made up as a new nafl or as a missed sunnah. Abu Hanifa and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ: according to al-Haqa'iq, the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) present the two rak'ahs first, while Muhammad says four. The fatwa is on Muhammad's view? The text is ambiguous. In al-Manzoomah, Abu Yusuf's statement is contrary to Muhammad's. The first sunnah of Dhuhr, if missed, should be made up before the two rak'ahs after. In al-Mustafa, they differ: if it is a new nafl, make it up after; if it is a sunnah, make it up before. The preferred view is that it is a sunnah, so it should be made up before the two rak'ahs, following the principle of starting with the missed one, analogous to obligatory prayers.

Key Terms
نفل مبتدأ (nafl mubtada'): A supererogatory prayer that is initiated anew, not considered a makeup of a missed sunnah.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah, regularly performed by the Prophet (peace be upon him), and its qada is recommended.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed prayer after its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if one misses the four rak'ahs before Dhuhr, when should they be made up?
A) After the two rak'ahs of Dhuhr sunnah, as a new nafl.
B) Before the two rak'ahs of Dhuhr sunnah, as a missed sunnah.
C) They are not made up at all.
D) After 'Asr prayer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a missed sunnah mu'akkadah is made up as a sunnah and performed before the current related sunnah, by analogy to the prioritization of obligatory prayers.

Sunnah of 'Isha: Four Before and Four After, with Option
Ruling on recommended prayers before and after 'Isha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah prayers before and after 'Isha and apply the condition that determines when the worshiper may choose between two and four rak'ahs after 'Isha.

Core Idea
Four before 'Isha are recommended; after, choose two or four, but if you delay 'Isha, pray four to compensate.

This lesson explains the recommended (mustahabb) prayers associated with the 'Isha prayer. The Hanafi school teaches that praying four rak'ahs before 'Isha is meritorious, and after 'Isha the worshiper may choose between two and four. However, this choice is conditional: if one prays 'Isha at its earliest preferred time, both options are valid; if one delays 'Isha, then four are required to make up for the lateness. Understanding this time-based ruling helps you maximise reward and practice the sunnah correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah prayers for 'Isha
First, identify that the passage discusses two sets of sunnah prayers: four before 'Isha and the option of two or four after 'Isha.
The four before are always recommended.
2
State the ruling for the four before 'Isha
The text says 'they are recommended (mustahabbat)'. So the ruling is sunnah mustahabbah – performing them brings reward, omitting them is not sinful.
No condition attaches to these four.
3
Examine the option after 'Isha
After 'Isha, one may pray two or four. The phrase 'wa in shaa rakaʿtayn' indicates permissibility. But this is not unrestricted.
The default is that both are valid.
4
Apply the time condition
The choice applies only when 'Isha is prayed in its mustahabb time (early night). If 'Isha is delayed beyond that time, the option is removed: one must pray all four to compensate for the deficiency.
This shows the Hanafi principle that sunnah can compensate for delay in obligatory prayers.
5
Note the practical outcome
If you pray 'Isha late, the recommended practice becomes four after, not two. This is to increase reward and make up for the less preferable timing.
The condition is based on the quality of time; the later you pray, the more sunnah you should add.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* قوله : (وأربعاً قبل العشاء)، وهنَّ مستحبات.
* قوله : (وأربعاً بعدها، وإن شاء ركعتين).
قيل : إن هذا التخيير إذا صلى العشاء في الوقت المستحب، أما إذا صلاها في غير الوقت المستحب: فإنه يؤدي الأربع كلها؛ جبراً لذلك النقص، ولا يتخير.
His statement: (And four before 'Isha), and they are recommended. His statement: (And four after it, and if he wishes, two). It is said: This choice is when he prays 'Isha in the preferred time, but if he prays it outside the preferred time, then he performs all four, compensating for that deficiency, and does not choose.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage presents the sunnah prayers associated with 'Isha. Four rak'ahs before 'Isha are recommended (mustahabbat). After 'Isha, one may pray four or two, but with a condition: if one prays 'Isha in its preferred time (i.e., early), then the choice between four and two is permissible. However, if one delays 'Isha beyond the preferred time, then one should pray all four to compensate for the delay. This shows the Hanafi consideration of time and compensation in sunnah prayers.

Key Terms
وقت مستحب (waqt mustahabb): The preferred time for 'Isha prayer, which is early in the night (before one-third of the night passes).
مستحبات (mustahabbat): Recommended acts; performing them brings reward, omitting them does not incur sin.
جبراً (jabran): Compensation; making up for a deficiency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) When one is tired.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on post-'Isha sunnah is time-sensitive: choose two or four if you pray 'Isha early, but pray four if you delay to compensate.

Sunnah of Jumu'ah: Four Before and Four After with Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on number of sunnah rak'ahs after Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding the number of sunnah rak'ahs after Jumu'ah and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Four before and four after Jumu'ah is the established Hanafi position, but Abu Yusuf held six after.

You already know that sunnah prayers accompany the obligatory Jumu'ah. But did you know that even the great Hanafi imams disagreed on the exact number? This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute about how many sunnah rak'ahs to pray after Jumu'ah. Understanding this shows you how the madhhab evolved and why you might see different practices in different Hanafi communities today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base position
The text first states a position: four rak'ahs before Jumu'ah and four after it. It attributes this to 'the two' (عندهما). In this context, 'the two' most likely refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, as the following sentence contrasts Abu Yusuf's view.
The phrase 'the two' in Hanafi texts usually refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but here it seems to refer to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad since Abu Yusuf is mentioned separately.
2
Recognize Abu Yusuf's variant
Immediately after, Abu Yusuf is reported to have said: four before Jumu'ah and six after it. This reveals a clear difference: Abu Yusuf adds two extra rak'ahs after Jumu'ah.
The number before Jumu'ah is agreed upon; the dispute is only about the after rak'ahs.
3
Examine Muhammad's conflicting transmissions
The text then notes two different reports about Muhammad's position. In al-Karkhi, Muhammad agrees with Abu Yusuf (six after). In al-Manzoomah, he agrees with Abu Hanifa (four after). This shows that Muhammad's own reported view is not uniform across sources.
This kind of variance in transmission is common in early fiqh; later scholars weighed the reliability of each riwayah.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence (thamarah) is the number of rak'ahs a Hanafi follower prays after Jumu'ah. Those who follow the 'two' (Abu Hanifa and the version of Muhammad with him) will pray four; those who follow Abu Yusuf (and the other version of Muhammad) will pray six.
The thamarah is directly observable in mosque practice.
5
Establish the mufta bihi
Although the text does not explicitly give a tarjih, the Hanafi school generally adopts the view of four before and four after as the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. This is supported by the fact that it is attributed to 'the two' and is the more commonly transmitted view.
In later Hanafi works, four after Jumu'ah is the standard fatwa position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأربعاً قبل الجمعة وأربعاً بعدها، وهذا عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف: أربعاً قبلها، وستاً بعدها.
وفي الكرخي: محمد مع أبي يوسف.
وفي المنظومة : مع أبي حنيفة.
And four before Jumu'ah and four after it, and this is according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?), and Abu Yusuf said: four before it and six after it. In al-Karkhi: Muhammad is with Abu Yusuf. In al-Manzoomah: (he is) with Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sunnah prayers of Jumu'ah. The base position is four rak'ahs before and four after, attributed to 'the two' (possibly Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, or Abu Hanifa and one other). However, Abu Yusuf reports a variant: four before and six after. In al-Karkhi, Muhammad agrees with Abu Yusuf, while in al-Manzoomah, Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa. The text does not provide a clear tarjih, showing that this was a debated issue. The Hanafi school generally adopts the view of four before and four after as the mufta bihi.

Key Terms
عندهما (indahuma): According to the two (usually Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, but here likely Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Two Rak'ahs After Maghrib: Sunnah Mu'akkadah
States ruling and recommendation for two rak'ahs after Maghrib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the two rak'ahs after Maghrib as sunnah mu'akkadah and identify the recommended recitation practice.

Core Idea
Two rak'ahs after Maghrib are an emphasized sunnah; lengthening recitation with specific surahs is recommended.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar establishes the ruling for the two rak'ahs prayed after the Maghrib fard. It not only classifies them as sunnah mu'akkadah but also provides a specific recommendation from the Prophet's practice: to recite Surah as-Sajdah and Surah al-Mulk. Understanding this will help you appreciate the gradation of sunnah prayers and how to follow the Prophetic model.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Focus on the phrase 'ركعتين بعد المغرب وهما مؤكدتان'. The text explicitly states the act (two rak'ahs after Maghrib) and its ruling (mu'akkadatān = emphasized sunnah).
In Hanafi fiqh, sunnah mu'akkadah has a higher rank than nafl, regularly performed by the Prophet ﷺ.
2
Distinguish the recommendation
The word 'يستحب' (yustaḥabbu) introduces a recommended action: lengthening the recitation. This is not obligatory but a virtue.
The recommendation is tied to a specific practice of the Prophet.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The text cites a narration (rawā) that the Prophet ﷺ used to recite Surah 32 in the first rak'ah and Surah 67 in the second. This proof establishes the recommendation.
The hadith is a single narration (khabar wāḥid), hence the ruling is zannī, but its regular practice elevates the sunnah to mu'akkadah.
4
Apply the ruling to practice
If a person prays these two rak'ahs without long recitation or with different surahs, the prayer is still valid and considered sunnah, but they miss out on the recommended perfection.
The mu'akkadah status is achieved by the act itself; the recitation quality is an additional sunnah.

Sunnah Prayers Before and After Isha
Ruling on sunnah before and after Isha with conditional choice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sunnah prayers before and after Isha and identify the condition that affects the option between two and four rak'ahs after Isha.

Core Idea
The sunnah after Isha is four rak'ahs, but you may pray two if you pray Isha early; if delayed, you must pray all four to compensate.

This lesson examines the sunnah prayers associated with the Isha prayer as recorded in the matn of al-Quduri and its commentary. The text gives a straightforward ruling with an important nuance: the option to reduce to two rak'ahs depends on timing. Understanding this condition ensures the sunnah is performed correctly according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
Locate the two acts mentioned: sunnah prayers before Isha (four rak'ahs) and sunnah prayers after Isha (four rak'ahs, with option of two).
2
Determine the hukm level
For the four before Isha, the commentary states they are mustahabb (recommended, not emphasized). For after Isha, the default is four, but two may be substituted conditionally.
Mustahabb is weaker than sunnah mu'akkadah.
3
Understand the condition for the option
The commentator specifies that the choice between two and four applies only when Isha is prayed in its most virtuous time (early part of the night).
If Isha is delayed, no choice exists.
4
Note the consequence of praying Isha outside the preferred time
If Isha is performed in the non-preferred time (i.e., delayed), the worshipper must perform all four rak'ahs to compensate for the deficiency of delay.
This is a unique Hanafi condition.
5
Recognize the basis
The commentary cites a report (or principle) that the additional two rak'ahs act as compensation for the delay, so when the prayer is early, the compensation is optional.
The logic is jabar (compensation).

Sunnah Prayers for Jumu'ah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Number After
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sunnah rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the number of sunnah rak'ahs after Jumu'ah and identify the two transmissions from Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
The number of sunnah rak'ahs after Jumu'ah varies among Hanafi imams: four according to Abu Hanifa, six according to Abu Yusuf.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah records a disagreement among the early Hanafi masters on how many sunnah rak'ahs should be prayed after Jumu'ah. While the base text of al-Quduri states four before and four after, Abu Yusuf holds for six after. Additionally, there are conflicting reports about the final position of Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this dispute is important because it shows how the Hanafi school accommodates internal differences and how the preferred opinion is determined.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Look at the matn (base text): 'Four before Jumu'ah and four after it.' This is the standard position from al-Quduri.
2
Note the attribution
The phrase 'وهذا عندهما' attributes this position to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (according to one transmission).
'عندهما' here refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, not the two students.
3
Recognize Abu Yusuf's opposition
Abu Yusuf says: four before and six after. The six are prayed as four then two additional rak'ahs.
4
Resolve the transmission conflict about Muhammad
Al-Karkhi reports Muhammad agrees with Abu Yusuf; al-Manzoomah reports Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa. This shows two different transmissions.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text does not explicitly tarjih, but the reliance on the matn and the phrase 'وهذا عندهما' suggests the position of four after is the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأربعاً قبل الجمعة وأربعاً بعدها، وهذا عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف: أربعاً قبلها، وستاً بعدها. وفي الكرخي: محمد مع أبي يوسف. وفي المنظومة: مع أبي حنيفة. ثم عند أبي يوسف: يصلي أربعاً، ثم اثنتين.
And four rak'ahs before Jumu'ah and four after it, and this is according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). And Abu Yusuf said: four before it, and six after it. And in al-Karkhi: Muhammad is with Abu Yusuf. And in al-Manzoomah: (Muhammad is) with Abu Hanifa. Then according to Abu Yusuf: he prays four, then two.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sunnah prayers of Jumu'ah. The base statement (al-Quduri) says four before and four after, which is attributed to 'them' (presumably Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Abu Yusuf disagrees: he says four before but six after. Then there are two transmissions about Muhammad's final position: in al-Karkhi's work, Muhammad agrees with Abu Yusuf; in al-Manzoomah (a versified text by al-Nasafi), Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa. The 'then' clause explains that Abu Yusuf's six are prayed as four followed by two. This is a complete dispute with multiple positions. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is typically the one attributed to Abu Hanifa (four after) as mentioned in al-Manzoomah, but the text does not explicitly tarjih.

Key Terms
عندهما ('indahuma): According to them (dual), referring to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
الكرخي (al-Karkhi): Reference to a work by the Hanafi scholar al-Karkhi (d. 340 AH).
المنظومة (al-Manzoomah): A versified text on Hanafi fiqh by al-Nasafi (d. 537 AH).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, how many rak'ahs are to be prayed after Jumu'ah?
A) Four rak'ahs.
B) Six rak'ahs.
C) Two rak'ahs.
D) Eight rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
The number of sunnah rak'ahs after Jumu'ah is disputed within the Hanafi school: four (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) versus six (Abu Yusuf), with the relied-upon position being four.

Ranking the Strongest Sunnah Prayers
Provides ranking of sunnah prayers by virtue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two classical Hanafi rankings of sunnah prayers and identify the preferred (al-asahh) view.

Core Idea
The two rak'ahs of Fajr are the strongest sunnah; after that, there is disagreement.

Not all sunnah prayers are equal in virtue. The Hanafi school has discussed which are the most strongly recommended (aqwa al-sunan). This lesson presents two opinions: one by al-Halwani giving a detailed ranking, and another by an unnamed scholar who simplifies it. Knowing this helps prioritize when time is limited – you'll always start with the strongest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ranking
Both opinions agree that the two rak'ahs of Fajr are the strongest sunnah. Understand that the ranking concerns relative virtue (fadilah), not obligation.
All listed prayers are sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Note the disagreement in sequence
Al-Halwani gives a long list: Fajr, Maghrib, after Dhuhr, after Isha, before Dhuhr, before Asr, before Isha. Another scholar says the correct view is that Fajr is strongest, then the four before and after Dhuhr and the two after Maghrib are equal in virtue.
The other scholar's view is introduced as 'al-asahh' (most correct).
3
Identify the preferred view
The passage explicitly says 'al-asahh an aqwaha...' indicating that the second ranking is the relied-upon position in the school.
This does not make the other ranking invalid; it shows the development of tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الحلواني أقوى السنن ركعتا الفجر، ثم ركعتا المغرب، ثم التي بعد الظهر، ثم التي بعد العشاء، ثم التي قبل الظهر، ثم التي قبل العصر، ثم التي قبل العشاء. وقال بعضهم: الأصح أن أقواها ركعتا الفجر، ثم الأربع التي قبل الظهر والتي بعد الظهر والتي بعد المغرب: سواء.
Al-Halwani said: The strongest of the sunnah prayers are the two rak'ahs of Fajr, then the two rak'ahs of Maghrib, then those after Dhuhr, then those after Isha, then those before Dhuhr, then those before Asr, then those before Isha. And some of them said: The most correct is that the strongest are the two rak'ahs of Fajr, then the four before Dhuhr, the four after Dhuhr, and the two after Maghrib are equal.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage presents two opinions on the relative virtue (strength) of various sunnah prayers. Al-Halwani gives a detailed ranking starting with the two rak'ahs of Fajr as the strongest, then Maghrib sunnah, then after Dhuhr, etc. Another unnamed scholar says the most correct view is that the Fajr sunnah is strongest, and then the four before Dhuhr, four after Dhuhr, and two after Maghrib are all equal. This is not a ruling on obligation but on preference (fadilah). The passage helps muftis and students understand which sunnah to prioritize if time is limited. The two rak'ahs of Fajr are universally agreed to be the strongest sunnah in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
أقوى السنن (aqwa al-sunan): The strongest/most emphasized of the sunnah prayers in terms of virtue and recommendation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The two rak'ahs of Fajr.
B) The four before Dhuhr.
C) The two after Maghrib.
D) The four after Isha.

Key Takeaway
The Fajr sunnah is the strongest sunnah prayer; after it, the four before and after Dhuhr and the Maghrib sunnah are equal in virtue according to the preferred Hanafi view.

The Wisdom Behind Sunnah Prayers: Compensation and Preemption
Answers a question about the wisdom behind sunnah before and after fard prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two wisdoms for sunnah prayers before and after fard prayers and apply the concept of jabr al-nuqsan to other acts of worship.

Core Idea
After-fard sunnah compensates; before-fard sunnah thwarts Satan by building obedience.

Why do we pray certain sunnah prayers before the fard and others after? This short passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira provides a beautiful wisdom: the after-prayer sunnah makes up for any shortcomings in the fard, while the before-prayer sunnah trains the soul to obey Allah even in non-obligatory acts, cutting off Satan's hope that we will neglect the fard. Let's explore this hikmah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Distinguish between sunnah before fard (qabliyyah) and sunnah after fard (ba'diyyah).
Common examples: before Dhuhr, after Maghrib.
2
Understand the wisdom for after-prayer sunnah
Jabr al-nuqsan: compensation for deficiency. The after-prayer sunnah fills any gaps in the fard.
This includes both unintentional mistakes and voluntary completions.
3
Understand the wisdom for before-prayer sunnah
Qat' al-tama' al-shaytan: cutting off Satan's hope. By performing voluntary prayers, the believer demonstrates obedience, making it harder for Satan to tempt them to skip the fard.
Satan argues: if they obey in non-obligatory, they will obey in obligatory.
4
Analyse the Satan quote
Read the quote: 'The one who does not obey me in leaving what was not written upon him, how will he obey me in leaving what was written upon him?' This shows the logic of Satan being discouraged.
5
Apply to specific prayers
For example, the sunnah after Maghrib compensates for any deficiency in Maghrib fard; the sunnah before Fajr (or before Dhuhr) preempts Satan by establishing obedience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل لك : لمَ تُشرع بعض النوافل قبل الفرض، وبعضها بعده؟ فالجواب: أن الذي بعد الفرض شرع لجبر النقصان، والذي قبله؛ قطعاً لطمع الشيطان، فإنه يقول: من لم يُطعني في ترك ما لم يكتب عليه: كيف يطيعني في ترك ما كتب عليه؟
If it is said to you: Why are some supererogatory prayers prescribed before the fard and some after it? The answer: That which is after the fard is prescribed to compensate for deficiency, and that which is before it is to cut off the hope of Satan, for he says: 'The one who does not obey me in leaving what was not written upon him, how will he obey me in leaving what was written upon him?'
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage provides a rational wisdom (hikmah) for the placement of sunnah prayers relative to the fard. The after-prayer sunnah (like after Maghrib and Isha) serve to make up for any shortcomings or omissions in the fard prayer. The before-prayer sunnah (like before Dhuhr and Fajr, though Fajr sunnah is before but actually considered before the fard, but here the emphasis is on prayers before the fard) are meant to thwart Satan by establishing a habit of obeying Allah even in non-obligatory acts, thus making it harder for Satan to tempt one to abandon the fard. The quote from Satan is explanatory: if a believer is diligent in supererogatory acts, he is less likely to neglect obligatory ones.

Key Terms
جبر النقصان (jabr al-nuqsan): Compensation for deficiency; the after-prayer sunnah makes up for any imperfections in the fard.
قطع طمع الشيطان (qat' tama' al-shaytan): Cutting off the hope of Satan; the before-prayer sunnah aims to thwart Satan by establishing obedience.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To increase reward.
B) To compensate for deficiencies in the fard.
C) To make prayer longer.
D) To annoy Satan directly.

Key Takeaway
Sunnah prayers after fard are for compensation, while those before are for preempting Satan.

Ruling on Imam and Ma'mum Praying Nafl in the Place of Fard
States ruling for imam and ma'mum regarding nafl in place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the imam and ma'mum regarding praying nafl in the place of fard, and explain the evidence and reasoning behind the distinction.

Core Idea
Imam should not pray nafl in his fard place; ma'mum may stay.

When the obligatory (fard) prayer is completed, the imam and followers often wish to offer supererogatory (nafl) prayers. This lesson clarifies the ruling on where they may pray those nafl rak'ahs, based on a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ and considerations of avoiding confusion in the mosque. The rule differs for the imam and the ma'mum, as we will see.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and subject
The act is praying nafl (supererogatory prayer) in the exact place where one has just prayed the fard. The subjects are the imam (leader) and the ma'mum (follower).
2
State the ruling for the imam
The passage states it is makruh (disliked) for the imam. Understand why: a latecomer might think the imam is still in the fard and follow him, causing confusion.
Makruh here is tanzihi, not tahrimi.
3
State the ruling for the ma'mum
It is not disliked for the ma'mum. In fact, a narration from al-Karkhi says it is even recommended, to help fill gaps in the rows.
The ma'mum may also move but is not required to.
4
Analyze the evidence
The hadith 'Is one of you unable, when he prays, to step forward or backward?' implies it is good to move after fard, but does not forbid staying. The imam's case is distinguished by the risk of misleading others.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and Ibn Majah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره للإمام أن يتنفل في مكانه الذي صلى فيه الفرضَ. ولا يكره للمأموم ذلك ؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «أيعجز أحدكم إذا صلى أن يتقدم أو يتأخر » (١). ولأنه إذا تنفل في مكانه : ظن الداخل أنه في الفرض، فيقتدي به. وروي أيضاً : أن ذلك يستحب للمأموم؛ حتى تتشوش الصفوف. كذا في الكرخي».
And it is disliked for the imam to perform supererogatory prayer in the place where he prayed the fard. And it is not disliked for the ma'mum that, because of his saying ﷺ: 'Is one of you unable, when he prays, to step forward or backward?' And because if he prays nafl in his place, the one entering will think he is still in the fard and follow him. And it is also narrated that it is recommended for the ma'mum so that the rows become disordered. Thus in al-Karkhi.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling with two proofs. For the imam: it is makruh (disliked) to pray a supererogatory prayer in the exact spot where he led the fard prayer. The reason given is that someone entering the mosque late might see him and incorrectly think he is still in the fard prayer and follow him, causing confusion. For the ma'mum (follower): it is not disliked, based on a hadith that encourages changing position after prayer, even just stepping forward or back. Additionally, a narration from al-Karkhi states that it is even recommended for the ma'mum to stay in place because the disorder in rows (presumably filling gaps) is considered good. Thus, the ruling differs between imam and ma'mum.

Key Terms
مأموم (ma'mum): The person praying behind the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it is makruh.
B) No, it is not disliked.
C) It is haram.
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
The imam should avoid praying nafl in his fard place to prevent confusion; the ma'mum may do so without dislike.

Ranking of Sunan Rawatib and Wisdom of Before/After Placement
Describes the ranking of sunan rawatib and explains wisdom of before/after placement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ranking of sunan rawatib according to the more correct Hanafi view and explain the wisdom behind their placement before or after the fard prayers.

Core Idea
The two rak'ahs of Fajr are the strongest sunnah; after-prayers compensate for deficiencies, before-prayers cut off Satan's hope.

Not all supererogatory prayers carry the same weight. In this passage, the commentator presents and weighs different Hanafi opinions on the ranking of the regular sunnah prayers (rawatib). He also provides a profound explanation for why some sunnah are offered before the obligatory prayer and some after. Understanding this hierarchy helps you prioritize when time is limited and deepens your appreciation of the wisdom behind the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the different opinions on ranking
Read the text and locate the two views: one by Al-Halwani giving a detailed order, and another by 'some scholars' presenting a simpler, more equal ranking. Note which one is marked as 'asahh' (most correct).
The first opinion is more granular; the second is more general.
2
Determine the more correct (asahh) ranking
The text states that the most correct view is: Fajr sunnah is strongest, then the four rak'ahs before Zuhr, the two after Zuhr, and the two after Maghrib are equal in strength. This is the relied-upon position.
This ranking affects prioritization when a person cannot pray all sunan.
3
Understand the wisdom behind before/after placement
The commentator explains that after-prayers (ba'diyyah) are prescribed to compensate for any deficiencies in the obligatory prayer. Before-prayers (qabliyyah) are prescribed to cut off Satan's hope that one will leave even voluntary acts, thus making it harder for him to tempt one to leave the obligatory.
This is a rational (ma'qul) explanation based on the psychology of obedience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم عند أبي يوسف: يصلي أربعاً، ثم اثنتين. قال الحلواني أقوى السنن ركعتا الفجر، ثم ركعتا المغرب، ثم التي بعد الظهر، ثم التي بعد العشاء، ثم التي قبل الظهر، ثم التي قبل العصر، ثم التي قبل العشاء. وقال بعضهم: الأصح أن أقواها ركعتا الفجر، ثم الأربع التي قبل الظهر، والتي بعد الظهر والتي بعد المغرب: سواء. فإن قيل لك : لمَ تُشرع بعض النوافل قبل الفرض، وبعضها بعده؟ فالجواب: أن الذي بعد الفرض شرع لجبر النقصان، والذي قبله؛ قطعاً لطمع الشيطان، فإنه يقول: من لم يُطعني في ترك ما لم يكتب عليه: كيف يطيعني في ترك ما كتب عليه؟
Then according to Abu Yusuf: He prays four, then two. Al-Halwani said: The strongest of the sunnahs are the two rak'ahs of Fajr, then the two rak'ahs of Maghrib, then those after Zuhr, then those after 'Isha', then those before Zuhr, then those before 'Asr, then those before 'Isha'. And some said: The most correct is that the strongest are the two rak'ahs of Fajr, then the four before Zuhr, and those after Zuhr and those after Maghrib are equal. If it is said to you: Why are some supererogatory prayers prescribed before the obligatory and some after? The answer: That which is after the obligatory is prescribed to compensate for deficiencies, and that which is before it is prescribed to cut off the hope of Satan, for he says: 'Whoever does not obey me in leaving what was not prescribed upon him, how can he obey me in leaving what was prescribed upon him?'
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage from the commentary discusses the relative strength (quwwa) of the sunan rawatib (regular supererogatory prayers associated with the obligatory prayers). The author first reports the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the order of praying the sunnah prayers when entering the mosque: he prays four rak'ahs (probably the tahiyyat al-masjid and then the sunnah), then two. Then he quotes Al-Halwani's ranking: the strongest sunnah is the two rak'ahs of Fajr, followed by the two rak'ahs of Maghrib, then the sunnah after Zuhr, then after 'Isha', then before Zuhr, then before 'Asr, then before 'Isha'. However, another group of scholars holds the more correct view: the two rak'ahs of Fajr are strongest, and then the four before Zuhr, the two after Zuhr, and the two after Maghrib are all equal in strength. The passage then answers an objection: why are some sunnahs prescribed before the fard and some after? The explanation is that after-prayers compensate for any deficiencies in the fard (since the fard may have incompleteness), while before-prayers are meant to cut off Satan's hope that a person will neglect even voluntary acts, making it less likely they will neglect obligatory ones. This is a rational explanation based on the psychology of obedience and Satan's whisperings.

Key Terms
النوافل (an-nawāfil): Supererogatory prayers, both regular (rawatib) and non-regular.
السنن (as-sunan): Here refers to the regular sunnah prayers (rawatib) associated with the obligatory prayers.
الفرض (al-fard): Obligatory prayer, as in the five daily prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The two after Maghrib are strongest.
C) The four before Zuhr are strongest.
D) All sunan rawatib are equal.

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs of Fajr are the strongest sunnah; after-prayers compensate for deficiencies in the fard, while before-prayers block Satan's hope.

Dislike for Imam to Pray Supererogatory in His Place After Fard
Ruling on imam's supererogatory prayer in his place after fard, with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the imam performing nafl prayer in the place of fard and explain the proof and rationale.

Core Idea
It is makruh for the imam to pray nafl in his place; the ma'mum is not disliked.

This lesson addresses a specific adab of congregational prayer: what the imam should do after the fard. The Hanafi school holds that it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) for the imam to remain in his spot to pray supererogatory. This is based on a hadith and a practical wisdom to avoid confusion for latecomers. Followers, however, are not subject to this dislike and may even be encouraged to pray in the same spot.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the hukm is. The act is the imam praying nafl in the exact place where he performed the fard. The ruling is makruh (disliked), specifically makruh tanzihi.
The dislike is not severe; it is better to avoid but not sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof the author cites. Two proofs: (1) a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ encouraging moving forward or backward after the prayer, (2) a rational reason: to avoid a latecomer mistakenly joining the nafl thinking it is fard.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and Sunan Ibn Majah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. The hadith implies that staying in place is contrary to the sunnah; moving is better, so staying is disliked.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Observe the distinction between imam and ma'mum. The text states it is not disliked for the ma'mum, and some reports even recommend it for them. This is a known intra-Hanafi variation.
The ma'mum's action causes the rows to become disordered, which is a sign that the fard is over.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Determine the relied-upon position. The dislike for the imam is established; the recommendation for the ma'mum is a weaker view. The primary ruling is that the imam should move.
This is the position of the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره للإمام أن يتنفل في مكانه الذي صلى فيه الفرضَ. ولا يكره للمأموم ذلك ؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «أيعجز أحدكم إذا صلى أن يتقدم أو يتأخر ». ولأنه إذا تنفل في مكانه : ظن الداخل أنه في الفرض، فيقتدي به. وروي أيضاً : أن ذلك يستحب للمأموم؛ حتى تتشوش الصفوف. كذا في الكرخي».
It is disliked for the imam to pray supererogatory in his place where he prayed the obligatory prayer. It is not disliked for the follower to do that, because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Is any of you unable, when he prays, to move forward or backward?' And because if he prays supererogatory in his place, the one entering may think he is still in the obligatory prayer and follow him. It is also narrated that it is recommended for the follower to do so, so that the rows become disturbed. As in al-Karkhi.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage states a ruling regarding the place of supererogatory prayer after the obligatory. It is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) for the imam to pray any supererogatory (nafl) prayers in the same spot where he performed the fard prayer. However, this dislike does not apply to the ma'mum (follower). The proof is twofold: first, a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ encouraging moving a little after the fard prayer before praying nafl; second, a rational reason: if the imam prays in the same place, a latecomer entering the mosque might think the imam is still engaged in the fard and thus join him in what is actually a nafl prayer, which would be problematic. Additionally, it is reported that it is actually mustahabb (recommended) for the ma'mum to pray nafl in the same spot, as this causes the rows to be in disarray (which is desirable after fard to indicate the prayer is over). This ruling is confirmed in al-Karkhi's work.

Key Terms
يكره (yukrahu): It is disliked (makruh tanzihi), meaning not sinful but better to avoid.
الإمام (al-imām): The prayer leader who leads the congregational prayer.
المأموم (al-ma'mūm): The follower who prays behind the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The ma'mum only.
C) Both imam and ma'mum.
D) Neither.

Key Takeaway
The imam should avoid praying nafl in the same spot as fard to prevent confusion, reflecting the adab of congregation.

Number of Rak'ahs for Night and Day Supererogatory Prayers
Specifies minimum rak'ahs for night and day nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum rak'ahs for night supererogatory prayer according to Abu Hanifa, and explain the ruling for day supererogatory prayers regarding the maximum number per taslima.

Core Idea
Night supererogatory prayer requires a minimum of eight rak'ahs; day supererogatory prayer is limited to two or four rak'ahs per taslima.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira addresses a common question: how many rak'ahs should one pray for the night supererogatory (tahajjud) and what is the rule for day supererogatory prayers? The text gives specific numbers based on the Hanafi school, supported by Quranic and prophetic evidence. Understanding these limits is important for proper practice and avoiding disliked acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage distinguishes between night supererogatory (nāfilat al-layl) and day supererogatory (nāfilat al-nahār) prayers. Recognize that different rules apply.
2
State the minimum for night prayer
According to Abu Hanifa, the minimum appropriate number is eight rak'ahs. Note that this is a recommendation (sunnah muakkadah), not an obligation.
The text says 'the minimum that is appropriate' – it is not the only permissible amount.
3
State the ruling for day supererogatory
For day nafl, one may pray two or four rak'ahs with one taslima. Exceeding four rak'ahs in one taslima is disliked (makruh tanzihi).
This applies to general nafl during the day, not to specific sunan like Zuhr sunnah.
4
Locate the evidence
The author supports the virtue of night prayer with Quran 32:16-17 and a hadith about ease on Judgment Day. These prove the reward, while the specific number of eight is from the practice of the school.
The dalil does not directly mandate eight; it establishes virtue.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is do not restrict day nafl to four per taslima and may allow any number. The Hanafi ruling is based on the principle of tawfīr (abundance) for night and avoiding exaggeration for day.
The ikhtilaf is a legitimate difference; each school has its proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن صلى بالليل : صلى ثمان ركعات . ونوافل النهار إن شاء صلَّى ركعتين بتسليمة واحدة، وإن شاء أربعاً، وتكره الزيادة على ذلك . وأما نافلة الليل، فقال أبو حنيفة : إن صلى ثماني ركعات [ صلاة التهجد :] * قوله : (فإن صلى بالليل : صلى ثمان ركعات (۱) . يعني: أقل ما ينبغي أن يتنفل في الليل بثماني ركعات. واعلم أن صلاة الليل أفضل من صلاة النهار؛ لقوله تعالى: تَتَجَافَى جُنُوبُهُمْ عَنِ الْمَضَاجِعِ .. السجدة / ١٦ ، ثم قال: ﴿ فَلَا تَعْلَمُ نَفْسٌ مَّا أُخْفِيَ لَهُم مِّن قُرَّةٍ أَعْيُنَ ). وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: مَن أطال قيام الليل: خَفَّف الله عنه يوم القيامة» (٢). * قوله : ( ونوافلُ النهار : إن شاء صلى ركعتين بتسليمة واحدة، وإن شاء أربعاً وتكره الزيادة على ذلك ، يعني بتسليمة واحدة. * قوله: (وأما نافلة الليل: فقال أبو حنيفة : إن صلى ثماني ركعات
If he prays at night, he prays eight rak'ahs. And supererogatory prayers of the day: if he wishes, he prays two rak'ahs with one taslima, and if he wishes, four, and it is disliked to exceed that. As for supererogatory prayer of the night, Abu Hanifa said: If he prays eight rak'ahs... [commentary:] His saying: 'If he prays at night, he prays eight rak'ahs' means: the minimum that is appropriate to pray as supererogatory at night is eight rak'ahs. Know that night prayer is superior to day prayer because of His saying: 'Their sides forsake their beds' (Sajdah 16), then He said: 'No soul knows what joy is laid up for them' (32:17). And he, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever lengthens the night prayer, Allah will ease for him the Day of Resurrection.' (2) His saying: 'And supererogatory prayers of the day: if he wishes, he prays two rak'ahs with one taslima, and if he wishes, four, and it is disliked to exceed that' means with one taslima. His saying: 'As for supererogatory prayer of the night, Abu Hanifa said: If he prays eight rak'ahs...'
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage establishes the numbers for supererogatory prayers. For night prayer (tahajjud), the minimum recommended is eight rak'ahs, as stated by Abu Hanifa. The author clarifies that the matn's 'eight' is the minimum appropriate. Night prayer is superior to day prayer, proven by Quranic verses (Sajdah 16, 32:17) describing those who pray at night, and a hadith promising ease on the Day of Resurrection for those who prolong night prayer. For day supererogatory prayers (such as the sunan rawatib or general nafl), the ruling is: one may pray two rak'ahs with one taslima, or four rak'ahs with one taslima. It is disliked (makruh tanzihi) to exceed four rak'ahs in a single taslima during the day. This is the Hanafi position. The commentary also notes that the four rak'ahs with one taslima is permissible for the day but not for the night, where the recommendation is to pray two rak'ahs per taslima, though the minimum total is eight.

Key Terms
نافلة الليل (nāfilat al-layl): Supererogatory prayer performed at night, also called tahajjud. Minimum 8 rak'ahs according to Abu Hanifa.
نافلة النهار (nāfilat an-nahār): Supererogatory prayer performed during the day. May be 2 or 4 rak'ahs per taslima.
تسليمة (taslīma): The act of concluding the prayer by saying salam. One taslima ends one unit of prayer (e.g., 2 or 4 rak'ahs).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Permitted.
B) Disliked.
C) Forbidden.
D) Recommended.

Key Takeaway
The minimum for night supererogatory is eight rak'ahs; day supererogatory must not exceed four rak'ahs per taslima.

Voluntary Night and Day Prayers: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Rak'ahs per Taslim
Intra-Hanafi dispute on optimal rak'ahs per taslim for night nawafil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the optimal number of rak'ahs per taslim for voluntary night prayers, explain their respective proofs, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds four-by-four for both night and day; the Sahibayn prefer two-by-two for night — both are permissible, the dispute is over preference.

Voluntary prayers (nawafil) are a means of drawing closer to Allah. This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, as explained by al-Shurunbulali in al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the best way to perform night nawafil: should one pray two rak'ahs per taslim or four? The discussion reveals the principles that guide preference (afdaliyyah) in Hanafi fiqh and shows how the school accommodates multiple valid opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and the dispute
Recognize that the passage discusses the number of rak'ahs per taslim for voluntary night and day prayers, and that the dispute is about the optimal (afdal) form, not permissibility.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the best is to pray four rak'ahs per taslim (four-by-four) for both night and day, and it is permissible to pray up to eight with one taslim for night, though disliked to exceed that.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that for night prayers, the best is two rak'ahs per taslim (two-by-two); for day prayers, they agree with Abu Hanifa that four-by-four is best.
4
Analyse the proofs
The Sahibayn argue by analogy with tarawih and because two-by-two increases the number of takbirat al-ihram, taslims, and supplications. Abu Hanifa argues that grouping four rak'ahs makes the ihram longer (adum), thus more strenuous and more virtuous.
Both arguments are valid within Hanafi usul; the dispute is over which aspect of worship is prioritized.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Hanafi may pray night nawafil either two-by-two or four-by-four. In practice, tarawih (a confirmed sunnah) is commonly prayed two-by-two following the Sahibayn, while general nawafil may follow either.

وتكره الزيادة على ذلك .
وأما نافلة الليل، فقال أبو حنيفة : إن صلى ثماني ركعات
بتسليمة واحدة : جاز، وتكره الزيادة على ذلك .
وقالا : لا يزيد بالليل على ركعتين بتسليمة واحدة .

واعلم أن صلاة الليل أفضل من صلاة النهار؛ لقوله تعالى: تَتَجَافَى جُنُوبُهُمْ عَنِ الْمَضَاجِعِ .. السجدة / ١٦ ، ثم قال: ﴿ فَلَا تَعْلَمُ نَفْسٌ مَّا أُخْفِيَ لَهُم مِّن قُرَّةٍ أَعْيُنِ ).
وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «من أطال قيام الليل: خفف الله عنه يوم القيامة».
قوله: ( ونوافلُ النهار : إن شاء صلى ركعتين بتسليمة واحدة، وإن شاء أربعاً وتكره الزيادة على ذلك ) يعني بتسليمة واحدة.
قوله: ( وأما نافلة الليل: فقال أبو حنيفة : إن صلى ثماني ركعات بتسليمة واحدة جاز، وتكره الزيادة على ذلك ) يعني إن شاء صلى بالليل أربعاً بتسليمة واحدة، وإن شاء ستاً بتسليمة واحدة، وإن شاء ثمانياً بتسليمة. وتكره الزيادة على ذلك. ولكن الأفضل أربعاً أربعاً بتسليمة، ليلاً ونهاراً.
قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد لا يزيد بالليل على ركعتين بتسليمة واحدة) : أي من حيث الأفضلية.
قال في «الهداية»: الأفضل في الليل عند أبي يوسف ومحمد : مثنى مثنى، وفي النهار : أربع أربع.
وعند الشافعي : فيهما مثنى مثنى.
وعند أبي حنيفة : فيهما أربع أربع.
لهما : الاعتبار بالتراويح، ولأن فيه زيادة تحريمة، وتسليمة، ودعاء. ولأبي حنيفة أنه أدوم تحريمةً، فيكون أكثر مشقة، وأزيد فضيلة.
Chapter of Voluntary Prayers
If he prays at night: he prays eight rak'ahs.
And voluntary prayers of the day: if he wishes, he prays two rak'ahs with one taslim, and if he wishes, four, and increasing beyond that is disliked.
As for the night voluntary prayer, Abu Hanifa said: If he prays eight rak'ahs with one taslim: it is permissible, and increasing beyond that is disliked.
And (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He should not increase at night beyond two rak'ahs with one taslim.
His saying: (If he prays at night: he prays eight rak'ahs) means: the minimum that he should perform voluntarily at night is eight rak'ahs. Know that night prayer is more virtuous than day prayer because of His saying: Their sides forsake their beds... [Sajdah 16], then He said: No soul knows what joy is hidden for them. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever lengthens his night standing, Allah will ease for him on the Day of Resurrection.'
His saying: (And voluntary prayers of the day: if he wishes, he prays two rak'ahs with one taslim, and if he wishes, four, and increasing beyond that is disliked) means with one taslim.
His saying: (As for the night voluntary prayer, Abu Hanifa said: If he prays eight rak'ahs with one taslim, it is permissible, and increasing beyond that is disliked) means: if he wishes, he prays at night four with one taslim, if he wishes six with one taslim, and if he wishes eight with one taslim. And increasing beyond that is disliked. But the best is four by four with a taslim, both night and day.
His saying: (And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: He should not increase at night beyond two rak'ahs with one taslim) means in terms of preference.
It is stated in al-Hidayah: The best at night according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is two by two, and in the day four by four. According to al-Shafi'i: in both it is two by two. According to Abu Hanifa: in both it is four by four. For them (Sahibayn): consideration of tarawih, and because it involves more takbirat al-ihram, taslim, and supplication. For Abu Hanifa: that it has a longer duration of takbirat al-ihram, thus it is more strenuous and more virtuous.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), on the best way to perform voluntary night prayers. The discussion arises from the matn of al-Quduri, which states that the minimum night prayer is eight rak'ahs, and the day prayer can be two or four per taslim. The commentator elaborates: night prayer is more virtuous than day, citing Quran and hadith. For night prayer, the matn reports Abu Hanifa's view that praying eight rak'ahs with one taslim is permissible but disliked to exceed that. The Sahibayn restrict night prayer to two rak'ahs per taslim (i.e., optimum). The commentator clarifies that this is about preference (afdaliyyah), not permissibility. He then cites al-Hidayah: the Sahibayn prefer two-by-two for night (like tarawih), and four-by-four for day (as in the matn). Shafi'i holds two-by-two for both. Abu Hanifa holds four-by-four for both. The reasoning: the Sahibayn argue that praying two-by-two increases the number of takbirat al-ihram (opening takbirs), taslims, and supplications, so more acts. Abu Hanifa argues that grouping four rak'ahs makes the takbirat al-ihram longer (adum), meaning the worshipper remains longer in a state of ihram (consecration), which involves more effort and thus greater reward. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position? The text does not explicitly state tarjih, but the commentary notes the best (al-afdal) is four-by-four for both night and day, which is Abu Hanifa's view; however, the Sahibayn's view is also valid and often followed in practice for tarawih.

Key Terms
نوافل (nawafil): Voluntary prayers beyond the obligatory ones; in this context, the sunnah prayers of night and day.
تسليمة (taslimah): The greeting of peace that concludes the prayer; here it means a single unit of prayer ending with one taslim, i.e., a set of rak'ahs linked by one opening takbir and one closing taslim.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The takbirat al-ihram (opening takbir) that initiates the prayer; each set of rak'ahs has one tahrimah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the preferred number of rak'ahs per taslim for voluntary night prayer according to Abu Hanifa?
A) Two rak'ahs per taslim
B) Four rak'ahs per taslim
C) Six rak'ahs per taslim
D) Eight rak'ahs per taslim

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits both two-by-two and four-by-four for night nawafil, but the preferred view of Abu Hanifa is four-by-four for greater continuous ihram; the Sahibayn's two-by-two is also valid and commonly followed in tarawih.
