Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Rak'ahs per Taslimah in Nafil Prayers
Intra-Hanafi dispute on preferred rak'ahs per taslimah in nafil prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the preferred number of rak'ahs per taslimah in voluntary prayers, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the ruling to vow scenarios.

Core Idea
Praying more than eight rak'ahs at night or four by day with one taslimah is permissible but disliked; the best (afdal) is four by four.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah delves into an intra-Hanafi disagreement about the most virtuous way to perform voluntary prayers. While the matn states that praying multiple rak'ahs with a single taslimah is permissible, it also identifies a disliked increase and presents the views of the great imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this dispute is crucial for correctly applying the preferred practice and for fulfilling vows related to prayer units.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
Determine the permissibility and the disliked limit for praying multiple rak'ahs with one taslimah as stated in the matn.
The matn says 'jaza' (permissible) and 'takrah al-ziyada' (increase is disliked).
2
Locate the Sahibayn's Restriction
Find the statement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding night prayers and understand that it concerns preference, not prohibition.
They say 'la yazid' meaning 'should not increase' from an optimal perspective.
3
Analyze the Proofs
Examine the reasoning of the Sahibayn (qiyas to tarawih) and Abu Hanifa (longer continuous prayer is more virtuous).
Consider the role of tahrimah, taslimah, and du'a in their arguments.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Identify which position is relied upon in the text and why.
The text states 'الأفضل أربعاً أربعاً' indicating preference for Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Apply to Vows
Work through the practical rule: if one vows four rak'ahs with one taslimah, it cannot be fulfilled with two taslimahs, and vice versa.
This shows the legal effect of the disagreement on the validity of prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
بتسليمة واحدة : جاز، وتكره الزيادة على ذلك .
وقالا : لا يزيد بالليل على ركعتين بتسليمة واحدة .
يعني إن شاء صلى بالليل أربعاً بتسليمة واحدة، وإن شاء ستاً بتسليمة واحدة، وإن شاء ثمانياً بتسليمة.
وتكره الزيادة على ذلك.
ولكن الأفضل أربعاً أربعاً بتسليمة، ليلاً ونهاراً.
قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد لا يزيد بالليل على ركعتين بتسليمة واحدة) : أي من حيث الأفضلية.
قال في «الهداية» (۱): الأفضل في الليل عند أبي يوسف ومحمد : مثنى مثنى، وفي النهار : أربع أربع.
وعند الشافعي : فيهما مثنى مثنى.
وعند أبي حنيفة : فيهما أربع أربع.
لهما : الاعتبار بالتراويح، ولأن فيه زيادة تحريمة، وتسليمة، ودعاء. ولأبي حنيفة أنه أدوم تحريمةً، فيكون أكثر مشقة، وأزيد فضيلة.
ولهذا لو نذر أن يصلى أربعاً بتسليمة: لا يخرج عنه بتسليمتين، وعلى العكس : يخرج. كذا في «الهداية».
وأما في التراويح : فإنها تؤدى بجماعة، فيراعى فيها التيسير.
وقوله : وتكره الزيادة على ذلك أي على ثمان ركعات في صلاة الليل بتسليمة، والزيادة في صلاة النهار على أربع بتسليمة.
Chapter of Voluntary Prayers. With one taslimah: it is permissible, and increase beyond that is disliked. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He should not increase at night more than two rak'ahs with one taslimah. He means: If he wishes, he may pray at night four with one taslimah, or six with one taslimah, or eight with one taslimah. And increase beyond that is disliked. But the best is four by four with a taslimah, night and day. His statement: (And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: He should not increase at night more than two rak'ahs with one taslimah) means from the perspective of preference. It is stated in al-Hidayah: The best at night according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is two by two, and during the day is four by four. According to al-Shafi'i: in both they are two by two. According to Abu Hanifa: in both they are four by four. Their proof: analogy with tarawih, and because there is an increase in initiating takbir, taslimah, and supplication. And for Abu Hanifa: it is more continuous in the initiating takbir, so it is more strenuous and more virtuous. Because of this, if one vows to pray four with one taslimah, he does not fulfill it with two taslimahs; and the opposite, he fulfills. Thus in al-Hidayah. As for tarawih, it is performed in congregation, so ease is considered. And his statement: And increase beyond that is disliked means beyond eight rak'ahs in night prayer with one taslimah, and increase in day prayer beyond four with one taslimah.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the preferred number of rak'ahs per taslimah in voluntary (nafil) prayers, with mention of the Shafi'i position. The matn of Quduri states that praying with one taslimah is permissible (jaza) and any increase beyond the limit is disliked (makruh tanzihan). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restrict this permissibility at night, saying one should not exceed two rak'ahs per taslimah. The commentary explains: 'jaza' means it is allowed; the disliked increase is beyond eight at night and four by day. The best (afdal) according to Abu Hanifa is four by four, night and day. Al-Hidayah clarifies that the Sahibayn's view is about preference (afdaliyya), not prohibition: at night they prefer two by two, by day four by four. Imam al-Shafi'i prefers two by two in both. Abu Hanifa prefers four by four in both. The Sahibayn's proof: analogy with tarawih (which is two by two) and because praying with more taslimahs increases the number of initiating takbirs, salutations, and supplications, thus more blessed. Abu Hanifa's proof: a longer continuous prayer is more taxing and thus more virtuous. A practical application: if one vows to pray four rak'ahs with one taslimah, he cannot fulfill it with two separate taslimahs, but if he vows to pray four with two taslimahs, he can fulfill it with one taslimah (since the act is valid). Tarawih is excepted: because it is congregational, ease is prioritized. The karaha (dislike) is explained as being for exceeding eight at night and four by day.

Key Terms
تسليمة (taslimah): The final salutation (saying السلام عليكم) that ends a prayer; here used to count the number of rak'ahs between two salutations.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying الله أكبر) that initiates the prayer; here used as a unit of merit.
نافلة (nafila): Voluntary (supererogatory) prayer, not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the best (afdal) way to pray voluntary prayers at night according to Abu Hanifa?
A) Two rak'ahs by two with one taslimah
B) Four rak'ahs by four with one taslimah
C) Eight rak'ahs by eight with one taslimah
D) One rak'ah by one with one taslimah

Key Takeaway
In voluntary prayers, the Hanafi school permits multiple rak'ahs with one taslimah, but the mufta bihi opinion (Abu Hanifa) holds that the best is four by four, both night and day, because it is more strenuous and virtuous.

Basic Obligation in Supererogatory Prayer: Two Rak'ahs
Explains the principle that the minimum obligatory unit in nafila is two rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum obligatory unit in supererogatory prayer and apply the rule for makeup after spoilage.

Core Idea
The basic obligatory unit in nafila is two rak'ahs; only two are owed even if you intended more.

This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayirah explains a fundamental principle of supererogatory prayer (nafila): the contractual obligation (mojib al-aqd) is a pair of rak'ahs. Using a striking analogy—each pair is like a separate prayer—it establishes a clear rule: if you spoil a nafila intended for multiple pairs, you only owe two rak'ahs in makeup. The text also addresses vows for odd or fractional rak'ahs, reinforcing the pair-based structure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and obligation
Recognize that starting a nafila creates a binding contract (aqd) with a minimum obligation (mojib) of two rak'ahs.
This is the central ruling.
2
Understand the pair structure
Each pair (shaf') is an independent prayer unit; additional pairs only become binding upon standing for the first rak'ah of that pair.
The second pair becomes obligatory when you stand for the third rak'ah.
3
Analyze the evidence
Note the qiyas (analogy) that pairs are like separate prayers: you recite Fatiha and a sura in every rak'ah, and when standing for the third, you recite the opening supplication as at the start.
This structure shows independence.
4
Apply to spoilage case
If you intend multiple pairs and spoil the prayer, you only need to make up two rak'ahs (according to Zahir al-Riwayah).
This is the operative ruling.
5
Note intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one requiring four rak'ahs, another requiring whatever was intended. But the relied-upon position is two.
The text explicitly says 'fi zahir al-riwayah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وموجب العقد في التطوع ركعتان وإنما يلزمه الشفع الثاني بالقيام إليه في الثالثة ؛ لأن كل شفع من التطوع : كصلاة على حدة. ألا ترى أنه يقرأ في كل ركعة منه الفاتحة وسورة، وإذا قام إلى الثالثة : استفتح كما يستفتح عقيب التحريمة.
فعلى هذا : إذا افتتح التطوع بنية الأربع أو الست أو الثمان، ثم أفسده : لم يلزمه إلا قضاء ركعتين، في ظاهر الرواية.
وعن أبي يوسف روايتان في رواية يلزمه أربع، وفي رواية: يلزمه ما نوى. ولو قال: الله علي أن أصلي ركعة: لزمه ركعتان.
وإن قال: ثلاث ركعات يلزمه أربع ؛ لأن التطوع لا يجوز أن يكون
وإن قال : نصف ركعة لزمه ركعة ؛ لأنها لا تتبعض، وإذا لزمته
And the obligatory component of the contract in supererogatory prayer is two rak'ahs, and the second pair only becomes obligatory upon his standing up for the third; because each pair in supererogatory prayer is like a separate prayer. Do you not see that he recites in each rak'ah of it the Fatiha and a sura, and when he stands for the third, he recites the opening supplication as he does after the initiating takbir. Based on this: If one begins supererogatory prayer with the intention of four, or six, or eight, then spoils it, he is only required to make up two rak'ahs, in the apparent narration. And from Abu Yusuf there are two narrations: in one narration he is required to make up four, and in another narration he is required to make up what he intended. And if he says: By Allah, I owe a rak'ah, he is required to pray two rak'ahs. And if he says: three rak'ahs, he is required to pray four; because supererogatory prayer is not valid as (odd). And if he says: half a rak'ah, he is required to pray one rak'ah; because it cannot be divided, and if it becomes obligatory upon him...
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage discusses the minimum obligation that becomes binding upon starting a supererogatory prayer (nafila). The principle is that the basic unit ('mojib al-aqd') is two rak'ahs. If one intends more than two, additional pairs only become obligatory when one physically stands for the next pair (e.g., the third rak'ah). The proof: each pair is like a separate prayer; you recite Fatiha and a sura in every rak'ah, and when standing for the third rak'ah, you say the opening supplication (istaftah) as at the start. Therefore, if you start a nafila intending four, six, or eight rak'ahs and then spoil it (e.g., by breaking wudu or talking), you only need to make up two rak'ahs according to the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah). This is the relied-upon position. Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one that you must make up four, and another that you must make up whatever you intended. Other rulings: If someone vows to pray one rak'ah, he must pray two (because a nafila cannot be one rak'ah). If he vows three, he must pray four (since odd numbers are not valid in nafila; the minimum pair is two, so he must add one to make an even number). If he vows half a rak'ah, he must pray one rak'ah (since a rak'ah cannot be divided).

Key Terms
موجب العقد (mojib al-aqd): The obligatory component that is required by the act of initiating a contract; here it refers to the minimum number of rak'ahs that become binding upon starting a supererogatory prayer.
شافع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; in supererogatory prayer, each pair is considered a separate prayer unit.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent/official narration from Imam Muhammad's six books; the most authoritative position in the Hanafi school.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed or spoiled prayer; in this context, the obligatory makeup of two rak'ahs after spoiling a nafila.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person starts a supererogatory prayer intending to pray six rak'ahs with one taslimah, and then spoils it after the fourth rak'ah, how many rak'ahs must he make up according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah)?
A) Six rak'ahs
B) Two rak'ahs
C) Four rak'ahs
D) Eight rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
In supererogatory prayer, the basic obligatory unit is two rak'ahs; if spoiled, only two need to be made up, even if more were intended.

Voluntary Prayers: Binding of Pairs and Disliked Increase
Ruling statement on voluntary prayer pairs and disliked limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the binding of pairs in voluntary prayer and identify the disliked increase per taslimah.

Core Idea
Each pair of voluntary prayer is independent; only the first becomes binding upon intention.

Voluntary prayers (nawafil) have unique rules distinguishing them from obligatory prayers. The Hanafi school emphasizes that each pair (shaf‘) is like a separate prayer, leading to specific rulings on intention, invalidation, and disliked increases. This lesson unpacks the key principles from the matn.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of a 'taslimah'
Identify that a taslimah concludes a prayer unit. In voluntary prayer, the number of rak'ahs per taslimah is limited, and exceeding it is disliked.
Taslimah refers to the salam ending.
2
Grasp the binding of the first pair
When one intends a voluntary prayer, only the first two rak'ahs (the first pair) become immediately binding. Subsequent pairs become binding only when one stands for their first rak'ah.
This is because each pair is like a separate prayer.
3
Apply the rule to invalidation
If one begins a four-rak’ah voluntary and invalidates it, only two rak’ahs must be made up, as only the first pair was binding. This is the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah).
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute here.
4
Identify the disliked increase
It is makruh to pray more than eight rak’ahs per taslimah at night, or more than four during the day.
Tarawih is an exception due to congregation and ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
ولهذا لو نذر أن يصلى أربعاً بتسليمة: لا يخرج عنه بتسليمتين، وعلى العكس : يخرج. كذا في «الهداية».
وأما في التراويح : فإنها تؤدى بجماعة، فيراعى فيها التيسير.
وقوله : وتكره الزيادة على ذلك أي على ثمان ركعات في صلاة الليل بتسليمة، والزيادة في صلاة النهار على أربع بتسليمة.
وموجب العقد في التطوع ركعتان وإنما يلزمه الشفع الثاني بالقيام إليه في الثالثة ؛ لأن كل شفع من التطوع : كصلاة على حدة. ألا ترى أنه يقرأ في كل ركعة منه الفاتحة وسورة، وإذا قام إلى الثالثة : استفتح كما يستفتح عقيب التحريمة.
فعلى هذا : إذا افتتح التطوع بنية الأربع أو الست أو الثمان، ثم أفسده : لم يلزمه إلا قضاء ركعتين، في ظاهر الرواية.
وعن أبي يوسف روايتان في رواية يلزمه أربع، وفي رواية: يلزمه ما نوى. ولو قال: الله علي أن أصلي ركعة: لزمه ركعتان.
وإن قال: ثلاث ركعات يلزمه أربع ؛ لأن التطوع لا يجوز أن يكون وتراً. وإن قال : نصف ركعة لزمه ركعة ؛ لأنها لا تتبعض، وإذا لزمته ركعة: وجب عليه ركعتان؛ لأن التطوع لا يكون وتراً.
ولو قال : ركعتين بغير وضوء : لا يلزمه شيء عند محمد. وقال أبو يوسف: يلزمه ركعتان بوضوء؛ تصحيحاً للنذر.
ولو قال: ركعتين بغير قراءة: لزمه ركعتان بقراءة، إجماعاً؛ لأن الصلاة بغير طهارة ليست بعبادة، وأما بغير قراءة: فهي عبادة، كصلاة الأمي والأخرس.
Chapter of Voluntary Prayers. For this reason, if one vows to pray four (rak'ahs) with one taslimah: he is not absolved by two taslimahs, and conversely he is absolved. Thus in Al-Hidayah. As for Tarawih: it is performed in congregation, so ease is observed. And his statement: And it is disliked to increase beyond that, i.e., beyond eight rak'ahs in night prayer per taslimah, and increase in day prayer beyond four per taslimah. The required binding in voluntary prayer is two rak'ahs, and the second pair only becomes binding by standing for the third, because each pair of voluntary prayer is like a separate prayer. Do you not see that he recites Al-Fatihah and a Surah in each rak'ah, and when he stands for the third, he begins (the opening supplication) just as he begins after the takbir tahrimah? Based on this: if one begins voluntary prayer with the intention of four, six, or eight, then invalidates it, he is only required to make up two rak'ahs in the apparent narration. From Abu Yusuf there are two narrations: in one narration, he is required (to make up) four, and in one narration: he is required what he intended. And if one says: I owe it to Allah to pray one rak'ah: he must pray two rak'ahs. And if he says: three rak'ahs, he must pray four, because voluntary prayer cannot be odd (witr). And if he says: half a rak'ah, he must pray one rak'ah, because it is not divisible. And when one rak'ah becomes binding, he must pray two rak'ahs, because voluntary prayer cannot be odd. And if he says: two rak'ahs without ablution: nothing is binding upon him according to Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: he must pray two rak'ahs with ablution, to validate the vow. And if he says: two rak'ahs without recitation: he must pray two rak'ahs with recitation, by consensus, because prayer without purity is not an act of worship, but without recitation it is an act of worship, like the prayer of the unlettered and the mute.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement from the chapter on voluntary prayers. It begins by explaining that if one vows to pray four rak'ahs with a single taslimah (i.e., without separating with salam after two), they cannot fulfill that vow by praying with two taslimahs; conversely, if one vows four with two taslimahs, they are absolved by one taslimah? Actually the text says 'and conversely he is absolved' meaning if he vows four with two taslimahs, he can fulfill with one taslimah? The Hidayah clarifies. Then it mentions that Tarawih is performed in congregation, so flexibility is observed. It then states that it is disliked to increase beyond eight rak'ahs per taslimah in night prayer and beyond four in day prayer. The core ruling: the binding minimum in voluntary prayer is two rak'ahs (a pair). A second pair only becomes binding when one stands for the third rak'ah, because each pair is like a separate prayer. Evidence: in each rak'ah one recites Fatihah and a surah, and when standing for the third, one begins anew like after the opening takbir. Therefore, if one begins a voluntary prayer intending four, six, or eight rak'ahs and then invalidates it, they are only obligated to make up two rak'ahs according to the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: from Abu Yusuf there are two narrations: one requires four rak'ahs, another requires what he intended. Then it covers vows: if one vows to pray one rak'ah, they must pray two; if three, they must pray four because voluntary prayer cannot be odd (witr); if half a rak'ah, one rak'ah is required, but since one rak'ah is binding, they must complete two because voluntary prayer cannot be odd. Finally, if one vows to pray two rak'ahs without ablution: Muhammad says nothing is binding, but Abu Yusuf says they must pray two with ablution to validate the vow. If one vows to pray two rak'ahs without recitation: by consensus they must pray with recitation, because prayer without purity is not worship, but without recitation it is still worship, like the prayer of an unlettered person or mute.

Key Terms
تسليمة (taslimah): The final salutation ending a prayer; used here as a unit to measure pairs of rak'ahs.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; in voluntary prayer, each pair is considered an independent unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration, if someone begins a voluntary prayer intending six rak'ahs and then invalidates it before standing for the third rak'ah, how many rak'ahs must they make up?
A) Six rak'ahs
B) Two rak'ahs
C) Four rak'ahs
D) Eight rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
In voluntary prayer, only the first pair is automatically binding; increasing beyond 8 per taslimah at night is disliked.

Vows (Niffling) in Voluntary Prayers: Intra-Hanafi Rules
Ruling statement on vows for voluntary prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on vows for voluntary prayers, including correcting odd numbers and the effect of conditions like ablution and recitation.

Core Idea
A vow for voluntary prayer must be for an even number; odd vows are corrected to the next even, and conditions contrary to worship are invalid.

Vows (niffling) regarding voluntary prayers require careful attention to the Hanafi rules on parity and conditions. This lesson covers the corrections for odd numbers, the rulings on vows with missing purity or recitation, and the intra-Hanafi differences between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the vow's intention
Determine the number of rak'ahs the person vows. If it is odd, it must be corrected to the next even number, because voluntary prayer cannot be odd (witr).
E.g., 1 becomes 2, 3 becomes 4, 5 becomes 6.
2
Handle fractions
If someone vows half a rak'ah, it is rounded up to one rak'ah, and then to two because it cannot be odd.
Thus half a rak'ah becomes two rak'ahs.
3
Apply conditions of the vow
If the vow includes a condition that violates the validity of prayer (e.g., without ablution), the condition is nullified, and the prayer must be performed correctly. There is a dispute between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.
Muhammad: vow without ablution is invalid; Abu Yusuf: it is valid but must be prayed with ablution.
4
Consensus on recitation
Vowing to pray without recitation is invalid; the prayer must include recitation by consensus, as prayer without recitation is still worship but the vow is not fulfilled without it.
Prayer without ablution is not worship, so vow is void.

Recitation in Obligatory Prayers: Only the First Two Rak'ahs
Establishes Hanafi position and proves it against other schools

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the obligation of recitation in obligatory prayers, explain the Hanafi proof from the Quran and qiyas, and evaluate the Shafi'i and Maliki counter-arguments.

Core Idea
Recitation is obligatory only in the first two rak'ahs; a single Quranic command does not demand repetition.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that recitation in obligatory prayers is only required in the first two rak'ahs. This position is derived from the Quranic verse 'So recite what is easy from the Qur'an' and the principle that a command does not imply repetition. We will contrast this with the Shafi'i view requiring recitation in every rak'ah and the Maliki view requiring it in three. Understanding this dispute is key to proper prayer practice and to appreciating how different usul principles lead to different rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that recitation (qira'ah) in obligatory prayers is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs. It is fard qat'i in terms of action.
The author clarifies it is a definitive obligation in practice, even if technically wajib in terminology.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their arguments
Al-Shafi'i requires recitation in all rak'ahs based on the hadith 'No prayer except with recitation' and that each rak'ah is a prayer. Al-Malik requires it in three rak'ahs, applying the principle of treating the majority as the whole for ease.
Note the different usul principles: Shafi'i uses general hadith; Malik uses evaluating the majority.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof from the Quran
The Hanafi rely on Quran 73:20: 'So recite what is easy from the Qur'an.' The command is general and does not require repetition; therefore it is fulfilled by reciting in two rak'ahs.
This is a key Hanafi usul principle: al-amr bi al-fi'l la yaqtadi al-tikrar.
4
Understand the Hanafi use of qiyas
The first two rak'ahs are analogous (mutashakil) in every respect, so recitation in the second is justified by analogy to the first. The last two rak'ahs are different because they are dropped during travel (shortened prayer), so recitation is not obligatory there.
Qiyas is used to extend the obligation from first to second, but the distinguishing factor (travel) blocks analogy for the last two.
5
Examine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
A Hanafi following a Shafi'i imam must still recite in the first two rak'ahs but may remain silent in the last two; a Shafi'i recites in all. A Maliki recites in three.
The difference affects how a Hanafi prays behind a non-Hanafi imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والقراءة في الفرائض واجبةٌ في الركعتين الأوليين): أي فرض قطعي في حق العمل.
وقال الشافعي: فرض في الركعات كلها؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لا صلاة إلا بقراءة»، وكل ركعة صلاة.
وقال مالك: فرض في ثلاث؛ إقامة للأكثر مقام الكل؛ تيسيراً.
ولنا: قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْرَءُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْءَانِ﴾، والأمر بالفعل لا يقتضي التكرار وإنما أوجبناها في الثانية؛ استدلالاً بالأولى؛ لأنهما يتشاكلان من كل وجه، وأما الأخريان فيفارقانهما في حق السقوط بالسفر،
His statement: (And recitation in obligatory prayers is obligatory in the first two rak'ahs) i.e., it is certain obligatory in terms of action. Al-Shafi'i said: It is obligatory in all rak'ahs, because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'There is no prayer except with recitation,' and every rak'ah is a prayer. Malik said: It is obligatory in three, treating the majority as the whole, for ease. Our proof: The Almighty's statement: 'So recite what is easy from the Qur'an' [al-Muzzammil 73:20], and a command to act does not necessitate repetition. And we made it obligatory in the second by analogy with the first, because they are similar in every respect. As for the last two, they differ from them in that they are dropped during travel.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage is an inter_madhhab_dispute concerning the obligation of recitation in obligatory prayers. The Hanafi position states that recitation is obligatory only in the first two rak'ahs. The author clarifies that this is a definitive obligation (fard qat'i) in terms of action, meaning it is obligatory to perform. Al-Shafi'i argues that recitation is obligatory in every rak'ah, citing the Prophet's hadith 'There is no prayer except with recitation' and reasoning that each rak'ah is a prayer. Malik says it is obligatory in three rak'ahs, using the principle of treating the majority as the whole for ease. The Hanafi response (lana) presents the Quranic verse from Surah al-Muzzammil: 'So recite what is easy from the Qur'an.' The argument is that a command to perform an action (al-amr bi al-fi'l) does not necessitate repetition (la yaqtadi al-tikrar) – meaning the verse commands recitation but does not specify it for every rak'ah. Hanafis then establish recitation in the second rak'ah by analogy (istidlalan) with the first, because the first two rak'ahs are identical in all respects. The last two rak'ahs differ because they can be dropped during travel (i.e., the traveler shortens the prayer to two rak'ahs, so the last two are not performed; hence recitation there would be dropped as well, showing they are not analogous to the first two). Thus, the Hanafi proof is based on the Quranic command (which does not require repetition) and the analogy between the first two rak'ahs, contrasted with the last two which are subject to abrogation in travel.

Key Terms
فرض قطعي في حق العمل (fard qat'i fi haqq al-'amal): A legally established obligation that is definitive and must be acted upon; equivalent to fard in the Hanafi classification.
لا يقتضي التكرار (la yaqtadi al-tikrar): The command in the Qur'an to recite does not imply that it must be repeated in every rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the specific distinguishing factor that the Hanafi use to argue that recitation is not obligatory in the last two rak'ahs?
A) The last two rak'ahs are silent in all prayers.
B) The last two rak'ahs are dropped during travel.
C) The Quran does not mention the last two rak'ahs.
D) The Prophet never recited in the last two rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
Recitation in obligatory prayers is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs, based on the Quranic command and the analogy that the last two are dropped in travel.

Rulings on Vows Regarding Prayer Conditions
Matn statements on vowing to pray deficiently and intra-Hanafi dispute on wudu condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on vowing to pray deficiently and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on vowing without wudu.

Core Idea
A vow to pray without wudu is invalid per Muhammad; corrected by Abu Yusuf; recitation is not essential.

Vows (nadhr) to perform supererogatory prayers raise questions about essential conditions. The Hanafi school has a clear ruling on the minimum rak'ahs, but for conditions like wudu and recitation, there are nuances. This lesson examines three cases from Al-Quduri's Matn and the dispute between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three vow scenarios
List the three cases: vowing one rak'ah, vowing two rak'ahs without wudu, vowing two rak'ahs without recitation.
2
Apply the principle of minimum valid supererogatory prayer
For the one-rak'ah case, note that supererogatory prayer must be at least two rak'ahs, so the vow is corrected to two.
This is based on the definition of tatawwu'.
3
Distinguish the validity of conditions
Compare wudu and recitation: wudu is a condition for validity (prayer without it is not worship), recitation is not (prayer without it is still worship, as for the illiterate).
This explains why the recitation case is unanimous.
4
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
For vowing without wudu, Imam Muhammad says nothing is owed; Abu Yusuf says the vow is corrected to two rak'ahs with wudu.
The dispute hinges on whether the vow can be fulfilled by a corrected valid act.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Muhammad's view frees the person from any obligation; Abu Yusuf's view requires two rak'ahs with wudu.
This affects whether one must act or is absolved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ركعة: وجب عليه ركعتان؛ لأن التطوع لا يكون وتراً. ولو قال : ركعتين بغير وضوء : لا يلزمه شيء عند محمد. وقال أبو يوسف: يلزمه ركعتان بوضوء؛ تصحيحاً للنذر. ولو قال: ركعتين بغير قراءة: لزمه ركعتان بقراءة، إجماعاً؛ لأن الصلاة بغير طهارة ليست بعبادة، وأما بغير قراءة: فهي عبادة، كصلاة الأمي والأخرس.
If he says: one rak'ah, then two rak'ahs are obligatory upon him, because the supererogatory prayer is not odd. And if he says: two rak'ahs without ablution, then nothing is obligatory upon him according to Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said: two rak'ahs with ablution are obligatory upon him, to correct the vow. And if he says: two rak'ahs without recitation, then two rak'ahs with recitation are obligatory upon him, by consensus; because prayer without purity is not worship, but without recitation it is worship, like the prayer of the illiterate and the mute.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage presents rulings on vows regarding prayer. First, if someone vows to pray one rak'ah, it is not valid as a voluntary prayer (which must be at least two), so he must pray two. Second, vowing to pray two rak'ahs without wudu: according to Imam Muhammad, the vow is invalid because prayer without wudu is not a valid act of worship, so nothing is owed. Abu Yusuf, however, says the vow is corrected to the minimum valid prayer (with wudu), making it obligatory. Third, vowing to pray without recitation: by consensus, the vow is valid and he must recite, because prayer without recitation is still a valid worship (like the prayer of an illiterate or mute person), whereas prayer without wudu is not.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship
تطوع (tatawwu'): Supererogatory prayer, which must consist of at least two rak'ahs

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what happens if someone vows to pray two rak'ahs without wudu?
A) The vow is valid and he must pray with wudu.
B) The vow is invalid and nothing is owed.
C) He must pray two rak'ahs without wudu.
D) He must pray one rak'ah with wudu.

Key Takeaway
Vows to pray deficiently require that the core act be valid worship; conditions (wudu) are essential, while recitation is not, leading to an intra-Hanafi dispute on the wudu case.

Recitation in Obligatory Prayer: Wajib in First Two Rak'ahs
Inter-madhhab dispute with legal proof analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in obligatory prayer, explain the Hanafi proof from Quran and hadith, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi interpretation of 'لا صلاة إلا بقراءة'.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, recitation (qira'ah) is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs of obligatory prayer; the last two are optional.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayra explains that recitation in obligatory prayers is wajib (binding) only in the first two rak'ahs, not in all rak'ahs. It presents the Hanafi evidence from the Quran and hadith, and responds to the Shafi'i and Maliki positions. Understanding this ruling is crucial for correctly performing the obligatory prayers according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the precise ruling: recitation is wajib (فريض قطعي في حق العمل) only in the first two rak'ahs of obligatory prayers. Note that it is not fard because it can be dropped in certain situations (e.g., travel).
2
Identify the opposing schools and their proofs
Summarize Shafi'i (obligatory in all rak'ahs, using hadith 'لا صلاة إلا بقراءة' and claiming every rak'ah is a prayer) and Maliki (obligatory in three rak'ahs, using the principle of treating the majority as the whole).
3
Analyze the Hanafi Quranic proof
Examine Quran 73:20 'فَاقْرَءُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْءَانِ'. The Hanafi argue that the command does not imply repetition; thus recitation is required only once in the prayer (i.e., in the first two rak'ahs by analogy).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i hadith
Understand the Hanafi interpretation: 'لا صلاة إلا بقراءة' refers to the complete prayer (two rak'ahs), not each individual rak'ah. Support is given by oath examples: if someone swears not to pray 'a prayer', they break the oath only after two rak'ahs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Shafi'i must recite in every rak'ah, while Hanafi may choose (recite, glorify, or remain silent) in the last two rak'ahs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والقراءة في الفرائض واجبةٌ في الركعتين الأوليين): أي فرض قطعي في حق العمل. وقال الشافعي (۱): فرض في الركعات كلها؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لا صلاة إلا بقراءة»(۲)، وكل ركعة صلاة. وقال مالك (۳) : فرض في ثلاث؛ إقامة للأكثر مقام الكل؛ تيسيراً. ولنا: قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْرَءُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْءَانِ . المزمل / ۲۰ ، والأمر بالفعل لا يقتضي التكرار وإنما أوجبناها في الثانية؛ استدلالاً بالأولى؛ لأنهما يتشاكلان من كل وجه، وأما الأخريان فيفارقانهما في حق السقوط بالسفر، وهو مُخيَّر في الأخريين : إن شاء قرأ الفاتحة، وإن شاء سبح، وإن شاء سكت. وصفة القراءة في الجهر والإخفاء، وفي قدر القراءة: فلا يلحقان بهما. وأما قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لا صلاة إلا بقراءة : فهو شاهد لنا ؛ لأنه ذَكَرَ الصلاة مطلقاً، والصلاة متى ذُكرت مطلقة: لا تنصرف إلى ركعة، وإنما تنصرف إلى صلاة كاملة، وهي ركعتان عرفاً، كمن حلف: لا يصلي صلاة: فإنه لا يحنث حتى يصلي ركعتين. بخلاف ما إذا حلف لا يصلي، ولم يقل: صلاةً: فإنه يحنث إذا صلى ركعة.
His saying: 'And recitation in obligatory prayers is obligatory in the first two rak'ahs': meaning it is an obligatory requirement in terms of action. Al-Shafi'i said: it is obligatory in all rak'ahs, because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'There is no prayer without recitation', and every rak'ah is a prayer. And Malik said: it is obligatory in three, treating the majority as the whole, for facilitation. Our evidence: The Almighty's saying: 'So recite what is easy from the Qur'an' [Al-Muzzammil 73:20], and the command does not necessitate repetition. Rather, we made it obligatory in the second by analogy with the first, because they are similar in every respect. As for the last two, they differ from them in that they can be dropped during travel, and he is given a choice in the last two: if he wishes he recites the Fatiha, if he wishes he glorifies, if he wishes he remains silent. And the description of recitation in terms of loudness and softness, and the amount of recitation: they do not follow them. As for his statement, peace be upon him: 'There is no prayer without recitation', it is a witness for us, because he mentioned prayer absolutely, and prayer when mentioned absolutely does not refer to a single rak'ah, but rather refers to a complete prayer, which is two rak'ahs by custom, like the case of one who swears: 'I will not pray a prayer' – he does not break the oath until he prays two rak'ahs. Unlike if he swears not to pray and does not say 'a prayer', then he breaks the oath if he prays one rak'ah.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the matn's ruling that recitation is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs of obligatory prayers. It presents the views of Shafi'i (obligatory in all rak'ahs) and Malik (obligatory in three). The Hanafi evidence includes the Quranic verse (73:20), arguing that the command does not imply repetition; the second rak'ah is analogized to the first, while the last two are distinguished by their permissibility of being dropped during travel and the given choice. The hadith 'لا صلاة إلا بقراءة' is interpreted to refer to the complete prayer of two rak'ahs, not individual rak'ahs, supported by oath examples. The Hanafi position is thus established.

Key Terms
قراءة (qira'ah): Recitation of Qur'an in prayer
فرض قطعي (fard qat'i): A definitive obligation in terms of action (not belief) according to the Hanafi school
ركعة (rak'ah): One unit of prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person prays the four-rak'ah Zuhr prayer and recites Fatiha and a surah only in the first and third rak'ahs, remaining silent in the second and fourth, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because recitation is wajib in every rak'ah.
B) The prayer is valid but deficient because recitation was omitted in the second rak'ah (a wajib).
C) The prayer is valid and complete because recitation in the third rak'ah compensates for the second.
D) The prayer is invalid because recitation must be in the first two rak'ahs only.

Key Takeaway
Recitation in obligatory prayer is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs according to the Hanafi school; the last two are optional, and the Shafi'i counter-argument is answered by interpreting 'prayer' in the hadith as a complete two-rak'ah unit.

Choice in Last Two Rak'ahs of Obligatory Prayer
Explanation of options in the last two rak'ahs: recite, glorify, or remain silent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three options in the last two rak'ahs of obligatory prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling on sajdah sahw when recitation is omitted.

Core Idea
In the last two rak'ahs, recitation is not obligatory; silence is permitted, and no sajdah sahw is required.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on the last two rak'ahs of obligatory prayer. While the first two rak'ahs require Fatiha recitation, the last two offer flexibility. The text explains the three permissible options and the key consequence: no sajdah sahw is needed if recitation is left out.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three options
Read the text and list the three choices: recite, glorify (tasbih), or remain silent.
Silence is limited to the duration of three tasbihs.
2
Understand the time limit
Note that both tasbih and silence are defined by the time it takes to say 'Subhanallah' three times.
This prevents indefinite silence.
3
Derive the ruling on sajdah sahw
Since recitation in the last two rak'ahs is not wajib, omitting it does not require sajdah sahw, according to the apparent riwayah.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Note the preferred option
Although any option is permissible, reciting the Fatiha is afdal (best).
Al-Nihayah confirms that recitation means the Fatiha.
5
Recognize the authority
The ruling is from the apparent riwayah (zahir al-riwayah), as stated in Al-Hidayah and Al-Nihayah.
This is the established transmission of the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وهو مُخيَّر في الأخريين: إن شاء قرأ، وإن شاء سبح، وإن شاء سكت) : يعني مقدار ما يمكن أن يقول فيه ثلاث تسبيحات. ولهذا: لا يجب السهو بترك القراءة فيهما، في ظاهر الرواية. كذا في «الهداية» (١). إلا أن الأفضل أن يقرأ فيهما الفاتحة. قال في «النهاية»: إن شاء قرأ: الفاتحة، يعني وإن شاء سبح: يعني ثلاث تسبيحات، وإن شاء سكت يعني مقدار ما يمكن أن يقول فيه ثلاث تسبيحات.
His saying: 'And he is given a choice in the last two: if he wishes he recites, if he wishes he glorifies, if he wishes he remains silent': meaning the amount in which he can say three glorifications. And for this reason, forgetfulness prostration is not required upon leaving recitation in them, in the apparent narration. So it is in Al-Hidayah. Except that the best is to recite the Fatiha in them. He said in Al-Nihayah: if he wishes he recites the Fatiha, meaning, and if he wishes he glorifies, meaning three glorifications, and if he wishes he remains silent, meaning the amount in which he can say three glorifications.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage clarifies the matn's statement about the last two rak'ahs of obligatory prayer. The worshiper has a choice: recite (preferably the Fatiha), say tasbih (three times), or remain silent (for the duration of three tasbihs). Consequently, if one omits recitation, no prostration for forgetfulness (sajdah sahw) is required, according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). However, it is better (afdal) to recite the Fatiha. The commentator quotes Al-Nihayah for the exact definitions of each option.

Key Terms
تسبيح (tasbih): Glorification of Allah, specifically saying 'Subhanallah'
سهو (sahw): Forgetfulness prostration (sajdah al-sahw) required for leaving an obligatory element

Key Takeaway
In the last two rak'ahs of obligatory prayer, the worshiper has three choices: recite, glorify, or remain silent (limited to three tasbihs), and omitting recitation does not require sajdah sahw.

Choice in the Last Two Rak'ahs of Supererogatory Prayer
Ruling on the options in last two rak'ahs with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three permissible actions in the last two rak'ahs of a supererogatory prayer and explain the Hanafi proof from the hadith 'No prayer except with recitation.'

Core Idea
Recitation in the last two rak'ahs is optional; silence is allowed but sinful if deliberate.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explains the ruling of the last two rak'ahs in supererogatory (nafl) prayers. The matn grants the worshipper a choice: recite al-Fatiha, glorify Allah, or remain silent. The commentary clarifies that the best practice is to recite, and that omission of recitation does not require prostration of forgetfulness. The proof is drawn from the hadith 'No prayer except with recitation,' which is interpreted to mean a complete prayer of two rak'ahs, thereby confining the obligation of recitation to the first two rak'ahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Identify the act as the last two rak'ahs of a supererogatory prayer. Determine the ruling: the worshipper has a choice (mukhayyar) between reciting al-Fatiha, glorifying, or remaining silent.
The choice is only valid if the silence is for the duration of three tasbihat.
2
Locate the primary proof
Find the hadith 'No prayer except with recitation.' The commentator uses this to argue that 'prayer' in the absolute sense refers to a complete two-rak'ah unit, so recitation is only required in the first two rak'ahs of a supererogatory prayer.
The legal analogy (qiyas) is made with an oath: one who swears 'not to pray a prayer' only breaks the oath after two rak'ahs.
3
Understand the consequence of omission
Note that abandoning recitation in these two rak'ahs does not require sajdah al-sahw according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). The best practice is still to recite al-Fatiha.
This is a key Hanafi distinction: sunnah omission does not entail sahw.
4
Analyze the hadith's indication (wajh al-dalalah)
The hadith uses the absolute term 'prayer.' In Hanafi usul, an absolute command implies obligation only when it refers to the complete act. Here, the complete nafl prayer is two rak'ahs, so recitation is wajib in the first two and sunnah in the last two.
The Shafi'i school reads this hadith differently, requiring recitation in every rak'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
وهو مُخيَّر في الأخريين : إن شاء قرأ الفاتحة، وإن شاء سبح، وإن شاء سكت.
وصفة القراءة في الجهر والإخفاء، وفي قدر القراءة: فلا يلحقان بهما. وأما قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لا صلاة إلا بقراءة» : فهو شاهد لنا ؛ لأنه ذَكَرَ الصلاة مطلقاً، والصلاة متى ذُكرت مطلقة: لا تنصرف إلى ركعة، وإنما تنصرف إلى صلاة كاملة، وهي ركعتان عرفاً، كمن حلف: لا يصلي صلاة: فإنه لا يحنث حتى يصلي ركعتين. بخلاف ما إذا حلف لا يصلي، ولم يقل: صلاةً: فإنه يحنث إذا صلى ركعة.
قوله: (وهو مُخيَّر في الأخريين: إن شاء قرأ، وإن شاء سبح، وإن شاء سكت) : يعني مقدار ما يمكن أن يقول فيه ثلاث تسبيحات. ولهذا: لا يجب السهو بترك القراءة فيهما، في ظاهر الرواية. كذا في «الهداية». إلا أن الأفضل أن يقرأ فيهما الفاتحة.
قال في «النهاية»: إن شاء قرأ: الفاتحة، يعني وإن شاء سبح: يعني ثلاث تسبيحات، وإن شاء سكت يعني مقدار ما يمكن أن يقول فيه ثلاث تسبيحات.
فإذا لم يقرأ، ولم يسبح كان مسيئاً إن تعمد السكوت، وإن كان ساهياً: فالأصح أنه لا يجب عليه سهو.
* قوله : وإن شاء سكت هذا عند أبي يوسف، فإن السكوت عنده: ليس بإساءة، وعندهما: إساءة.
وعند بعضهم كراهة والكراهة أفحش من الإساءة، فالقراءة سنة، والتسبيح مباح، والسكوت إساءة.
Chapter of supererogatory prayers. And he has a choice in the last two: if he wishes, he recites al-Fatiha; if he wishes, he glorifies; if he wishes, he remains silent. And the description of recitation regarding loudness and quietness, and regarding the amount of recitation: they are not attached to them. And as for his statement, peace and blessings be upon him: 'No prayer except with recitation' is a witness for us; because he mentioned prayer absolutely, and when prayer is mentioned absolutely it does not refer to one rak'ah, but rather it refers to a complete prayer, which is two rak'ahs customarily, like one who swears: he will not pray a prayer - then he does not break his oath until he prays two rak'ahs. Unlike if he swears he will not pray, and did not say 'a prayer' - then he breaks his oath if he prays one rak'ah. His statement: (And he has a choice in the last two: if he wishes, he recites; if he wishes, he glorifies; if he wishes, he remains silent) means the duration in which three tasbihat can be said. For this reason, the prostration of forgetfulness is not obligatory for abandoning recitation in them, in the apparent narration. Thus in al-Hidayah. Except that the best is to recite al-Fatiha in them. He said in al-Nihayah: If he wishes he recites al-Fatiha, meaning; and if he wishes he glorifies, meaning three tasbihat; and if he wishes he remains silent, meaning the duration in which three tasbihat can be said. Then if he does not recite and does not glorify, he is sinful if he deliberately remains silent; and if he is forgetful, the most correct view is that prostration of forgetfulness is not obligatory on him. * His statement: 'If he wishes he remains silent' is according to Abu Yusuf, for silence according to him is not a sin, but according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) it is a sin. And according to some there is dislike, and dislike is more severe than sin. So recitation is sunnah, glorification is permissible, and silence is sinful.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on supererogatory prayers (nawafil) regarding the choice (takhyir) the worshipper has in the last two rak'ahs of a supererogatory prayer. The matn states that one may either recite Surah al-Fatiha, glorify Allah (tasbih), or remain silent. The commentator clarifies that silence means remaining silent for the duration of saying three tasbihat (subhanallah). The ruling is that recitation is not obligatory in these rak'ahs; therefore, if one omits recitation, no prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) is required, according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). The best practice is to recite al-Fatiha. The passage then considers the case where one neither recites nor glorifies: if done intentionally, it is sinful (isaa); if forgetful, no sajdah is required. The commentary includes an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Yusuf, silence is not sinful, but according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two) it is sinful. Some scholars consider it makruh (disliked), which is worse than sinful. Thus, the hierarchy: recitation is sunnah, tasbih is mubah (permissible), and silence is sinful (unless one follows Abu Yusuf's view). The proof for the ruling is the hadith 'No prayer except with recitation,' which is used to argue that the absolute mention of prayer refers to a complete prayer of two rak'ahs, and since the two rak'ahs are complete, recitation is only required in the first two rak'ahs of a supererogatory prayer, leaving the last two optional.

Key Terms
مُخيَّر (mukhayyar): Having a choice between three options: reciting Fatiha, glorifying Allah, or remaining silent.
السكوت (al-sukut): Remaining silent for the duration of approximately three tasbihat, without reciting or glorifying.
السهو (al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) performed to compensate for certain omissions in prayer.
الإساءة (al-isaa): Sinful action; doing something blameworthy though not necessarily invalidating the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting al-Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs of a supererogatory prayer?
A) It is obligatory (fard).
B) It is a recommended sunnah.
C) It is forbidden (haram).
D) It is permissible but disliked (makruh).

Key Takeaway
In the last two rak'ahs of a supererogatory prayer, recitation is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory; the best is to recite al-Fatiha.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Is Silence in the Last Two Rak'ahs Sinful?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sinfulness of silence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) regarding the sinfulness of intentional silence in the last two rak'ahs of nafl, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Intentional silence without recitation or glorification is sinful (isaa) according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but not according to Abu Yusuf.

The previous lesson established that the worshipper has a choice in the last two rak'ahs. However, a nuanced dispute arises within the Hanafi school when the worshipper deliberately remains silent without any dhikr. This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira details the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Understanding this dispute helps in applying the correct ruling for fatwa and clarifies the hierarchy of choices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The issue is whether it is sinful (isaa) to intentionally remain silent in the last two rak'ahs of a supererogatory prayer without reciting al-Fatiha or glorifying Allah. Note that the silence must be for the duration of three tasbihat.
If one glorifies even once, it is not silence, so the dispute only applies to complete silence.
2
State the position of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad)
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, such intentional silence is sinful (isaa). They consider it a neglect of the recommended act of dhikr, and the person is blameworthy.
Some Hanafi scholars even consider it makruh (disliked), which is more severe than isaa.
3
State the position of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that silence is not sinful. Since recitation is not obligatory in these rak'ahs, remaining silent is permissible without sin.
Abu Yusuf's reasoning is based on the optional nature of the last two rak'ahs.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that intentional silence is sinful (isaa), following the majority of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. However, one may follow Abu Yusuf's view if there is a need (darurah).
The commentator leans towards the view that silence is sinful, as he mentions that karahah (dislike) is even more severe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
وهو مُخيَّر في الأخريين : إن شاء قرأ الفاتحة، وإن شاء سبح، وإن شاء سكت.
وصفة القراءة في الجهر والإخفاء، وفي قدر القراءة: فلا يلحقان بهما. وأما قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لا صلاة إلا بقراءة» : فهو شاهد لنا ؛ لأنه ذَكَرَ الصلاة مطلقاً، والصلاة متى ذُكرت مطلقة: لا تنصرف إلى ركعة، وإنما تنصرف إلى صلاة كاملة، وهي ركعتان عرفاً، كمن حلف: لا يصلي صلاة: فإنه لا يحنث حتى يصلي ركعتين. بخلاف ما إذا حلف لا يصلي، ولم يقل: صلاةً: فإنه يحنث إذا صلى ركعة.
قوله: (وهو مُخيَّر في الأخريين: إن شاء قرأ، وإن شاء سبح، وإن شاء سكت) : يعني مقدار ما يمكن أن يقول فيه ثلاث تسبيحات. ولهذا: لا يجب السهو بترك القراءة فيهما، في ظاهر الرواية. كذا في «الهداية». إلا أن الأفضل أن يقرأ فيهما الفاتحة.
قال في «النهاية»: إن شاء قرأ: الفاتحة، يعني وإن شاء سبح: يعني ثلاث تسبيحات، وإن شاء سكت يعني مقدار ما يمكن أن يقول فيه ثلاث تسبيحات.
فإذا لم يقرأ، ولم يسبح كان مسيئاً إن تعمد السكوت، وإن كان ساهياً: فالأصح أنه لا يجب عليه سهو.

وعند بعضهم كراهة والكراهة أفحش من الإساءة، فالقراءة سنة، والتسبيح مباح، والسكوت إساءة.

Obligation of Recitation in All Rak'ahs of Nafl and Witr
Ruling with reasoning on recitation in nafl and witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in supererogatory (nafl) and witr prayers and explain the reasoning using qiyas and ihtiyat.

Core Idea
Recitation is wajib in every rak'ah of nafl (each pair is a separate prayer) and witr (precaution due to its dual nature).

In this passage, the commentator explains why recitation (qira'ah) is obligatory in every rak'ah of supererogatory (nafl) and witr prayers. While many students know recitation is required in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers, the ruling for other prayers differs. The Hanafi school bases its rule on careful reasoning: for nafl, each two-rak'ah pair is a complete prayer, so the third rak'ah is like a new prayer; for witr, precaution (ihtiyat) is applied because witr shares characteristics of both fard and nafl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules that recitation (qira'ah) is wajib (obligatory) in every rak'ah of supererogatory (nafl) prayers and in every rak'ah of witr prayer. Note that this is wajib, not fard.
Wajib means omission requires sajdah al-sahw, not repetition of the prayer.
2
Examine the proof for nafl
Each pair (shaf') of nafl is considered a separate prayer. When you stand for the third rak'ah, it is like an initiating takbir (tahrimah). Therefore, you must recite, and you also recite the opening supplication (istiftah) and seek refuge (ta'awwudh).
This is a qiyas: the third rak'ah in a four-rak'ah nafl is analogous to the first rak'ah of a new prayer.
3
Examine the proof for witr
Witr is ambiguous (mutaraddad) between fard and nafl because it has signs of both. To be safe, the jurists made recitation obligatory in all three rak'ahs by precaution (ihtiyat).
Precaution is used when legal status is unclear, especially in worship.
4
Note the distinctions between nafl and witr
In nafl, you recite istiftah and ta'awwudh in the third rak'ah. In witr, you do not recite them in the third rak'ah, nor do you complete the first tashahhud after two rak'ahs, because witr resembles fard.
These distinctions show that the wajib ruling is the same, but other details differ due to witr's resemblance to fard.
5
Understand the thamarah (practical consequence)
The ruling means that in any nafl prayer of more than two rak'ahs, recitation is required in every rak'ah. For witr, the same applies. Omission of recitation in any rak'ah requires sajdah al-sahw.
This is different from fard prayers, where recitation is fard only in the first two rak'ahs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والقراءة واجبة في جميع ركعات النفل، وفي جميع الوتر). أما النفل : فلأن كل شفع منه صلاةٌ على حدة، والقيام إلى الثالثة كتحريمة مبتدأة، ولهذا يستفتح فيها، ويتعوذ.
وأما الوتر : فللاحتياط ؛ لأنه متردد بين الفرض والنفل؛ لوجود علامة الأمرين، فاحتاطوا له بإيجاب القراءة ؛ لاحتمال أن يكون نفلاً، ولا يستفتح في الثالثة منه، ولا يتعوذ ، ولا يُكمل تشهده الأول؛ لشبهه بالفرض.
His statement: (And recitation is obligatory in all rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer, and in all of witr). As for supererogatory: because each pair from it is a separate prayer, and standing for the third is like an initiating takbir, and for this reason he makes the opening supplication (istiftah) and seeks refuge (ta'awwudh) in it. And as for witr: for precaution; because it is between obligatory and supererogatory, due to the presence of signs of both matters, so they acted cautiously for it by making recitation obligatory, due to the possibility that it may be supererogatory; and he does not make the opening supplication in its third rak'ah, nor seek refuge, nor complete the first tashahhud, due to its resemblance to the obligatory.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the commentary on the matn, stating that recitation (qira'ah) is obligatory (wajib) in all rak'ahs of supererogatory (nafl) prayers and in all rak'ahs of the witr prayer. The commentator provides the reason for each. For supererogatory prayers: each pair (shaf') is considered as a separate prayer in itself. Therefore, when one rises to the third rak'ah, it is like a new initiation (tahrimah), and thus the worshipper recites the opening supplication (istiftah) and seeks refuge (ta'awwudh) at the start of the third rak'ah. This indicates that recitation is required in every rak'ah because each rak'ah pair is independent. For witr: the ruling is precautionary (ihtiyat) because witr shares characteristics of both fard and nafl. Since it is a prayer with a specific number (odd) but not obligatory like fard, the jurists made recitation obligatory in all its rak'ahs to be safe, in case it is considered like nafl. However, unlike nafl, the worshipper does not recite the opening supplication or seek refuge in the third rak'ah, nor does he complete the first tashahhud after two rak'ahs, because witr resembles the fard in some aspects. Thus, recitation is wajib in every rak'ah of both nafl and witr, but other details differ.

Key Terms
الشفع (al-shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs in supererogatory prayer; each two rak'ahs constitute a separate unit of prayer.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): The principle of precaution; when the legal status is ambiguous, the stricter or more cautious ruling is applied.
متردد (mutaraddad): Something that has characteristics of two categories; witr is between fard and nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is recitation obligatory in all rak'ahs of supererogatory (nafl) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because nafl is like fard.
B) Because each pair is a separate prayer.
C) Because the Prophet always recited in every rak'ah.
D) Because of precaution (ihtiyat).

Key Takeaway
Recitation is wajib in every rak'ah of supererogatory and witr prayers, based on qiyas and ihtiyat respectively.

Making Up an Invalidated Supererogatory Prayer: Intention and Number of Rak'ahs
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on making up invalidated nafl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which making up an invalidated nafl prayer is required and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of rak'ahs to be made up.

Core Idea
A supererogatory prayer invalidated after intentional entry must be made up, but only the first two rak'ahs count—even if you intended a hundred.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira clarifies the ruling on qada of nafl prayers. It distinguishes between intentional and forgetful entry, and then addresses a subtle dispute: how many rak'ahs must one make up if the intention was for a large number? The Hanafi school’s majority view limits the obligation to just the first pair.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is invalidating a supererogatory prayer after entering it. The ruling is that it must be made up (qada) if the entry was intentional.
This is the matn's basic statement.
2
Distinguish intentional vs forgetful entry
If one entered forgetfully, e.g., mistakenly standing for a fifth rak'ah, then invalidating does not require qada. The intention at entry is key.
Forgetful entry negates the obligation.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two) hold that only two rak'ahs are binding regardless of intended number. Abu Yusuf holds that the intended number becomes binding.
The dispute is on the scope of obligation after invalidation.
4
Understand the dalil for the majority view
Each pair of nafl is a separate prayer; intention for more rak'ahs does not bind beyond the first pair because nafl is not continuous like fard.
The default in nafl is that each two rak'ahs complete.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the two: only two rak'ahs must be made up, regardless of intention.
This is the position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* قوله: (ومن دخل في صلاة نفل، ثم أفسدها : قضاها).
هذا إذا دخل فيها قصداً، أما إذا دخل ساهياً، كما إذا قام إلى الخامسة ساهياً، ثم أفسدها: لا يقضيها.
ثم أيضاً لا يلزمه إلا ركعتان وإن نوى مائة ركعة عندهما، خلافاً لأبي يوسف.
* His statement: (And whoever enters a supererogatory prayer, then invalidates it: he makes it up). This is if he entered it intentionally. But if he entered forgetfully, as when he stands for the fifth rak'ah forgetfully, then invalidates it: he does not make it up. Then also, only two rak'ahs are binding upon him, even if he intended one hundred rak'ahs, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the obligation to make up (qada) a supererogatory prayer that has been invalidated. The matn states that if one enters a supererogatory prayer and then invalidates it, he must make it up. The commentator adds conditions: this applies only if one entered intentionally. If the entry was forgetful, such as mistakenly standing for a fifth rak'ah (thinking it is the fourth) and then invalidating the prayer, he is not required to make it up. This is because the nafl prayer was not intended from the start. The passage then includes an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of rak'ahs that must be made up. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), only two rak'ahs are obligatory, even if one had intended to pray a large number (e.g., one hundred rak'ahs). This is because each pair of rak'ahs in nafl is considered a separate prayer, and the invalidation of the entire prayer is treated as invalidating only the first pair. Abu Yusuf differs: he holds that whatever number one intended becomes wajib to make up. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the two: only two rak'ahs are required.

Key Terms
أفسدها (afsadahā): Invalidated the prayer; nullified it, e.g., by speaking or breaking wudu while in prayer.
قضاها (qadāhā): Make it up; perform it again after the fact as a substitute for the invalidated prayer.
ساهياً (sāhiyan): Forgetfully; without intention, e.g., mistakenly standing for an extra rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone intentionally enters a supererogatory prayer intending to pray 20 rak'ahs but invalidates it after 4 rak'ahs, how many rak'ahs must he make up according to the majority of Hanafi imams?
A) 20 rak'ahs, as he intended.
B) 4 rak'ahs, since that is what he performed.
C) 2 rak'ahs, because only the first pair is binding.
D) None, because supererogatory prayers are voluntary.

Key Takeaway
Making up an invalidated supererogatory prayer is wajib only if entered intentionally, and only the first two rak'ahs are binding regardless of intention.

Recitation is Wajib in All Rak'ats of Nafl and Witr
Ruling on recitation in nafl and witr with legal reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that recitation is wajib in every rak'ah of nafl and witr, and explain the legal reasoning (qiyas and ihtiyat) that supports this obligation.

Core Idea
Recitation is wajib in every rak'ah of nafl and witr due to structural analogy and precaution.

This lesson examines the ruling on recitation (qira'ah) in supererogatory (nafl) and witr prayers. While many assume recitation is only required in the first two rak'ats, the Hanafi school holds it is obligatory in all rak'ats of these prayers. The reasoning combines qiyas (analogy) based on the structure of nafl and ihtiyat (precaution) due to witr's ambiguous nature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Identify that the act in question is recitation (qira'ah) during prayer. The ruling is that recitation is wajib in all rak'ats of both nafl and witr. Note that the hukm level is wajib, not fard.
Wajib means obligatory but proven by zanni evidence; fard is proven by qat'i evidence.
2
Analyze the Reasoning for Nafl
For nafl, the text says each pair (shaf') of rak'ats is a separate prayer. Standing for the third rak'ah is like a new takbir (tahrimah), indicating the start of a new unit. Therefore, like the first rak'ah of any prayer, recitation is required in each new unit.
This is qiyas: each pair of nafl is analogized to Fajr prayer, which requires recitation in its two rak'ats.
3
Analyze the Reasoning for Witr
For witr, the text uses the principle of ihtiyat (precaution). Witr shares characteristics of both fard (e.g., it is linked to 'isha and has a specific time) and nafl (e.g., it is odd-numbered and can be performed individually). To ensure it is valid, recitation is made wajib in all its rak'ats.
If witr were nafl, recitation would be required per the nafl rule; if it were fard, recitation would be required in all rak'ats anyway (as per the school). So precaution ensures obligation.
4
Contrast the Treatment of the Third Rak'ah
Despite making recitation wajib in all rak'ats of witr, the text notes that one does not recite isti'adhah in the third rak'ah nor complete the first tashahhud, because witr resembles fard in some aspects. This shows the reasoning is nuanced.
This nuance reflects the balance between its nafl-like and fard-like aspects.
5
Determine the Authority and Applicability
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and agreed upon by the three Hanafi imams. It is mufta bihi. Some other schools may allow optional recitation in nafl, but the Hanafi position is clear and based on strong analogy.
Understanding this ruling helps avoid common errors in performing nafl and witr prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل. والقراءة واجبة في جميع ركعات النفل، وفي جميع الوتر. أما النفل : فلأن كل شفع منه صلاةٌ على حدة، والقيام إلى الثالثة كتحريمة مبتدأة، ولهذا يستفتح فيها، ويتعوذ. وأما الوتر : فللاحتياط ; لأنه متردد بين الفرض والنفل; لوجود علامة الأمرين، فاحتاطوا له بإيجاب القراءة ; لاحتمال أن يكون نفلاً، ولا يستفتح في الثالثة منه، ولا يتعوذ ، ولا يُكمل تشهده الأول; لشبهه بالفرض.
Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers. Recitation is obligatory in all rak'ats of nafl and in all rak'ats of witr. As for nafl: because every pair (shaf') from it is a prayer on its own, and standing for the third rak'ah is like an initiating takbir (tahrima), and for this reason one seeks refuge and recites the isti'adhah in it. As for witr: out of precaution, because it is ambiguous between obligatory and supererogatory, due to the presence of signs of both, so they exercised caution by making recitation obligatory, due to the possibility that it is nafl. And one does not seek refuge or recite isti'adhah in the third rak'ah, nor does one complete the first tashahhud, because of its resemblance to obligatory prayers.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on supererogatory prayers states the ruling that recitation (qira'ah) is wajib in all rak'ats of nafl (supererogatory) prayers and in all rak'ats of witr prayer. The commentator then provides the legal reasoning (ta'lil) for this ruling. For nafl, each pair of rak'ats (shaf') is considered a separate prayer unit. Thus, when one stands for the third rak'ah, it is as if one is initiating a new prayer with a new takbir (tahrima). Hence, one recites the opening supplication (isti'adhah) and seeks refuge. For witr, the precaution (ihtiyat) is applied because witr has characteristics of both fard and nafl; to ensure it is performed correctly, recitation is made wajib in all its rak'ats. However, due to its resemblance to fard, one does not recite isti'adhah in the third rak'ah, nor does one complete the first tashahhud. The ruling is based on qiyas (analogy) and ihtiyat, not on a direct textual command, which is why it is classified as wajib rather than fard.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayer, voluntary acts of worship beyond the obligatory.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after the night prayer, which is wajib in the Hanafi school.
الشفع (al-shaf'): A pair of rak'ats; in the context of nafl, each two rak'ats form a separate prayer unit.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) that initiates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is recitation wajib in all rak'ats of witr?
A) Because witr is considered fard.
B) Out of precaution (ihtiyat) due to its resemblance to both fard and nafl.
C) Because the Prophet ﷺ explicitly commanded it.
D) Because witr has no resemblance to nafl.

Key Takeaway
Recitation in all rak'ats of nafl and witr is wajib based on qiyas (each pair is a separate prayer) and ihtiyat (witr's ambiguous nature).

Ruling on Silence in Supererogatory Prayer
Intra-madhhab dispute on silence in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on silence in supererogatory prayer and distinguish between the positions of Abu Yusuf and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).

Core Idea
Silence in nafl prayer without recitation or tasbih is sinful according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, but Abu Yusuf permits it.

This passage explores an intra-Hanafi dispute: is it sinful to remain silent in supererogatory prayer without reciting Qur’an or performing tasbih? The position of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) says it is sinful (isa'ah), while Abu Yusuf alone says it is permissible. The passage also addresses the case of forgetful silence and notes that some scholars consider it makruh (disliked), which is even more severe. Understanding this difference helps you apply the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? Remaining silent in supererogatory prayer without recitation or tasbih. What is the basic ruling? The text states 'recitation is sunnah, tasbih is mubah, and silence is sinful.'
2
State the position of the two (Sahibayn)
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two), silence is sinful (isa'ah). This is the position reported in Zahir al-Riwayah.
The two = Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
State Abu Yusuf’s position
According to Abu Yusuf alone, silence is not sinful; it is permissible, based on the matn phrase 'And if he wishes, he may remain silent.'
Some scholars also hold it to be makruh (disliked), which is worse than isa'ah.
4
Identify the thamarah (practical consequence)
Abu Yusuf: no sin; the two: sin incurred. In both views, the prayer is still valid because recitation is sunnah, not wajib.
The difference only affects whether one incurs sin, not the validity of the prayer.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that silence is sinful (isa'ah), as indicated by the final sentence of the passage.
The commentator implicitly prefers the view of the two.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا لم يقرأ، ولم يسبح كان مسيئاً إن تعمد السكوت، وإن كان ساهياً: فالأصح أنه لا يجب عليه سهو. * قوله : وإن شاء سكت هذا عند أبي يوسف، فإن السكوت عنده: ليس بإساءة، وعندهما: إساءة. وعند بعضهم كراهة والكراهة أفحش من الإساءة، فالقراءة سنة، والتسبيح مباح، والسكوت إساءة.
If one neither recites nor glorifies (tasbih), he is sinful if he intentionally remains silent. But if he is forgetful, the correct view is that no prostration of forgetfulness is required. 'And if he wishes, he may remain silent.' This according to Abu Yusuf, for silence in his view is not sinful. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is sinful. According to some, it is makruh (disliked) and makruh is worse than sinfulness. So recitation is sunnah, tasbih is mubah (permissible), and silence is sinful.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on remaining silent in supererogatory prayer when one neither recites nor performs tasbih. The preferred view (al-asahh) is that if one intentionally remains silent, he is sinful (musi'). If he does so forgetfully, no prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) is required. The commentator then clarifies an intra-madhhab dispute by quoting the matn phrase 'And if he wishes, he may remain silent.' According to Abu Yusuf, silence is not sinful; it is permissible. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), silence is sinful. Some scholars hold it to be makruh (disliked), which is even more severe than simple sinfulness. The final relied-upon position (mu'tamad) is that recitation is sunnah, tasbih is mubah, and silence is sinful. This means that in supererogatory prayer, one should either recite or do tasbih; remaining completely silent without reason is considered sinful.

Key Terms
السكوت (al-sukut): Remaining silent in prayer without reciting Qur'an or performing any dhikr or tasbih.
الإساءة (al-isa'ah): Sinfulness or doing something blameworthy that does not invalidate the prayer but is makruh tahrimi.
الكراهة (al-karahah): Dislike; a ruling that the act is undesirable. In this context, some consider it worse than isa'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Sunnah (recommended)
C) Isa'ah (sinful)
D) Wajib (obligatory)

Key Takeaway
In supererogatory prayer, one should either recite or do tasbih; remaining completely silent intentionally is considered sinful in the relied-upon Hanafi view.
