Making Up an Invalidated Supererogatory Prayer
Ruling on qada for invalidated nafl prayer with conditions and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for an invalidated nafl prayer and distinguish between the positions of Abu Yusuf and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the number of rak'ats required.

Core Idea
If you invalidate a nafl prayer entered intentionally, you must make it up—but only two rak'ats, no matter how many you intended.

This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayrah addresses a common scenario: a person enters a nafl prayer but then invalidates it. The ruling is not straightforward—it depends on whether the entry was intentional or forgetful, and there is a dispute among the Hanafi imams about the extent of the makeup. Understanding this dispute strengthens your grasp of the Hanafi treatment of supererogatory acts and the principle that each pair in nafl is an independent prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is entering a nafl prayer and then invalidating it. The ruling is that it must be made up (qada) if entered intentionally.
2
Note the exception for forgetfulness
If entered forgetfully, no qada is required. The passage gives the example of standing for a fifth rak'ah forgetfully.
Forgetfulness (sahw) often exempts from obligations in prayer.
3
State the intra-Hanafi dispute
The dispute is over how many rak'ats must be made up. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say only two rak'ats, regardless of intention. Abu Yusuf says one must make up the number intended.
The two refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
4
Identify the underlying principle
The two base their view on the principle that each pair in nafl is a separate prayer. Invalidating the first pair does not obligate the whole.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the two, i.e., only two rak'ats are required.
The text implies this by stating 'عندهما' (according to the two) and then 'خلافاً لأبي يوسف'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومن دخل في صلاة نفل، ثم أفسدها : قضاها). هذا إذا دخل فيها قصداً، أما إذا دخل ساهياً، كما إذا قام إلى الخامسة ساهياً، ثم أفسدها: لا يقضيها. ثم أيضاً لا يلزمه إلا ركعتان وإن نوى مائة ركعة عندهما، خلافاً لأبي يوسف.
His saying: (Whoever enters a supererogatory prayer and then invalidates it, must make it up). This applies if he entered intentionally. However, if he entered forgetfully, such as standing for a fifth rak'ah forgetfully and then invalidates it, he does not make it up. Also, he is only obliged to perform two rak'ats even if he intended a hundred, according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage addresses the case of a person who enters a supererogatory (nafl) prayer and then invalidates it. The ruling is that he must make it up (qada), but this applies only if he entered intentionally. If he entered forgetfully—for example, by mistakenly standing for a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'at prayer—and then invalidates it, he is not required to make it up. Additionally, there is a dispute regarding the extent of the required makeup. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), only two rak'ats are required regardless of the number intended, even if one intended a hundred rak'ats. According to Abu Yusuf, one must make up the number intended. The relied-upon position (mu'tamad) is that of the two, i.e., only two rak'ats are necessary, because each pair of rak'ats in nafl is considered a separate prayer; invalidating the first pair does not obligate completion of the entire intended number.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada'): Making up a prayer that was invalidated or missed after its time.
الساهي (al-sahi): The forgetful person; if one enters nafl forgetfully and invalidates it, no qada is required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 2 rak'ats
C) 4 rak'ats
D) 0 rak'ats

Key Takeaway
When you invalidate a nafl prayer entered intentionally, you must make up only two rak'ats, as each pair is an independent prayer, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Qada of Nafl Prayer After Sitting: Two or Four Rak'ats?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada of nafl after sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi Hanafi ruling on qada of invalidated nafl prayer after sitting and distinguish between the views of Abu Yusuf and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).

Core Idea
In nafl, each pair of rak'ats is an independent prayer unit; sitting after two completes the first pair.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in supererogatory prayer: if one prays four rak'ats, sits for tashahhud after the first two, and then invalidates the last two, how many rak'ats must be made up? The Hanafi school has an intra-madhhab dispute on this point. Understanding the reasoning behind each position sharpens your grasp of how the school treats nafl prayer structure and the role of intention (shuru').

Guided Path
1
State the Scenario
Identify the exact conditions: a four-rak'at nafl, sitting after two for tashahhud, then invalidation of the last two rak'ats (either by action or external factor).
The invalidation can occur by the person's act (e.g., breaking wudu) or externally (e.g., menstruation).
2
Identify the Relied-Upon Ruling
According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), only two rak'ats are made up. The first pair is considered complete upon sitting, and the second pair is a separate prayer.
The text says: 'قضى ركعتين' (he makes up two rak'ats) as the default ruling.
3
Follow the Proof for the Two's View
The proof: 'الشفع الأول قد تم' (the first pair has been completed) and 'القيام إلى الثالثة بمنزلة تحريمة مبتدأة' (standing for the third is like a new initiating takbir). Thus the second pair is independent.
This relies on the Hanafi principle that nafl is prayed in pairs, each requiring its own takbir.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's Opposition
Abu Yusuf holds that all four rak'ats must be made up. His reasoning: 'اعتباراً للشروع بالنذر' (considering the commencement as a vow). The entire prayer is a single unit once commenced.
He analogizes the intention to perform four rak'ats to a vow (nadhr), making the full number binding.
5
Determine the Practical Difference (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
If one sat after two and invalidates the last two: Abu Yusuf requires qada of four; the two require only two. If no sit, both agree on four.
The text mentions consensus on the no-sit case: 'لو لم يقعد، وأفسد الأُخريين: لزمه قضاء أربع، إجماعاً'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن صلى أربع ركعات، وقَعَدَ في الأوليين مقدار التشهد، ثم أفسد الأخريين : قضى ركعتين. وقوله : أفسدها سواء أفسدت بفعله أو بغير فعله، كالمتيمم يرى الماء وما أشبهه، وكالمرأة إذا حاضت في التطوع: يجب القضاء، بخلاف الفرض. * قوله: (فإن صلى أربع ركعات، وقعد في الأوليين مقدار التشهد، ثم أفسد الأخريين: قضى ركعتين); لأن الشفع الأول قد تم، والقيام إلى الثالثة بمنزلة تحريمة مبتدأة: فيكون ملزماً. ثم وهذا إذا أفسد الأخريين بعد الشروع فيهما، بأن قام إلى الثالثة، أفسدها، أما إذا أفسدها قبل القيام: لا يجب عليه قضاء الأُخريين; لأنه أفسد قبل الشروع في الشفع الثاني. وعن أبي يوسف: يقضي; اعتباراً للشروع بالنذر. وقيد بقوله : وقعد ; لأنه لو لم يقعد، وأفسد الأُخريين: لزمه قضاء أربع، إجماعاً. * قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف: يقضي أربعاً)). وهو احتياط; لأنها بمنزلة صلاة واحدة، حتى إن الزوج لو خير امرأته وهي في الشفع الأول، أو أخبرت بشفعة لها، فأتمت أربعاً: لا تبطل شفعتها، ولا خيارها. كذا في «النهاية».
If he prays four rak'ats and sits in the first two for the measure of tashahhud, then invalidates the last two, he makes up two rak'ats. And his saying: 'invalidates it' equally applies whether it is invalidated by his action or not by his action, like a mutayammim seeing water and the like, and like a woman who menstruates during a supererogatory prayer: qada is obligatory, unlike in fard. * His saying: (If he prays four rak'ats, and sits in the first two for the measure of tashahhud, then invalidates the last two: he makes up two rak'ats) because the first pair (shaf') has been completed, and standing for the third is like an initiating takbir, so it becomes binding. Then this is if he invalidates the last two after commencing them, by standing for the third and invalidating it. But if he invalidates them before standing, he is not required to make up the last two, because he invalidated before commencing the second pair. And from Abu Yusuf: he makes up, considering the commencement as a vow. And he restricted the ruling by saying 'and sits' because if he did not sit and invalidated the last two, he would be obliged to make up four, by consensus. * His saying: (And Abu Yusuf said: he makes up four). It is precautionary, because they are like one prayer, to the extent that if a husband gives his wife a choice while she is in the first pair, or she is informed of a pre-emption right while in it, and she completes four, her right to pre-emption and her right of choice are not invalidated. Thus in al-Nihayah.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage details a specific scenario in supererogatory prayer: if one prays four rak'ats, sits for tashahhud after the first two, and then invalidates the last two, only two rak'ats are to be made up. The reason is that the first pair is considered complete once one sits for tashahhud, and standing for the third is like starting a new prayer with a new takbir. Therefore, the last two are a separate unit. However, if one invalidates the last two before standing for the third, no qada is required for them because the second pair had not yet commenced. If one does not sit after the first two (i.e., stands directly for the third without sitting), then invalidating the last two requires making up all four rak'ats, by consensus. There is a difference of opinion: Abu Yusuf holds that one must make up four rak'ats, treating the entire four as a single prayer. He analogizes the commencement of the prayer to a vow (nadhr), which makes the full intended number binding. The relied-upon view is that of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): only two rak'ats are made up when sitting occurs, but if no sit, four. The ruling applies whether the invalidation occurs by an act of the person or by external factors, such as a mutayammim seeing water (invalidating tayammum) or a woman menstruating during the prayer. Unlike fard, where these would not require qada, in nafl they do.

Key Terms
الشفع (al-shaf'): A pair of rak'ats; in this context, the first two rak'ats form one pair (shaf' awwal) and the last two form a second pair.
التحريمة المبتدأة (al-tahrimah al-mubtada'ah): An initiating takbir that starts a new prayer; standing for the third rak'ah is likened to a new tahrimah.
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow; Abu Yusuf analogizes the commencement of nafl to a vow, making the full intended number binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the main reason for the ruling that only two rak'ats are made up when one sits after two and invalidates the last two?
A) Because the first pair has been completed by sitting, and standing for the third is like a new takbir.
B) Because the invalidation occurred before the second pair commenced.
C) Because Abu Yusuf's view is precautionary.
D) Because the prayer was nafl and qada is not required.

Key Takeaway
In nafl, sitting after two rak'ats completes the first pair, making the second pair independent; thus only the invalidated second pair requires qada.

Spoiling the Last Two Rak'ahs After Sitting in Nafl
Ruling on spoiling last two rak'ahs after sitting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating rak'ahs after spoiling the last two of a four-rak'ah nafl prayer when one has sat for tashahhud, and explain the dispute with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Sitting after the first two makes the second pair a separate prayer; only the spoiled pair needs repetition.

When performing a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, the first two rak'ahs constitute a complete pair (shaf'). The moment you sit for tashahhud, that pair is sealed. Standing for the third is like a new prayer, so if the last two are invalidated, only those two need to be made up. However, Abu Yusuf views the whole four as one unit requiring full repetition. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and condition
The act is a four-rak'ah nafl prayer where the person sits after the first two for the duration of tashahhud, then spoils the last two rak'ahs. Determine the ruling based on this condition.
The condition of sitting is critical; without it, the ruling changes.
2
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
The first pair is complete and valid. Standing for the third rak'ah is equivalent to a new initiating takbir (tahrima). Thus the second pair is a separate prayer; only its spoiling requires compensation.
This is the view of Abu Hanifa and the relied-upon position in the madhhab.
3
Compare Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf analogizes the commencement of the prayer to a vow (nazr), obligating completion of all four rak'ahs. Hence he requires repeating four rak'ahs.
His view is considered precautionary (ihtiyat).
4
Consider the scenario without sitting
If the person did not sit after the first two, there is consensus among the Hanafi imams that all four rak'ahs must be repeated.
This consensus reinforces the importance of the sitting condition.
5
Apply to practical examples
The dispute affects rulings on wife's option (khiyar) and pre-emption (shuf'ah) during prayer. According to al-Nihayah, completing four does not void the right; according to al-Jundi and al-Karkhi, saluting after two preserves it.
These examples illustrate the real-world consequences of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
فإن صلى أربع ركعات، وقَعَدَ في الأوليين مقدار التشهد، ثم أفسد الأخريين : قضى ركعتين.
وقوله : أفسدها سواء أفسدت بفعله أو بغير فعله، كالمتيمم يرى الماء وما أشبهه، وكالمرأة إذا حاضت في التطوع: يجب القضاء، بخلاف الفرض.
* قوله: (فإن صلى أربع ركعات، وقعد في الأوليين مقدار التشهد، ثم أفسد الأخريين: قضى ركعتين)؛ لأن الشفع الأول قد تم، والقيام إلى الثالثة بمنزلة تحريمة مبتدأة: فيكون ملزماً.
ثم
وهذا إذا أفسد الأخريين بعد الشروع فيهما، بأن قام إلى الثالثة، أفسدها، أما إذا أفسدها قبل القيام: لا يجب عليه قضاء الأُخريين؛ لأنه أفسد قبل الشروع في الشفع الثاني.
وعن أبي يوسف: يقضي؛ اعتباراً للشروع بالنذر.
وقيد بقوله : وقعد ؛ لأنه لو لم يقعد، وأفسد الأُخريين: لزمه قضاء أربع، إجماعاً.
* قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف: يقضي أربعاً)).
وهو احتياط؛ لأنها بمنزلة صلاة واحدة، حتى إن الزوج لو خير امرأته وهي في الشفع الأول، أو أخبرت بشفعة لها، فأتمت أربعاً: لا تبطل شفعتها، ولا خيارها. كذا في «النهاية».
(1) هذه المقاولة لم أجدها مثبتةً فيما لدي من نسخ القدوري.
وفى «الجندي»، و«الكرخي»: إن سلَّمت على ركعتين: فهي على خيارها، وإن أتمت الأربع بطل خيارها ؛ لأن ما زاد على ركعتين صلاةٌ أخرى.
وإذا كانت في أربع الظهر الأولى: لم يبطل خيارها بانتقالها إلى الشفع الثاني.
وإن صلى أربعاً، ولم يقرأ فيهن شيئاً : أعاد ركعتين عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف: أربعاً.
وهذه المسألة مبنية على أصلين :
أحدهما: أن فساد الشفع الأول بترك القراءة: لا يرفع التحريمة، ولا يمنع الدخول في الشفع الثاني عندهما.
وقال محمد: د : يرفع التحريمة، ويوجب فساد الشفع الثاني.
وأصل آخر : أن الشفع الأول إذا فسد بترك القراءة: فالشفع الثاني لا يلزمه بمجرد القيام حتى يأتي في الشفع الثاني بركعة كاملة بقراءة، عند أبي حنيفة.
وقال أبو يوسف: يلزمه بمجرد القيام.
وأجمعوا أن الشفع الأول إذا صح : يلزمه الشفع الثاني بمجرد القيام.
فإذا ثبت هذا: فيتفرع عليه ثمان مسائل:
Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers
If he prays four rak'ahs, and sits in the first two for the amount of tashahhud, then spoils the last two: he repeats two rak'ahs.
And his saying: 'spoils it' whether it is spoiled by his action or by other than his action, like the one who performs tayammum seeing water and the like, and like a woman who menstruates during a voluntary prayer: repeating is obligatory, unlike the obligatory prayer.
* His saying: (If he prays four rak'ahs, and sits in the first two for the amount of tashahhud, then spoils the last two: he repeats two rak'ahs); because the first pair has been completed, and standing for the third is like an initiating takbir: thus it becomes binding.
Then
This is if he spoils the last two after beginning them, by standing for the third, he spoils them; but if he spoils them before standing: repeating the last two is not obligatory upon him; because he spoiled before beginning the second pair.
And from Abu Yusuf: he repeats; considering the beginning as a vow.
And he restricted by his saying: 'and sits'; because if he did not sit, and spoiled the last two: he would be obligated to repeat four, by consensus.
* His saying: (And Abu Yusuf said: he repeats four).
And it is precautionary; because it is like one prayer, such that if the husband gave his wife a choice while she was in the first pair, or she was informed of a pre-emption right for her, and she completed four: her pre-emption right is not voided, nor her option. Thus in 'al-Nihayah'.
(1) I did not find this statement established in the copies of al-Quduri that I have.
And in 'al-Jundi' and 'al-Karkhi': If she saluted after two rak'ahs: she retains her option, and if she completed the four, her option is voided; because what exceeds two rak'ahs is another prayer.
And if she was in the first four of Zuhr: her option is not voided by her moving to the second pair.
And if he prays four, and does not recite anything in them: he repeats two rak'ahs according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and Abu Yusuf says: four.
And this issue is based on two principles:
One of them: That the corruption of the first pair by leaving recitation does not remove the initiating takbir, and does not prevent entering the second pair according to the two. And Muhammad said: it removes the initiating takbir, and causes the corruption of the second pair.
And another principle: That if the first pair becomes corrupt by leaving recitation, then the second pair is not binding upon him merely by standing until he performs one complete rak'ah with recitation in the second pair, according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf said: it is binding upon him merely by standing.
And they all agree that if the first pair is valid, the second pair is binding upon him merely by standing.

Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the Quduri matn addresses rulings for four-rak'ah supererogatory prayers (nafl). The author explains two distinct issues: (1) spoiling the last two rak'ahs after sitting for tashahhud, and (2) omitting Quran recitation entirely. Both involve intra-Hanafi disputes between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

For the first issue: If one prays four rak'ahs, sits after the first two for the duration of tashahhud, then invalidates the last two (e.g., by breaking wudu or speaking), he must repeat only two rak'ahs. This is because the first pair (shaf') is complete and valid; standing for the third rak'ah is akin to a new initiating takbir (tahrima), making the second pair a separate obligatory prayer. If he spoils the last two before standing (i.e., before beginning the second pair), no qada is needed. However, if he did not sit after the first two, he must repeat all four by consensus. Abu Yusuf holds that he must repeat four rak'ahs, considering the initial commencement (shuru') as analogous to a vow (nazr) that obligates completion. The commentary mentions that Abu Yusuf's view is precautionary (ihtiyat), treating the entire prayer as one unit. This leads to practical consequences, e.g., when a wife is given a choice during prayer or informed of a pre-emption right: if she completes four rak'ahs, her rights are not voided according to al-Nihayah, but according to al-Jundi and al-Karkhi, saluting after two preserves her rights while completing four voids them, because the additional two are a separate prayer.

For the second issue: If one prays four rak'ahs without reciting any Quran in any rak'ah, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), he repeats two rak'ahs; Abu Yusuf says four. This ruling is built on two principles. First, whether corruption of the first pair by omitting recitation removes the tahrima and prevents entering the second pair: according to Abu Hanifa and (likely) Abu Yusuf (as per 'عندهما', though problematic), it does not; but Muhammad holds that it does, causing the second pair to be invalid as well. Second, if the first pair is corrupt, whether the second pair becomes obligatory merely by standing up: Abu Hanifa says no, only after completing one full rak'ah with recitation; Abu Yusuf says it becomes binding immediately. There is consensus that if the first pair is valid, the second pair is binding upon standing. These principles yield eight derived rulings (not detailed in the text).

The chapter illustrates how Hanafi jurists derive rules from underlying principles (usul) and accommodate ikhtilaf within the school.

Key Terms
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; the first two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer are the first shaf', the last two the second shaf'.
تحريمة (tahrima): The initial takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer; removing it means the prayer becomes invalid.
نذر (nazr): A vow; commencing a nafl prayer is compared to a vow, making its completion obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person prays four rak'ahs of nafl, sits after the first two for tashahhud, and then spoils the last two, how many rak'ahs must he repeat?
A) Four rak'ahs
B) Two rak'ahs
C) One rak'ah
D) None

Key Takeaway
Sitting for tashahhud after the first two rak'ahs of a nafl prayer separates the prayer into two independent units; only the invalidated pair requires compensation.

Omitting Recitation in Nafl Prayer: Principles and Disputes
Ruling on omitting all recitation in nafl prayer and underlying principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two principles underlying the ruling on omitting all Quran recitation in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer and identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Omission of recitation corrupts the first pair, but whether it cancels the tahrima and binds the second pair is disputed.

If a person prays four rak'ahs of nafl without reciting any Quran at all, the prayer is invalid, but how much must be repeated? The answer depends on two key principles: whether the corruption of the first pair removes the tahrima (initiating takbir) and whether the second pair becomes obligatory merely by standing up. The Hanafi imams differ on these points, leading to different numbers of rak'ahs required for repetition.

Guided Path
1
State the case and the different rulings
The case: a four-rak'ah nafl prayer with zero Quran recitation. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say repeat two rak'ahs; Abu Yusuf says repeat four. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: the number of rak'ahs to repeat.
This is a purely intra-Hanafi dispute.
2
Analyze the first principle: effect on tahrima
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (in one view?), corruption of the first pair by omitting recitation does not remove the tahrima and does not prevent entering the second pair. Muhammad, however, holds that it does remove the tahrima and thereby corrupts the second pair. Understand each position and its implication.
Tahrima is the initiating takbir; its removal would invalidate the entire prayer from the start.
3
Analyze the second principle: binding nature of the second pair
If the first pair is corrupt, does standing for the third rak'ah automatically obligate the second pair? Abu Hanifa says no, unless one completes a full rak'ah with recitation in the second pair. Abu Yusuf says yes, standing alone obligates it. Note the consensus that if the first pair is valid, standing obligates the second pair.
This principle determines whether the second pair is considered a valid commencement.
4
Combine the principles to derive the rulings
For Abu Hanifa: first pair corrupt but tahrima remains, so he is still in prayer; second pair not binding merely by standing, so he only need to repeat the deficient first pair? Actually the ruling is to repeat two rak'ahs. For Muhammad: first pair corrupt removes tahrima, so the whole prayer is invalid? But he says repeat two as well? Wait, the text says 'أعاد ركعتين عندهما' (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad repeat two). So Muhammad agrees on the number despite his different principle. How? Perhaps his view that tahrima is removed means the second pair is not valid, so only the first pair is invalid? This requires careful reasoning: if tahrima is removed, the prayer is invalid from the start, so no obligation to complete? But the text says he repeats two, so he must consider that the first pair is corrupt but the tahrima removal does not nullify the entire prayer? Actually the text says Muhammad holds that corruption removes tahrima and causes corruption of second pair. But if tahrima is removed, the entire prayer is invalid, so one would need to repeat all four? But the text says he repeats two. There is a contradiction. Perhaps the text means that Muhammad agrees on the outcome (two rak'ahs) but for a different reason. However, the source says 'عندهما' meaning the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say repeat two, and Abu Yusuf says four. So we present that. The guided path should note the discrepancy in principles but convergence in ruling for Muhammad.
The two principles yield eight subsidiary issues not detailed here.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The matn states 'أعاد ركعتين عندهما' indicating that the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the primary one. Abu Yusuf's view is mentioned but not adopted.
Thus the relied-upon position is to repeat two rak'ahs.

Making Up Rak'ahs When Recitation Is Omitted in Nafl
Explains two principles and first four sub-issues on praying four rak'ahs without recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on how many rak'ahs to make up when recitation is omitted in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, and explain the reasoning behind each position using the two principles.

Core Idea
The number of rak'ahs to make up depends on whether the first pair's invalidity lifts the initial takbir and whether standing alone necessitates the second pair.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira addresses a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute about a person who prays four rak'ahs of voluntary prayer without any recitation—or with partial recitation. The disagreement revolves around two underlying principles: the effect of the first pair's invalidity on the initial takbir (tahrima), and whether mere standing (qiyam) after an invalid first pair makes the second pair obligatory. Understanding these principles is essential for deriving the correct ruling in various scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the schools' positions
Read the main ruling: if one prays four rak'ahs without recitation, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say make up two rak'ahs; Abu Yusuf alone says make up four. Note that the text later mentions agreement between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on two rak'ahs but via different reasoning.
There is a textual ambiguity: 'عندهما' might refer to both Sahibayn, but Abu Yusuf then gives a second opinion. We focus on the two positions: Sahibayn (two rak'ahs) and Abu Yusuf (four).
2
Analyze the first principle: effect of the first pair's invalidity on tahrima
According to the Sahibayn, the invalidity of the first pair due to omitting recitation does not lift the tahrima and does not prevent starting the second pair. Muhammad holds that it does lift the tahrima, making the second pair invalid.
This principle affects whether the second pair is even considered a valid continuation.
3
Analyze the second principle: when does the second pair become obligatory?
Abu Hanifa says the second pair is not necessitated by mere standing after an invalid first pair; a complete rak'ah with recitation is needed. Abu Yusuf says mere standing suffices. All agree that if the first pair is valid, standing immediately makes the second pair obligatory.
This principle determines whether the person was committed to the second pair.
4
Apply the principles to the first sub-case (no recitation at all)
Muhammad's reasoning: first pair invalid → tahrima lifted → no valid second pair → only the first pair needs compensation = two rak'ahs. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: first pair invalid but tahrima remains; second pair not necessitated because no rak'ah with recitation → only first pair counted = two rak'ahs. Abu Yusuf: first pair invalid, but standing necessitates second pair, so both pairs are counted, but both invalid due to no recitation → must make up four rak'ahs.
Thus Abu Hanifa and Muhammad agree on two rak'ahs, while Abu Yusuf holds four.
5
Examine the remaining sub-cases for consistency
Review the second and third sub-cases: recitation only in first two or only in last two → consensus on making up the missing pair. The fourth sub-case: recitation in one of each pair → Sahibayn say four, Muhammad says two. Trace how each principle leads to these results.
This step reinforces the logical derivation from the two principles.

Source Text

وإن صلى أربعاً، ولم يقرأ فيهن شيئاً : أعاد ركعتين عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف: أربعاً.

وقال محمد: يرفع التحريمة، ويوجب فساد الشفع الثاني.
وأصل آخر : أن الشفع الأول إذا فسد بترك القراءة: فالشفع الثاني لا يلزمه بمجرد القيام حتى يأتي في الشفع الثاني بركعة كاملة بقراءة، عند أبي حنيفة.

وأجمعوا أن الشفع الأول إذا صح : يلزمه الشفع الثاني بمجرد القيام.
فإذا ثبت هذا: فيتفرع عليه ثمان مسائل:
1- أحدها: إذا صلى أربعاً، ولم يقرأ فيهن شيئاً: فعليه قضاء ركعتين عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف: يقضي أربعاً.
فاتفق أبو حنيفة ومحمد من أصلين مختلفين.
أما عند محمد لما فسد الشفع الأول بترك القراءة: ارتفعت التحريمة، ولم يصح الشروع في الثاني، وعند أبي حنيفة: لم تفسد التحريمة، إلا أنه لما فسد الشفع الأول بترك القراءة: فالثاني لا يلزمه بمجرد القيام، ما لم يأت بركعة مع القراءة، ولم يوجد.
وعند أبي يوسف: يلزمه بمجرد القيام.
2- والثانية : إذا قرأ في الأوليين، لا غير فعليه قضاء الأُخريين، بالإجماع؛ لأن الشفع الأول قد تم، فلزمه الثاني بمجرد القيام، وأفسده بترك القراءة.
3- والثالثة : إذا قرأ في الأُخريين، لا غير: فعليه قضاء الأوليين، بالإجماع. وهل تكون الأخريان صلاة؟ عندهما: نعم، وعند محمد: لا، حتى لو اقتدى به إنسان في الشفع الثاني : لا يصح اقتداؤه، ولو قهقه : لا ينتقض وضوؤه.
4- والرابعة : إذا قرأ في إحدى الأوليين، وإحدى الأُخريين: فعليه قضاء أربع عندهما، وقال محمد: ركعتين.
Chapter of Voluntary Prayers. And in [the works of] al-Jundi and al-Karkhi: If she (the woman) greets after two rak'ahs, then her option (in marriage) remains; if she completes the four, her option is invalidated because what is added beyond two rak'ahs is another prayer. And if she is in the first four of Dhuhr, her option is not invalidated by her moving to the second pair (shaf'). And if one prayed four (rak'ahs), and did not recite in them anything, he repeats two rak'ahs according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Abu Yusuf said: four. And this issue is built upon two principles: One of them: That the invalidity of the first pair due to abandoning recitation does not lift the tahrima (initial takbir), nor prevent entering into the second pair according to the two. And Muhammad said: It does lift the tahrima, and causes the invalidity of the second pair. And another principle: That if the first pair becomes invalid due to abandoning recitation, the second pair is not necessitated by mere standing until he comes in the second pair with a complete rak'ah with recitation, according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf said: It is necessitated by mere standing. And they all agreed that if the first pair is valid, the second pair is necessitated by mere standing. So when this is established, eight issues branch from it: 1- The first: If one prayed four and did not recite in them anything, then upon him is to make up two rak'ahs according to the two, and Abu Yusuf said: he makes up four. So Abu Hanifa and Muhammad agreed from two different principles. As for according to Muhammad, when the first pair became invalid due to abandoning recitation, the tahrima was lifted, and the commencement of the second was not valid. And according to Abu Hanifa, the tahrima was not invalidated, except that when the first pair became invalid due to abandoning recitation, the second is not necessitated by mere standing until he comes with a rak'ah with recitation, and he did not. And according to Abu Yusuf, it is necessitated by mere standing. 2- The second: If he recited in the first two only, then upon him is to make up the last two, by consensus, because the first pair is completed, so the second is necessitated by mere standing, and he invalidated it by abandoning recitation. 3- The third: If he recited in the last two only, then upon him is to make up the first two, by consensus. And are the last two considered a prayer? According to the two: yes, and according to Muhammad: no, such that if someone followed him as imam in the second pair, his following is not valid, and if he laughed loudly, his ablution is not nullified. 4- The fourth: If he recited in one of the first two and one of the last two, then upon him is to make up four according to the two, and Muhammad said: two rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage from 'al-Jawhara al-Nayyira' deals with the intra-Hanafi disputes regarding the ruling of someone who prays four rak'ahs of a voluntary prayer (nafl) without any recitation (or partial recitation). The author first mentions a related ruling from al-Jundi and al-Karkhi about a woman's option (khiyar) in marriage when she prays two rak'ahs and then additional ones—this is likely a separate context referring to the prayer of a woman who has been given a marriage option. Then the main issue begins: if a person prays four rak'ahs without any recitation, what must he make up? Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two, known as Sahibayn) say he makes up two rak'ahs, while Abu Yusuf alone says four. This difference is built on two underlying principles: (1) The effect of the invalidity of the first pair (shaf') on the tahrima (initial takbir). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, invalidity of the first pair does not lift the tahrima nor prevent commencing the second pair; but Muhammad holds that it does lift the tahrima and invalidates the second pair. (2) The requirement for the second pair to be obligatory. Abu Hanifa says that if the first pair is invalid, the second pair is not necessitated by mere standing; one must actually perform a complete rak'ah with recitation for it to become due. Abu Yusuf says mere standing after the first pair (even if invalid) makes the second pair necessary. All agree that if the first pair is valid, standing automatically necessitates the second pair. From these principles, eight subsidiary rulings are derived, of which the first four are listed here. The first sub-case (no recitation at all) results in agreement between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on making up two rak'ahs, but from different reasoning. The second and third sub-cases (recitation only in first two or only in last two) are agreed upon: the missing pair must be made up. The fourth sub-case (one rak'ah recited from each pair) has a difference: the Sahibayn require four rak'ahs to be made up, while Muhammad requires only two. This shows how the principles yield different practical outcomes.

Key Terms
الشفع (ash-shaf‘): A pair of rak'ahs in prayer, typically referring to the first two or last two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer.
التحريمة (at-taḥrīmah): The initial takbir that commences the prayer and by which the worshipper enters into the state of ihram (sacred prohibition from worldly acts).
القيام (al-qiyām): Standing up after the first pair of rak'ahs intending to continue the prayer; it is a posture that may necessitate the second pair depending on validity of the first.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Abu Hanifa regarding whether the second pair becomes obligatory by mere standing after an invalid first pair?
A) It is obligatory by mere standing.
B) It is not obligatory until one performs a complete rak'ah with recitation.
C) It is obligatory only if the first pair was valid.
D) It becomes obligatory only after the second sujood.

Key Takeaway
The compensation for omitted recitation in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer is determined by the interplay of two principles: the effect of the first pair's invalidity on the tahrima and the role of standing in necessitating the second pair.
